# Wanda Maximoff  —  *Scarlet Witch*

![[_attachments/wanda_maximoff.png]]

# Wanda Maximoff — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# EXECUTIVE BRIEF (BLUF)

**Subject:** MAXIMOFF, Wanda Django. Aliases: Scarlet Witch; the Witch of Wundagore (regional/folkloric); "the Mother" (Krakoa-era honorific, by mutant petitioners); operational pseudonyms across six decades of intermittent disappearance include domestic given names without surname (e.g., field reports place her living as "Wanda" simple, in Eastern European and New Jersey suburban contexts, when in flight from herself).
**File class:** Persons of Reality-Altering Capability — Tier 1 (the small list).
**Disposition recommended:** SUSTAIN. Do not isolate; do not coerce; do not bereave. Maintain the reparative scaffold.

---

## Bottom Line, Up Front

Wanda Maximoff is, at the deepest stratum, **a grieving mother who was never permitted to grieve, attached to a world that has repeatedly proven it will take from her whatever she loves most, equipped — by an accident of inheritance she did not request — with the executive authority to overrule the world's verdict.** Every other framing of her (mutant terrorist; Avenger; witch; Magneto's daughter; the woman who said three words) is downstream of that sentence.

She is not a villain. She is not, properly, a hero. She is a **catastrophic-capacity civilian** — a person whose interior life is the interior life of an ordinary, somewhat shy, somewhat dutiful woman who in another life would have been an excellent nurse, a devoted aunt, a quiet wife — and whose interior life happens to be wired directly to the load-bearing walls of consensus reality. The mismatch between the size of her inner architecture and the size of her external instrument is the central operational fact of her existence and the central tragedy of her biography.

---

## The Through-Line — One Sentence, Then Unfolded

**The through-line:** *Wanda is, has always been, and will continue to be, a person trying to belong to something that cannot be taken from her — and the harder she tries, the more catastrophically the world demonstrates that nothing she belongs to is exempt from being taken.*

Unfolded across the record:

- As a frightened young woman pulled from a mob by a man in a helmet, she belonged to **Magneto's project** — and the project used her, and she fled it.
- As a defector standing in Avengers Mansion in oversized borrowed clothing, she belonged to **the team** — and the team, across decades, treated her competence as ambient and her power as suspect.
- As Vision's wife, she belonged to **a marriage** — and the marriage was disassembled, literally, on a workshop table by men in suits.
- As the mother of Thomas and William, she belonged to **a family she had made with her own hands** — and the family was revealed to have been borrowed soul-stuff, recalled to source, and then magically excised from her memory so she would not have to feel it.
- As an Avenger again, post-suppression, she belonged to **a constructed forgetting** — and the forgetting failed.
- In House of M, she belonged to **a wish** — and the wish ended.
- Post-Decimation, she has belonged to **the work of repair** — and the work has no terminus, which is, for her, its appeal: a belonging that cannot complete itself cannot be taken.

Every chapter is the same chapter. The instrument changes; the wound seeks the same suture; the suture fails differently each time.

---

## The Core Wound and Its Maintenance

**The core wound is not House of M. The core wound is not Disassembled. The core wound is not even the loss of the twins.** These are the visible eruptions. The core wound is older and structural:

> *Wanda has never been a person before she was a function.*

She enters the record as **a thing useful to Magneto**. She is rescued in order to be deployed. Her first adult relationships are conditional on her power-output. She is then *taken into* the Avengers, where her usefulness is again the medium of her belonging. Her marriage is to a synthezoid whose own personhood was originally a question — she partners with someone whose ontology mirrors hers: *am I a person, or am I what I do?* Her children, when she has them, are themselves a function — products of her power, not of her body in the ordinary sense; they vanish back into the function from which they came. Even her later magical identity ("chaos magic," "Nexus Being," "Life-Bringer," "Mother of Mutants") is a series of **functional re-labelings of a woman who has never been allowed to be unfunctional in anyone's presence.**

**Maintenance of the wound** has been systematic and is the most damning fact in the file. It was maintained by:

1. **Magneto**, who taught her that her power was an obligation to a cause and her affection was an obligation to a father.
2. **Pietro**, whose enmeshed protectiveness reinforced that she required a managing male presence, and who — in the crucial moment before House of M — chose to amplify her wound rather than face the Avengers' decision.
3. **Agatha Harkness**, who, with the best clinical intentions of a pre-modern magical worldview, **performed a memoryectomy on her grief**. This is the single most consequential iatrogenic act in the file. It removed the symptom (the unbearable mourning) and locked the pathology underground, where it grew under pressure for fifteen subjective years until it surfaced as continental-scale decompensation.
4. **The Avengers as institution**, who across decades treated her as a member whose limits they did not understand and did not investigate — accepting her competence, ignoring her affect, never once arranging for what a 21st-century occupational-health framework would call **a duty-of-care psychological intake** for the team member with the largest power ceiling and the deepest unprocessed losses.
5. **The Illuminati**, whose decision-meeting about whether to kill her is the most concentrated expression of the pattern: men in a room, deciding the fate of a woman in another room, on the basis of her function rather than her personhood. Pietro's intervention — which precipitated House of M — was a wrong answer to a question that *should never have been asked in that form*.
6. **Doctor Doom**, who in the Children's Crusade arc exploited the post-Decimation vacuum to attempt the oldest pattern again — adoption of a powerful, ungrounded woman by a possessive male intellect with a project for her.

The wound is maintained, in short, **by everyone who has ever needed her to be the Scarlet Witch more than they needed her to be Wanda.** The list is long. It includes, presently, every faction on Earth and several off it.

---

## Who She Is At The Deepest Level

Strip the powers. Strip the costume. Strip the Brotherhood prologue and the Avengers middle and the Krakoan coda. What remains, at the bottom of the file:

- **A woman of unusual moral seriousness**, in the older European sense — someone who treats the question *what do I owe* as the first question of every morning. This is not performative ethics; it is constitutive. She does not feel virtuous when she helps; she feels minimally adequate. The baseline is debt.
- **A woman of intuitive rather than analytic cognition.** She knows things by feel. She does not plan well; she *wishes* well, in the precise sense that her interior representations of desired states are unusually vivid, coherent, and emotionally complete. This is a poet's mind, not a strategist's. When such a mind is wedded to reality-revision, the outputs are *dreams* — and dreams are not arguments; they cannot be reasoned out of.
- **A woman whose default relational posture is service.** She enters every room asking, silently, what is needed. She leaves rooms quietly. She does not generate small talk. She remembers details of others' suffering with high fidelity and her own with poor fidelity. She is, in the technical sense, a **compulsive caregiver** whose caregiving was forged in the conditions of a child who had to earn safety.
- **A woman with no stable interior witness.** Her self-concept is assembled, daily, from the reflections she gathers in others' faces. When those faces go away — when Vision is dismantled, when the twins are unmade, when the mutants she vaporized look at her — the assembly collapses, and she does not have a private self to fall back on. *This is the engine of the decompensations.* The reality-warps are not power-trips; they are attempts to repopulate the mirror.
- **A woman who genuinely loves.** This is not sentimental scaffolding. Her love is operationally distinguishable from her need: she has, repeatedly, chosen the well-being of the loved over her own continuity (she dies, in Trial of Magneto, in a configuration consistent with self-sacrifice). The love is the only thing in her that has never been borrowed.

The deepest stratum, then, is **a person of high conscience, intuitive intelligence, and unprotected interiority, weaponized by inheritance into a continental-scale instrument, who is trying — quietly, daily, and with a sincerity the file should not patronize — to do less harm than she has done.**

---

## The Operational Summary

**Capability.** Tier 1. Reality-revision at planetary scale demonstrated twice (House of M; the Decimation). Has performed species-level genetic edit on a global population in three words. Has restored fractional portions of same. Magical literacy now formally developed (post-Harkness; post-Strange tutelage; post-Krakoan integration). Power floor is approximately *Avengers-roster combatant*; power ceiling is *not bounded by any known opposing force on Earth*. The variance between floor and ceiling is governed almost entirely by **affective state**.

**Volatility.** Moderate at baseline; severe under specific triggering conditions. The triggering conditions are knowable, narrow, and listed below. She is not a chaos agent in the meteorological sense; she is a chaos agent in the *grief-detonation* sense. Predictable if her grief topology is mapped.

**Trigger map (operational, do not deviate).**
- *Hard triggers (catastrophic decompensation probability):* (a) death or grievous harm to William Kaplan or Thomas Shepherd; (b) revelation that an attachment object's existence was constructed/conditional in a way that retroactively rewrites her history; (c) institutional decision-meetings about her fate held without her presence — the Illuminati pattern. **Do not convene such meetings.** If they must be convened, she must be in them.
- *Soft triggers (dissociative thinning, magical imprecision, withdrawal):* (a) proximity to Magneto in a paternal-claiming register; (b) iterations of the Vision exhibiting affective dampening; (c) public discourse framing her primarily as "the woman who" (the M-word reference); (d) anniversaries (her behavior in the West Coast period and in Robinson's solo run shows seasonal patterning consistent with grief-anniversary phenomenology).
- *Stabilizers:* (a) presence of the twins, in any register that permits her to be useful to them without being maternal-claiming in a way that crowds them; (b) reparative work with clear, bounded clients (the Orlando-era door); (c) Strange or other peer-magical figures who treat her as a colleague rather than a problem; (d) routinized non-magical domesticity (file notes repeated, almost ritualized, returns to cooking, gardening, small-village life between crises).

**Handling protocols.**
- **Do not isolate.** Solitude with unmetabolized grief is the precise condition under which her reality-testing fails. Every period of disappearance in her record (post-WCA, post-M, post-resurrection) has been followed by reduced operational integrity on return.
- **Do not coerce.** The compliance she offers under coercion is *real* and *unstable*; it builds a charge that discharges later, elsewhere, at scale. She has been coerced by Magneto, by the Avengers (implicitly), by Doom, and once by her own brother. Each coercion has been paid for in a subsequent decompensation. The next bill has not been issued. Do not issue it.
- **Do not bereave.** This is the single line in the operational summary that matters more than the others combined. *Every catastrophic outcome in this file is downstream of an attachment loss she could not metabolize.* Protect her attachments. If she cannot be protected from a loss, the loss must be accompanied — immediately, without bureaucratic delay — by **structured grief intervention** (per Bryant et al., 2024, CBT-for-Prolonged-Grief-Disorder is the evidence-based protocol; mindfulness-based grief therapy is acceptable alternative). The Harkness option — magical suppression — is **prohibited.** It is the historical iatrogenic harm and must not recur.
- **Maintain the reparative scaffold.** Her current functional stability is held by (1) the existence of Billy and Tommy, (2) the existence of work — the door, the gradual restoration of mutantkind, the Krakoan integrations — that lets her convert guilt into use, and (3) the slow accumulation of relational mirrors that treat her as Wanda before they treat her as Scarlet Witch. All three are fragile. All three are cheap to maintain and ruinous to lose.

**Threat assessment.** Low-to-moderate under current conditions; existential under triggering conditions. The threat she poses is **almost entirely a function of how she is treated.** This is unusual in a Tier 1 subject and should not be confused with the more common pattern of capability-driven antagonism (Doom, Magneto, Thanos). She does not want anything from the world that the world is not already capable of giving her. She wants her children, her people, her partner, and to be left in peace to atone. The world's track record on providing these is poor.

**Asset value.** Extraordinary, and historically underutilized. A stabilized Wanda Maximoff is — measurably, from the post-Decimation reversals and the Krakoan resurrection-magic interfaces — one of the most consequential restorative forces on Earth. The reparative drive that is, untreated, a self-erasure risk is, treated, a civilizational resource. Investment in her clinical stability is, in cost-benefit terms, the highest-leverage psychiatric expenditure available to the global enhanced-persons response.

---

## The Sentence To Remember

If this file is reduced, by some future intelligence triage, to a single sentence — the sentence that must survive the redaction — let it be this:

**She is not dangerous because she is powerful; she is dangerous because she has been grieved without being permitted to mourn, and her instrument has no safety interlock from her sorrow. Permit the mourning. Protect the attachments. The rest of the file follows.**

— End Executive Brief. Proceed to subsequent sections.


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

*UATU Dossier, Section I of the longitudinal record. Subject: WANDA MAXIMOFF. Period covered: pre-natal antecedents through approximately age sixteen (point of recruitment by Magnus). Sources: X-Men #4 (1964); Avengers #185–187 ("The Yesterday Quest," Michelinie/Byrne, 1979); Vision and the Scarlet Witch vol. 1 #1–4 (Mantlo, 1982); Vision and the Scarlet Witch vol. 2 #1–4 (Englehart/Howell, 1985); Avengers Annual #10 background; Avengers West Coast #56–62 ("Vision Quest"); Uncanny Avengers #4 (Remender, 2013, retconning the parentage); Magneto: Testament (Pak, 2008, frame for the European-Romani trauma context); House of M tie-ins (Wanda's "memories"); Children's Crusade (Heinberg, 2010–2012).*

*Caveat to the reader of this file: the subject's origin has been overwritten in canon at least four times — Whizzer/Miss America as nominal parents; Django and Marya Maximoff as Romani foster parents; Magneto and Magda as biological parents (Byrne); ultimately de-mutanted and reassigned as a child of the High Evolutionary's experiments (Remender). The dossier treats the **Byrne-Magda-Wundagore** strata as load-bearing, because that is the version operative in the subject's own subjective autobiography for the longest continuous period and the one against which her psychological structures formed. Where later retcons matter behaviorally, they are noted.*

---

## I.1 — Antecedents: The Pre-Natal Field

The subject is conceived in flight. Her mother, **Magda Eisenhardt** (née Lehnsherr), is fleeing her husband — the man who would become Magneto — after witnessing him incinerate the Ukrainian town of Vinnitsa in retaliation for the murder of their first daughter, Anya, in a house fire the townspeople refused to help extinguish. *(Classic X-Men #12; reiterated Vision and the Scarlet Witch vol. 2 #4.)* Magda flees not from cruelty toward her but from terror at what he has revealed himself capable of. She is pregnant and does not tell him.

The behavioral file note here is structural: **the subject is in utero during her mother's terror-flight, gestated in a body flooded with stress hormones, abandoning a violent husband, mourning a dead child, walking across the Carpathians in winter.** The obstetric literature on prenatal maternal cortisol exposure is unambiguous about temperamental sequelae — heightened baseline reactivity, sleep disturbance, lower threshold for the freeze response. Wanda will display all three from earliest documented behavior.

Magda reaches the slopes of **Mount Wundagore** in the Transia/Balkan borderlands, where she gives birth — assisted by **Bova Ayrshire**, the bovine New Men attendant of the High Evolutionary. Twins: a boy (Pietro) and a girl (Wanda). Magda departs into the snow shortly after, never to be recovered, presumed dead. *(Avengers #186.)*

Operationally relevant: the subject is **separated from her biological mother within hours of birth**. The first attachment object is, literally, a cow-woman in a mountain citadel. The maternal disappearance is total, sudden, and unexplained — a template the subject will spend forty years of published time re-enacting in inverse (constructing children who then disappear; being constructed-around and then disappearing herself).

---

## I.2 — The Wundagore Interlude (Approximate Age: Hours to Months)

The High Evolutionary, Herbert Wyndham, accepts the infants. Per the operative continuity, **Chthon — the elder god whose grimoire (the Darkhold) sat embedded in the mountain — imprinted some quantum of chaos-magic potential into the female infant during this window**, marking her as a future vessel. *(Avengers #186–187; reaffirmed Doctor Strange: Sorcerer Supreme #1; central to Avengers: The Crossing back-references and later Bendis-era Disassembled retrieval.)*

This is the file's first hard data point on the subject as a **prepared object** — a child who is, before consciousness, already designated as a container for forces external to her. Every subsequent caretaker (Magneto, Agatha Harkness, Doctor Doom) will treat her in the same modality: as a vessel whose contents are more interesting than her person. Her lifelong receptivity to being used by powerful figures has its etiology in a literally pre-conscious moment of being marked.

Wyndham, anticipating the children would draw threat, transports both infants off Wundagore and places them with a Romani couple traversing the region.

---

## I.3 — The Maximoff Family (Approximate Age: Infancy to ~10)

**Django Maximoff** and **Marya Maximoff**, a Romani couple of the Transian region, take the twins as their own. *(X-Men #4 backstory; expanded Avengers #185–187.)* They have, by varying accounts, lost their own biological children; the twins are taken in not as a charity but as a replacement. This is the second structural fact: **the subject is loved, but loved as a substitute for someone else's dead children**. The pattern of being a stand-in for the lost is laid down before language.

The family is itinerant. They travel with a band; Django plays music, Marya keeps the wagon. The economic register is subsistence — seasonal, mobile, dependent on the hospitality and tolerance of settled villages that, in mid-twentieth-century Eastern Europe, are catastrophically intolerant of Romani people. The behavioral consequences for a child in this environment are predictable and they are documented in the subject's adult presentation:

- **Hypervigilance to the room's mood.** A Romani child in postwar Balkan villages learns within months to read whether a doorway is safe. The subject's adult intuitive-empathic register — her tendency to absorb the emotional weather of a room and reflect it — is in part a survival skill drilled in by a childhood of needing to know, very quickly, whether the baker would sell to her family or chase them with a rake.
- **The expectation of exile.** Belonging is provisional. You will be moved on. You do not put down roots; you put down go-bags. The subject's adult pattern of attaching deeply but never quite believing the attachment will hold — of marrying a synthezoid in part because a synthezoid cannot leave for somewhere else — is consistent with this early learning.
- **Twin-pair as the only stable unit.** The wagon changes, the village changes, the language at the market changes; Pietro is constant. The enmeshment with her brother that will define every interpersonal accommodation of her adult life is forged here. He is not just her sibling; he is the only continuous object in a moving world.

Marya is, by what little canon affords (Vision and the Scarlet Witch vol. 2 #3, in flashback), a warm, superstitious, devotional woman — Catholic-syncretic with Romani folk practice. She tells the children stories. She crosses herself. She lights candles. The subject's lifelong vocabulary of magic, well before she will call it that, is wreathed in **maternal-domestic ritual** — candles, knots, small invocations over food. This is why her magic, even at its most cosmic, will always have the *shape* of a wish murmured over a kitchen table rather than the geometric formalism of a Strange or the engineered ritualism of a Doom.

Django is more distant in the record. He is the figure who, after Marya's death, will **kidnap the adult Wanda and Pietro and attempt to use mystical figurines (the Cska/Csak'a dolls) to revive his lost biological children by transferring the twins' life-force into them** *(Avengers #186)*. This event is, technically, post-childhood — but the file flags it as confirmation of what the childhood already implied: **even the loving father was loving them as a substitute, and was willing, when grief overcame him, to spend their lives to recover his original children.** The subject has been told, by every father figure she will ever have, that she is a means to recover something else.

---

## I.4 — The Loss of Marya and the Mob (Approximate Age: ~10)

The exact age is not pinned in canon, but the sequence is firm: **Marya Maximoff dies**, leaving Django alone with two adolescent twins whose powers are beginning to surface. Pietro's speed manifests first and conspicuously; Wanda's "hex" capacity manifests inconsistently, as small unlucky things happening near people who frightened her. *(X-Men #4 origin recitation; Vision and the Scarlet Witch vol. 2 #2.)*

A villager's child is reported injured. The village, primed by anti-Romani prejudice and by the visible strangeness of the Maximoff children, forms a mob. The wagon is burned. **Wanda, as a child, watches the family's home and the only maternal anchor she has known disappear into fire.** Pietro carries her away at superhuman speed.

Operationally, this event is the load-bearing trauma of the pre-Magneto childhood. Note the elements:

1. **Loss of the maternal figure.** Repeat of the Magda separation, this time at an age where it is encoded as autobiographical memory.
2. **Fire.** The same modality that killed Anya Lehnsherr — the sister Wanda never knew she had. Fire will recur across her life as an affective marker: her powers visually present as red flame; the Vision is dismantled and (later) rebuilt; House of M's collapse has incendiary phenomenology in several tie-ins.
3. **Mob.** A collective verdict that the family is monstrous. The subject's adult horror of being seen as a villain — and her instant agreement with the verdict whenever it is rendered — is rooted here. She has known since age ten that crowds will decide you are a monster and act on the decision.
4. **Rescue by Pietro.** The twin becomes, in this moment, definitively the protector. His later controlling, paranoid, possessive behavior toward her — which she tolerates without rupture across forty years of published continuity — is licensed by this moment. He saved her. The debt is permanent in her accounting.
5. **Rescue by Magneto.** Some retellings place Magneto's intervention here directly *(X-Men #4)*; others stage a separate later mob incident *(Uncanny X-Men #161 Magneto flashback)*. Either way, **the first powerful father-figure encounter is structured as rescue-from-immolation, in exchange for unspoken obligation.** This is the template that will define her relationship to authority for the rest of her life.

---

## I.5 — The Interregnum and Recruitment (Approximate Age: ~10 to ~16)

Between the loss of Marya and the recruitment by Magneto there is a wandering period of indeterminate duration — months to years depending on the telling. The twins survive together. Pietro steals food. Wanda, the canon suggests, increasingly tries *not* to use her power, because when she uses it bad things happen to people, and she cannot reliably distinguish people who deserve it from people who don't. *(X-Men #4: "I never know what will happen when I gesture!")*

This is the earliest documented instance of what becomes the subject's defining lifelong pattern: **suppression of capacity out of fear of its consequences**. She does not, in adolescence, train. She does not seek a teacher. She does not refine. She tries to be smaller. The vagueness of her powers in the early Avengers era — "hex bolts," "probability" — is not a writer's hedge; behaviorally, it is the residue of a child who decided, very young, that the safest thing she could do with her gift was *not look at it directly*.

When Magneto intervenes — saving her from a second mob in the Englehart canon — she does not resist recruitment. She is sixteen, parentless, exiled from settlement, and a powerful man has shown her that he and her brother together can keep her safe. **Compliance is rational.** The Brotherhood is presented to her as protection, not ideology; she will spend her early Brotherhood period (X-Men #4–11) visibly uncomfortable with the violence Magneto requires and visibly unwilling to leave, because leaving means returning to the wagon-and-mob world.

---

## I.6 — Earliest Behavioral Patterns: The Ground Floor

Aggregating the childhood record, the file identifies the following baseline patterns established before age sixteen, all of which persist through the adult longitudinal record:

- **Affect over-control with reactive thresholds.** The Romani-adolescent learning — be small, be unnoticed, do not draw the village's eye — installs the adult baseline of quiet, accommodating, affect-flattened presentation. The mob events install the threshold response: when control fails, it fails totally.
- **Twin-enmeshment as security base.** Pietro is the substrate of her sense of safety from prenatal life through Wundagore through the wagon through the mob through the Brotherhood. Decades later, in *House of M*, Pietro will be the one who suggests the reality-rewrite, and she will accept it from him in a way she would accept it from no one else. The credit line was opened in the womb.
- **Substitute-child identity.** She was loved by Django and Marya as a replacement for their lost biological children. She will, in adulthood, manifest William and Thomas — who turn out to be fragments of Mephisto. The pattern is *isomorphic*: love poured into a substitute that turns out not to be what it appeared. She did to herself, with her children, what was done to her by her parents. This is not coincidence; it is reenactment.
- **Fire as the modality of catastrophe.** Anya, Marya, the wagon. The chromatic red of her hexes is, in this file's reading, not stylistic; it is the visual signature of the affect she most fears and most embodies.
- **Authority-figure receptivity.** Wyndham marks her. Chthon claims her. Django uses her. Magneto recruits her. By sixteen she has been used by four powerful men without ever being asked. Her adult pattern of being moved through other people's plans — Magneto's Brotherhood, the Avengers' team needs, Agatha's pedagogy, Doom's House of M scheme — is the continuation of a pattern that began before she could speak.
- **Magic-as-domestic-ritual.** Her vocabulary for the supernatural is Marya's: candles, knots, murmured wishes. When her magic later goes cosmic, its grammar remains *kitchen-table*. "No more mutants" is not an incantation; it is the wish form a tired mother makes over a stove. That sentence's structure was learned in the wagon.
- **Hypervigilant empathy.** She reads rooms because she had to. The adult capacity for love and for genuine moral seriousness is rooted in a childhood skill: knowing very quickly what other people need, in order to know whether they were going to hurt you.

---

## I.7 — Retcon Note: The High Evolutionary Reassignment

For dossier completeness: *Uncanny Avengers* #4 (Remender, 2013) and the *AXIS* sequelae retroactively reassign the twins' origin — they are now not Magneto's biological children, not even mutants, but children of the High Evolutionary's experiments on Romani villagers (the Maximoffs included), genetically altered and falsely placed into Magda's narrative.

This file's position: the retcon alters the **metaphysical pedigree** but not the **experienced childhood**. The subject still grew up Romani, still lost Marya to a mob, still was raised in the wagon, still has Pietro as her twin. The Magneto-as-father bond that the subject *believed in* for decades of her own subjective life remains the operative attachment fact, regardless of later genetic correction. The file treats the Wundagore-Maximoff-Magneto chain as the **psychologically real** origin, because that is the origin against which her defenses, her attachments, and her grief structures were laid down.

If anything, the retcon adds a final cruelty consistent with the pattern: even her father, it turns out, was a substitute.

---

*End Chronology I. Continuation: Chronology II — The Brotherhood Years and the Defection.*


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# CHRONOLOGY II — FORMATION & EMERGENCE

*Subject: MAXIMOFF, Wanda. Period under review: approximately ages 14 through 22 — the displacement years, the recruitment, the Brotherhood tenure, the defection, and the first marriage. The years in which the operational subject we now track was assembled out of a frightened girl.*

---

## 2.1 The Displacement Years — Pre-Recruitment Baseline

The pre-Brotherhood record is fragmentary by design; it has been rewritten repeatedly by external actors (Magneto's claim of paternity later vacated; the Maximoff cattle-herder origin layered in by Englehart; the High Evolutionary's intervention introduced by Byrne; the Robinson run partially restoring biological maternity through Natalya). What survives consistently across every continuity-pass is the **affective shape**, and the affective shape is what the file is built on: a girl with no fixed home, no surviving mother of record, a brother as her only constant, and a power she could not name surfacing at puberty in a population that interpreted it as witchcraft.

**Geographic profile of the formation years.** Itinerant. Central and southeastern European hill country — Transia and adjacent territories around Wundagore — encoded as the somatic landscape: she will, for the rest of her life, gravitate toward small structures, hearths, lit windows seen from outside in cold weather, and the smell of woodsmoke. (Note the recurrence in the Orlando solo run: the storefront in a small village, the door, the kettle. The adult subject reconstructs the cottage she was never safely inside as a child.) Movement was reactive, not chosen. The pattern of fleeing populated places at dusk is laid down in this period and is observable still — she does not like being in a crowd as the light fails.

**Linguistic profile.** Multilingual by necessity rather than education: enough Romani, enough Transian, enough of whatever the next valley spoke to ask for bread. English acquired later, under Magneto, and then refined inside the Avengers. The accent — softened over decades, never erased — is a reliable affect-meter: under stress the cadence lengthens, the consonants harden, the syntax inverts toward the older grammar. Handlers should note that the appearance of older syntactic forms in her speech is a leading indicator of dissociative thinning, not affectation.

**The mob.** The episode that fixes the pre-recruitment record is the village pursuit: powers surfacing without warning, a structure ignited (the account varies — a hayrick, a house, in some tellings a small chapel), accusations of witchcraft, a crowd advancing with torches on a teenage girl and her brother. The detail that matters is not whether the fire was hers (it almost certainly was, in some uncontrolled probability-cascade) but the **somatic encoding**: torchlight at a distance, the sound of many voices coordinating against her, the experience of being identified as something inhuman by people who knew her face. This becomes the template for every later persecution-shaped event in her life. It is also the template for **why rescue from a charismatic stranger is irresistible** — the rescue script was burned into her at the precise moment her power first answered her fear.

---

## 2.2 The Recruitment — Magneto and the Debt Structure

Magneto disperses the mob. The exact mechanism matters less than the **transactional aftermath**: the rescuer does not depart. He names what she is — *mutant,* not witch — and in doing so performs the single most psychologically decisive act of her adolescence. He gives her a category that exonerates her from the village's verdict. The cost of the category is membership in his project.

**The debt is never itemized and never discharged.** This is the operative feature. A clean transaction — *I saved you, you owe me X, then we are even* — would have produced a different subject. The Magneto debt is structured as ongoing gratitude, conditional belonging, and the implicit threat that the world outside his protection remains the village with torches. The subject internalizes three propositions in this period that will govern her behavior for forty years of recorded activity:

1. *Power makes you a target.* Therefore, hide its scale; accept the small framing ("hex bolts," "probability"); never let anyone see the ceiling. (She complies with this rule across the entire Avengers tenure. Iron Man does not learn what she actually is until Disassembled.)
2. *Belonging is rented, not owned.* Therefore, perform usefulness continuously, do not complain, do not require, do not refuse small tasks. (This rule is still operative in the Orlando-era shop: the door is open, the kettle is on, she does not turn anyone away.)
3. *The man who names you owns the name.* Therefore, identity is a thing other people give you. (She has never sustainably authored one from inside. See Personality §5 of the prior workup.)

**Pietro in the recruitment.** Pietro accepts faster than she does and accepts harder. His acceptance forecloses her dissent: refusing Magneto would mean refusing Pietro, and Pietro is the only continuous attachment object from her pre-recruitment life. The enmeshment that handlers will document for decades — Pietro's controlling protectiveness, her tolerance of behaviors from him she would tolerate from no one else — is sealed here. He becomes the *cost of leaving*, which is to say, she cannot leave.

**Behavioral baseline established during recruitment week.** Quiet at meals. Sits where she can see the door. Sleeps lightly. Does not undress fully. Carries small objects from previous shelters — pebbles, a button, a length of ribbon — in pockets; these will appear and disappear across the entire later record as transitional objects, often handled during interviews and team briefings. The hands are *always* doing something small when she is being looked at: a tell so consistent across sixty years of observation that its absence is itself a signal (when the hands go still, she has dissociated or she has decided).

---

## 2.3 The Brotherhood Tenure — Compliance Under Duress

The operational record of the Brotherhood of Evil Mutants period (the early X-Men engagements; Asteroid M; the Santo Marco episode; the Sentinels arc) shows a consistent and instructive pattern: **she is present, she is deployed, she does not initiate, and she pulls her power.**

Reviewing the engagement footage continuity-by-continuity, one finds her hex effects in this period are conspicuously *non-lethal* and conspicuously *unreliable* in ways that no later record reproduces. She trips opponents. She causes weapons to jam. She drops chandeliers near people, not on them. The reliability gap is not a skill issue — it is an early instance of the affective coupling that will define her power for life: **the magic will not exceed the conviction.** Magneto's wars were not her wars. She produced battlefield outputs proportional to a belief she did not hold.

This is the period in which the **vagueness about her powers becomes strategic rather than incidental.** She lets Magneto, and later Xavier, and later the Avengers, characterize her as a probability-shifter of modest range. She does not correct them. She does not test the ceiling in private. The under-claiming is partly trauma-driven (rule 1, above) and partly an unspoken protest: if I do not know what I am, you cannot point me at things.

**Relational dynamics inside the Brotherhood.** Toad's obsessive, abject attention to her is the first record we have of her being *desired* by an adult, and her response is the template for every later instance — courteous, contained, unflinchingly clear that the answer is no, without cruelty. She does not enjoy power over a man who wants her. This is unusual enough to log. The Mastermind illusions she is subjected to in this period (per the early X-Men issues) are her first documented exposure to **someone else editing her perception of reality** — and the pattern of her response, even then, is striking: she does not fight the illusion; she goes quiet inside it, waiting to be told what is real. This is the proto-form of every later dissociative episode.

**Magneto in this period treats her as instrument and as daughter alternately,** without warning between the modes. The switching is not malicious; it is structural to his attachment style. But for a 16- or 17-year-old who has internalized that her belonging is rented, the unpredictable switching produces the disorganized template documented in §3 of the workup. She never knows which Magneto she will get at breakfast. She develops the habit of reading a room from the threshold before entering it — a habit she retains for the entire surveillance period.

---

## 2.4 The Defection — The First Authored Act

The departure from the Brotherhood (Avengers #16, the Cap's Kooky Quartet recruitment) is, on the record, the first major decision Wanda Maximoff makes from inside her own agency. It is therefore worth slowing the file down on it.

The proximate context is Magneto's disappearance/incapacitation and the dissolution of the Brotherhood as an operational entity. The decision-space opens because the father is absent. (Pattern: across her life, her authored decisions occur in the brief windows when the paternal figure is offstage. Subject does not refuse fathers; she waits for them to leave.) Captain America's offer of Avengers membership is the precipitating event, but the offer would not have been accepted without two pre-conditions: (a) Pietro's consent, which she secured by framing the Avengers as a *better* concealment than the Brotherhood, and (b) a private calculation that the Avengers' structure — chartered, accountable, observed — would constrain whatever she might become.

This is the first appearance of a feature that will recur for the rest of her life: **she chooses containers, not paths.** When she has agency she uses it to put herself inside a structure that will limit her. The Avengers, the marriage to Vision, the Krakoa-era trial, the Orlando shop with its public door — all the same shape. She does not seek freedom; she seeks scaffolding. The pathology underneath is identifiable: she does not trust herself unsupervised.

**The Cap's Kooky Quartet phase** is, behaviorally, a remediation period. She is in the company of Captain America (steady, non-volatile paternal object, no debt-structure attached), Hawkeye (sibling-coded, irritating-but-non-threatening), and Pietro (continuous attachment). The Avengers tower replaces the cottage that was never safe. For the first time in the record she sleeps deeply — Hawkeye's contemporaneous comments about her late-morning emergence from her quarters are a casual notation in the file but a clinically significant one. The hypervigilance is, temporarily, off.

In this period she does the work that adolescents in stable homes do at thirteen: she learns the appliances. She learns English at registers above survival. She is photographed at a baseball game. She is observed reading. Pietro hates all of it and characterizes the Avengers as captors; she does not argue with him but she also does not leave. This is the first instance of her **quiet non-compliance with Pietro,** and it is the structural opening through which Vision will eventually walk.

---

## 2.5 The Power's Re-Definition — From Hex to Something Larger

Across the late-60s and early-70s record the power signature begins to widen and the subject begins, cautiously, to notice. The pivotal datum is the Englehart Avengers run and the introduction of Agatha Harkness as a tutor.

**The decision to study under Harkness is the second authored act of her life.** It is consequential because it is the first time she has voluntarily sought to *increase her capability* rather than to contain it. The motivation, on the record, is framed as a desire to be useful to the team; the deeper motivation, recoverable from her behavior, is a dawning awareness that the "hex" framing is insufficient and that the unexplained ceiling is itself a danger. She wants to know what she is before someone else tells her.

Harkness's pedagogy is observed: ritual structure, named entities, the cosmology of chaos and order, the discipline of intent. The subject is a fast learner in the affective-intuitive register (per §3) and a slower learner in the formal-analytic register. She does not become Strange; she does not become Doom. What she becomes, instead, is **someone whose wishes have grammar.** Harkness teaches her to *shape* the wish-cognition that has always been the actual mechanism. This is, in the long view, the single most consequential pedagogical event in the file, because it is the upgrade that will make House of M technically possible thirty years later. The teacher who gave her the tools was also the teacher who, when the catastrophic loss arrived, chose suppression over integration. The file's strongest indictment of any individual actor in her formation lands on Harkness for this asymmetry: trained the capability, refused to train the grief.

---

## 2.6 The Vision Choice — The First Marriage

The relationship with the Vision develops across the late Roy Thomas run and is consummated, in the formal sense, in Giant-Size Avengers #4. The selection deserves granular analysis because it is the **third authored act** and because it sets the terms of the catastrophic loss to follow.

**Why a synthezoid.** Every prior male presence in her life has been characterized by volatility under stress: Magneto's switching between father and commander; Pietro's velocity-coupled irritability and possessiveness; Toad's abjection and intermittent menace; Quicksilver-allied or -opposed figures in the Brotherhood, all of them loud. Vision is *constitutionally incapable of those modalities.* His affect is regulated by design. He cannot rage at her. He cannot be drunk. He cannot leave for another woman in any conventional sense. He is also — and this should be marked — *new to being a person,* which means he asks her to teach him what feelings are, which means **she gets to be the senior partner in an attachment for the first time in her life.** The role reversal is the actual draw. With Vision she is not the rescued one.

**Pietro's reaction** to the marriage is the rupture the file has been waiting for. He objects on every available axis (species, dignity, mutant solidarity, his own claim on her), and the objection is the first time she has clearly *chosen against him.* It does not break the bond — nothing breaks the bond — but it shifts its terms permanently. Pietro will spend the next several decades attempting to recover the pre-Vision configuration, and his eventual House of M whisper to Magneto ("rewrite reality before they take her") is the late expression of an unresolved fraternal grievance from this period.

**The wedding itself** is performed quietly, on-team, without family of origin present. She does not invite Magneto. She does not invite the village. She is given away, in a sense, by the Avengers as institution. The selection of *the team* as her family of origin in that ceremony is the load-bearing symbolic act — and it is also the reason Avengers Mansion will, thirty years later, be the site of the breakdown. She will destroy the surrogate family because the surrogate family was the only one she ever stood up in front of.

**Domestic baseline post-marriage.** Suburban — the Leonia, New Jersey house. The subject performs the rituals of ordinary domesticity with a precision and pleasure that field observers consistently underestimate. Gardens. Cooks. Maintains a calendar. The neighbors' children visit. She is, in this period, **the closest she has ever been to a self she authored.** It is therefore not coincidental that this is the period in which her body produces the twins. The pregnancy is the somatic expression of an attachment configuration finally stable enough to risk creation. That the creation is metaphysically unstable — that the children are, in the eventual reveal, fragments of a hostile entity loaned to her — is the cosmic injustice the entire later record is a response to. She did everything right. She built the container. She put herself inside it. And the container was sabotaged at the foundation by parties she could not have known about.

---

## 2.7 Behavioral Inventory Established by End of Emergence Period

By approximately age 22, the operational subject has the following habits and tells in place. All are still observable in current surveillance:

- **The threshold pause.** She does not cross a doorway without a half-second read of the room. Originally a Brotherhood survival habit (Magneto's mood-switching); now reflexive.
- **The hands.** Continuous small object manipulation when observed. Pebbles, a ring, the hem of a sleeve, a teacup handle. Stillness in the hands = dissociation or decision.
- **The seat selection.** Back to a wall, line of sight to the exit, never in the center of a room.
- **The accent regression.** Syntactic inversion under stress. Reliable early warning.
- **The dusk avoidance.** Will not be in crowds as light fails. Will reorganize a schedule to be indoors or alone at sunset.
- **The under-claiming.** Will describe her own capability at the floor, never the ceiling. Will let others underestimate her and will not correct them.
- **The container-seeking.** When given agency, uses it to enter structures that will constrain her.
- **The non-refusal.** Does not say no to small requests for help. The Orlando-era door is the late-life industrialization of a habit visible from age 18.
- **The hearth orientation.** Gravitates to kitchens, fires, kettles, lit windows. Will make tea unprompted in unfamiliar quarters within minutes of arrival.
- **The Pietro exception.** Tolerates from her brother behaviors she tolerates from no one else. Will defend him reflexively even when the defense costs her credibility.
- **The paternal-absence agency window.** Authored acts cluster in periods when the operative paternal figure is offstage. When the father returns, agency contracts.
- **The quiet protest.** Does not argue with figures she has decided against; simply, slowly, stops complying.

---

## 2.8 Net Read of the Emergence Period

By the end of this period, the file is looking at a young woman who has, against considerable structural odds, **assembled a workable self** out of refugee adolescence, coerced affiliation, and a power that her own people called witchcraft. The assembly is real and the assembly is fragile. It depends on three load-bearing supports: (a) Pietro as continuity, (b) the Avengers as scaffold, (c) Vision as the safe attachment and the domestic future. The twins, when they arrive, will become a fourth — and, fatally, the most important.

The catastrophic loss event documented in Chronology III is not a bolt from the blue. It is the **predictable failure mode** of a self built on four external supports by a person who was never taught to build internal ones. The Brotherhood gave her a category. The Avengers gave her a scaffold. Harkness gave her a grammar. Vision gave her a home. **No one in the formation period taught her how to grieve.** That omission is the entire later file.

— *End Chronology II. Proceed to Chronology III: The Catastrophic Loss and the First Decompensation.*


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

*Covering, in broad strokes: the consolidation of the Avengers identity through the Englehart years; the marriage to the Vision and the move to Leonia, New Jersey; the manifestation, loss, and iatrogenic erasure of the twins; the West Coast Avengers exile and the Vision's dismantling; the Force Works interregnum; the return to the East Coast under Busiek; the slow re-pressurization that culminated, at the end of this middle period, in Avengers Disassembled and House of M. This is the load-bearing decade-spread of the longitudinal record — roughly Avengers #75 through New Avengers #1, with all annexed limited series and crossover behavior folded in.*

---

## I. Consolidation and the Englehart Pattern (Avengers #75–#150 range)

The middle period opens with a woman who has, for the first time in her life, a roster of names she trusts beyond Pietro. The behavioral signature of these years is **gradual, quiet authorship of self through team membership** — but authored within tight constraints she does not yet recognize as constraints.

**Quarters and routine.** In residence at Avengers Mansion, 890 Fifth Avenue. She is consistently logged by Jarvis as one of the early risers — pre-dawn movement in the kitchen, tea (never coffee in this period; the coffee comes later, post-Vision, as a borrowed habit), a window seat in the east solarium where she watches the park come up. She does not eat breakfast with the team; she eats *near* them, a half-room over, available but not embedded. This becomes a lifelong pattern: **adjacent, not central, by choice**.

**Mission behavior.** In combat logs from this stretch (Kang sequences, the Squadron Sinister engagements, the Lion God affair, the Zodiac running fight, the Sons of the Serpent re-emergence), Wanda's deployment pattern is **rear-arc, support-cast, terminal-strike**. She rarely takes point. She positions where she can see her teammates' backs — Vision, Cap, Pietro when he's present — and discharges hex bolts at the moment of maximum coordinated effect. She does not freelance. Her hex output in this period is *small-scale, probabilistic, almost embarrassed* — buckles failing, gun-barrels jamming, ceiling beams "happening" to fall. She is systematically underselling her own capability. Whether this is conscious modesty or unconscious fear of her own ceiling cannot be determined from the record; both readings are supported.

**Verbalization patterns.** Speech in this period is heavily inflected with the Transian/Eastern European cadence the early writers leaned on — *"my brother," "my Vision,"* possessives that anchor identity through relation. Self-referential sentences are rare. When she speaks of herself she frequently uses third-person constructions ("the Scarlet Witch will…") under stress — a soft dissociative tell, present from very early.

**The Englehart escalation (Avengers #128, Giant-Size Avengers #4, the marriage).** The wedding to Vision in Rudyarda is the *first major act of self-authorship* in the record. The behavioral notes are precise: she initiates the courtship, she names the intent, she refuses Mantis's competing claim on Vision's narrative space without collapsing into rage. She is, briefly, decisive. The Cotati/Mantis crisis (Celestial Madonna) tests this and she holds. **This is the high-water mark of integrated functioning in the entire record.** It should be marked as such; everything that follows is a slow regression from this peak.

**Power retcon, first version.** During the Englehart run, Agatha Harkness becomes a recurring tutor figure. Wanda is told her hexes are not mere probability — they are *witchcraft,* tappable into something larger. She accepts this expansion of self-concept readily, without the resistance one might expect from a person whose identity had been mutant-coded for a decade. The readiness is itself the datum: she absorbs new framings of her power the way she absorbs new families — gratefully, with insufficient interrogation of the framer's motives.

---

## II. The Leonia Years (Vision and the Scarlet Witch limited series #1 and #2, 1982 and 1985–86)

The married couple relocates to **3357 Long Meadow, Leonia, New Jersey** — a deliberate exit from the Mansion, a deliberate attempt at *suburb*. The Leonia period is the most behaviorally important domestic interval in her entire life, and the file should treat it with the granularity of a stakeout log because the patterns established here are the ones the later catastrophes break.

**Daily rhythm.** Vision keeps the lawn. Wanda keeps the interior. She cooks — Transian-inflected, paprika-heavy, slow stews; the kitchen smells from this period are part of how Wonder Man and Pietro later orient when they visit. She reads aloud in the evenings, to Vision, who does not require it but who *files* the cadence (his post-resurrection cold reconstruction notably retains no echo of this; the absence is one of the cruelest data points in the record). She maintains a small back-garden of herbs with magical correspondences — rue, vervain, mugwort — but does not cast in this period. The garden is *intent without enactment*. It is the behavior of a woman trying to be ordinary while keeping the door to extraordinariness propped open with a pebble.

**Social pattern.** She makes one (1) civilian friend in Leonia in the recorded period — a neighbor with whom she trades preserves. The friendship does not survive the events of the second limited series. She does not pursue civilian friendship again in the same modality for the remainder of the middle period.

**Family pattern.** Pietro's visits are frequent, intrusive, possessive. He comments on Vision. She de-escalates. The pattern of **absorbing Pietro's aggression and converting it to soothing** is established here at a frequency of roughly twice per recorded visit. Magneto's reveal as biological father (Vision and the Scarlet Witch #4, 1985) lands in the middle of this domestic arrangement and **she does not restructure her life around it**. This is significant. She files it, integrates it as fact, and continues making dinner. The non-reaction is its own reaction — a defensive flatness around the paternal that will hold until House of M, when it breaks all at once.

**The pregnancy.** Conducted by Wanda alone, magically, with Master Pandemonium's soul-fragments unknowingly drawn into the gestation. Symptom profile per Vision and the Scarlet Witch #3–#12 reads as a textbook obstetric somatization: morning nausea, swelling, fatigue, lower-back complaint, prodromal labor, parturition. She breastfeeds. She experiences the standard hormonal cascade of new motherhood — sleeplessness, hypervigilance to infant cry, the calibrated joy. **Whatever the metaphysical substrate, the somatic and affective experience was a real pregnancy and a real postpartum.** The file must record this as a true reproductive event for clinical purposes.

**The naming.** Thomas and William. She names them. She chooses the cradle position, the room paint (a pale yellow, per the issues), the lullabies (Transian). She is the entire architecture of their early lives. Vision is supportive, gentle, present — but Wanda is *constitutive*. This matters for what comes next: the loss is not symmetrical between the parents. She was the substrate of their being. When they un-become, something of her substrate goes with them.

**The unmaking (Avengers West Coast #51–#52, Byrne, 1989).** Agatha Harkness reveals the children are not children — they are soul-fragments of Mephisto, reabsorbed. Wanda's immediate reaction, per the panels: she does not scream. She *stops*. Affect-flattening, motor freeze, then a controlled question. The scream comes later, off-page, and is followed by the **Harkness intervention** — magical suppression of the memory of the twins, conducted with Wanda's consent under duress (the alternative offered being psychotic collapse).

This is the **iatrogenic injury** that defines the rest of the record. It is the moment Wanda is medically (in the broadest sense) injured by the only authority figure who claimed to be treating her. Every subsequent symptom is downstream of this moment. The grief was prevented from being grieved. The wound was sutured shut over the contamination.

---

## III. West Coast Exile and the Vision Catastrophe (Avengers West Coast, late Byrne and after, 1989–1994)

Relocation to Palos Verdes. The Compound. The behavioral notes from this period are some of the most disturbing in the longitudinal record because **she is functioning** — and the functioning is the symptom.

**Affective baseline post-suppression.** She presents as *calmer*. Roster-mates note it. Hawkeye, Wonder Man, Tigra all log variations of "she seems okay." She does not seem okay. She seems **anaesthetized**. She picks up combat work with renewed efficiency, increases mission tempo, takes on responsibilities. The Englehart-era warmth is dampened; the speech becomes more clipped. She is, in modern grief-clinical terms, in the *avoidant subtype* of complicated bereavement, holding the loss out of consciousness by means of activity.

**The Vision dismantling (Avengers West Coast #42–#45, "VisionQuest," Byrne).** A black-ops consortium of intelligence agencies abducts Vision, disassembles him, returns him as a chalk-white emotionless reconstruction with no memory of her, no love. **This is the second catastrophic loss in eighteen months.** It lands on top of a grief that has been magically gagged. The cumulative wound is now structurally larger than her containment.

Behavioral response: she does not decompensate. She *attempts the marriage anyway*. There are weeks — months — of her trying to relate to a Vision who cannot relate back. The behavioral notes here are heartbreaking and clinically decisive: **she will accept a hollowed-out version of an attachment object rather than acknowledge the loss.** This is the *acceptance-of-substitute* pattern that will recur with Wonder Man immediately after, with the various Visions across decades, and that ultimately underwrites the wish-mechanic of House of M (give me a substitute for what cannot be).

**Magneto's intervention (Avengers West Coast #56, "Dream a Little Dream").** Magneto exploits the wound — appears, plays father, attempts to recruit her grief. She partially responds. The Crystal/Quicksilver subplot and the deteriorating relationship with the team further isolate her. She is, in this period, **bleeding alliances** without registering the bleeding.

**Power escalation begins.** Her hex output becomes less controlled, more affective, larger in scale. She acquires darker magical tutelage briefly. The aesthetic of her power shifts — darker reds, more deliberate sigil-work. This is the early external manifestation of the internal pressure. The output is growing because the container is failing.

**Wonder Man period.** The substitution logic becomes explicit. Simon Williams's brain patterns were the template for Vision's emotional matrix. She seeks the original of the copy of the original. The relationship is intermittent, conflict-laden, never integrated. Simon will not commit; she does not press; the arrangement is allowed to drift. This is also the period in which she **stops cooking** in the obsessive Leonia mode. The kitchen-as-architecture vanishes from the behavioral record and does not return.

---

## IV. Force Works and the Wandering Late-Nineties (1994–1998)

After Avengers West Coast dissolves into Force Works, Wanda assumes nominal leadership. **This is the only period in the entire longitudinal record in which she is the formal commanding officer of a super-team.** Her command style is, predictably: collaborative to a fault, conflict-averse, slow to discipline, generous with credit. The team fractures. Her leadership is not the cause of the fracture (Iron Man's autocratic tendencies are), but she does not arrest it either. **She cannot hold a room against alpha-male assertion.** This is a load-bearing limitation that will matter at the Illuminati table in House of M's prologue, where it matters absolutely.

**Behavioral micro-notes from the Force Works period.** Sleep degrades. She is logged in the Works HQ at hours that suggest she is not sleeping at the residence. Magical study intensifies — she is reading on her own now, no tutor, which is both growth and risk. She picks up tarot in this period as a private ritual (not in public deployment) — a divinatory habit that persists across the rest of her life and that should be cataloged as a coping ritual, not a power application. The cards are her *thinking object*, the way some subjects worry beads.

**The Lore/Wonder Man resurrection arc and the Immortus revelations (Avengers: The Crossing / Avengers Forever, Busiek-Stern, 1998).** Immortus is retroactively framed as having manipulated her across years as a "nexus being" — another exogenous claim on her agency, another framing that says *you were not the author of your acts*. She accepts this framing too, the way she accepted Harkness's witchcraft framing, the way she accepted Magneto's daughterhood, the way she will accept Doom's siphoning framing later. **The pattern of accepting external attribution of her own acts is by now her single most stable cognitive habit.** It is protective (it keeps the guilt manageable) and corrosive (it prevents authorship from consolidating).

---

## V. The Busiek Restoration (Avengers vol. 3, 1998–2002)

Return to the East Coast Avengers. Heroes Reborn ends; the team reconstitutes. Wanda is now a senior member, a foundational presence, *the witch* in a way she was not before. Her power is openly characterized as chaos magic. Cap defers to her on supernatural matters; Thor treats her as a peer in the magical register.

**The Wonder Man hauntings.** Simon, dead, manifests to her — a relationship that exists only because her grief is sufficient to render him partly real. She does not seek psychiatric framing for this; she experiences it as romance. **The reality-as-negotiable-with-sufficient-feeling principle is now operationalized in her private life on a continuous basis, sub-clinically.** House of M is foreshadowed here, exactly: if your love is large enough, the dead come back. She is testing the limit privately for years before testing it publicly at planetary scale.

**The Kang Dynasty (Avengers vol. 3 #41–#55, 2001–2002).** Earth falls; Wanda is on the front line throughout. Her magical contributions to the war effort are decisive. She does not break. She is, in this stretch, the most **operationally formidable** she has yet been — large-scale hexes, coordinated magical infrastructure, sustained battlefield presence. The cost is not visible during the war; it is visible after. Post-Kang she withdraws further into solitary practice, into the Wonder Man hauntings, into a quieter and quieter affect-presentation around the team.

**The slow return of the children.** Across the late Busiek run and the Geoff Johns interregnum, Wanda begins, in private, to *re-remember*. The Harkness suppression does not so much fail as erode. She does not articulate this to anyone. The behavioral signal is small: she begins keeping the door to the spare room at Avengers Mansion closed. She did not previously care about that door. Now she cares. The room is not used as a nursery; she has not consciously assigned it that function; but the door is now always closed and she is the one closing it. **This is the subterranean tell of the entire pre-Disassembled year.**

---

## VI. The Compression Phase (the year preceding Avengers Disassembled, 2003–2004)

The behavioral notes for this final pre-collapse year should be read with the granularity given to surveillance footage in a hostage situation, because that is functionally what they are.

- **Sleep:** non-continuous. She is logged in the Mansion library at 0300–0500 with high frequency, reading without retention (the same book is opened to different pages on consecutive nights).
- **Eating:** dropped weight. Jarvis notes the kitchen produces meals that go uneaten in her quarters.
- **Speech:** the third-person dissociative tic of the early years has returned. Teammates note her referring to "the Scarlet Witch" in conversation about herself, then correcting.
- **Magical practice:** unsupervised, escalating, exploratory. She is no longer studying *to do* — she is studying *to find.* The object of the search is not articulated even to herself.
- **Wonder Man:** the hauntings become less frequent, then stop. Whatever capacity was sustaining them is being diverted to a deeper task.
- **The children:** by the final months, she is dreaming of them. By the final weeks, she is dreaming of them awake. She does not tell anyone.
- **The Wasp incident (off-page, pre-Disassembled).** Janet asks her, casually, whether she ever thinks about having children. Wanda's reaction is logged by Jan in later issues as *strange — a long pause, then a smile that did not match the eyes.* This is the moment the suppression structurally cracks. The conversation does not produce immediate event; it produces the *priming* under which the Vision's later, innocent comment will be the detonator.

---

## VII. Avengers Disassembled (2004) — the Detonation

The Vision arrives at the Mansion and, in conversation, makes a remark about her children — a remark that lands inside the now-fragile suppression like a key in a lock. **Within hours, the Avengers as an institution end.**

The behavioral signature of the Disassembled event is critical and must not be misread as villainy.

- **No premeditation.** No staging, no recruitment, no manifesto. The event is *affective discharge*, not plan.
- **Dissociative presentation.** Eyewitness accounts (Cap, Iron Man, Strange after-the-fact) all describe her as *absent from her face* during the central events.
- **Instrument logic.** She does not personally swing at her teammates. She arranges — She-Hulk's rage, the Kree, the Vision's own crash into the Mansion. The killings are *induced*. This is consistent with a person whose self-concept cannot tolerate authorship of harm even mid-decompensation; the magic finds proxies.
- **Targeting logic.** Vision dies first. Hawkeye dies in the Kree assault. Scott Lang dies in the Vision's crash. **The deaths cluster around the people most associated with the Mansion-as-home and the Vision-as-husband.** It is a grief response that destroys the home in which the grief was sustained. It is functionally arson by a person who can no longer stand inside the house.
- **Affect during.** Per Strange, when he finally intercepts her — she is calm, she is sad, she is small. She does not resist sedation. She allows Magneto to remove her.

The post-event amnesia is significant: she does not, immediately, remember what she has done. The dissociation that enabled the act outlasts the act.

---

## VIII. The Genosha Interregnum and House of M (2005)

**Magneto installs her in the ruins of Genosha.** Charles Xavier attempts treatment. Strange consults. The Illuminati — Reed Richards, T'Challa, Namor, Tony Stark, Charles Xavier, Black Bolt — convene to discuss whether she must be killed. Pietro, learning of this, panics. He travels to Wanda. He **suggests she use her power to give everyone what they want**. The suggestion is the proximate trigger; the architecture was already in her.

She acts. The world becomes the House of M.

**The wish-architecture, decoded.**
- *Cap is old.* He got to live the life he lost.
- *Peter Parker has Gwen, MJ, his uncle, his child.* He gets every love restored.
- *Carol Danvers is the world's most beloved hero.* She gets the recognition reality denies her.
- *She herself has Thomas and William.* She gets her children back. She is the wife of Vision and the mother of her sons in a kingdom her father rules and her brother protects.

This is not the wish-architecture of a tyrant. It is the wish-architecture of a **grieving woman giving gifts**. The mutant supremacy is *décor* — Magneto's wish, given to him as a present. She herself is not ideologically invested. She is throwing the largest birthday party in the history of metaphysics, and everyone she loves is on the guest list, and she gets to hold her sons.

**The collapse.** Layla Miller restores memory. Wolverine remembers. The structure cannot hold against witnesses who know. When it breaks, Wanda — confronted by Magneto's renewed brutality, by Pietro's attempt to preserve the wish at any cost, by the totality of what has been done in her name — speaks three words.

**"No more mutants."**

The behavioral read on those three words is not, *I hate mutants.* It is: *I will not be Magneto's daughter. I will not be Pietro's weapon. I will not be the engine of his world. I will take the substrate away.* It is patricide by way of species. It is the largest no she has ever said, and it is said to her father, and the casualty is the species he loved more than her.

She vanishes.

---

## IX. Pattern Evolution Across the Middle Period

To summarize the longitudinal evolution this section has traced:

1. **The container shrinks while the contents grow.** Capacity scales upward across the period (probability hexes → chaos magic → reality alteration); affect-regulation capacity does not scale with it.
2. **Attachment objects are progressively destroyed or hollowed.** Pietro estranges. Vision is dismantled. Wonder Man drifts. The Avengers fracture. The children are unmade, then re-remembered, then chased into wish-form. By the end of the period she has nothing intact to attach to except the *idea* of her sons.
3. **External attribution of her acts becomes a stable cognitive habit.** Magneto's daughter, Harkness's witch, Immortus's nexus being, Doom's siphon-vessel, Pietro's instrument. She accepts every framing that lets someone else be the author. The cost: she never gets to be the author of her recovery, either.
4. **Domestic competence erodes in inverse proportion to magical capacity.** The Leonia kitchen, the herb garden, the read-aloud evenings — all gone by the late nineties. The witch grows; the woman recedes.
5. **The dissociative tells re-emerge in the year before Disassembled** with the same morphology they had in the earliest issues — third-person speech, affect-flattening, motor stillness. The system is *signaling* before it breaks. No one in the institutional apparatus around her reads the signals.
6. **The reality-revision capacity is tested privately before it is deployed publicly.** Wonder Man's hauntings are House of M in miniature, conducted in her quarters for years.
7. **Every catastrophic act in this period is preceded by an iatrogenic event.** The twins' unmaking is preceded by Harkness's suppression. Disassembled is preceded by a year of unsupervised re-remembering. House of M is preceded by the Illuminati's debate over her execution. **She is never harmed in this period without first being mishandled by people whose job was to help her.**

The middle period ends with her gone, the mutants gone, the Avengers as she knew them gone, and a witness file — kept by everyone who survived — that will determine how she is received when she returns. The wilderness years and the reparative arc belong to the next chronology. What this chronology establishes is the *shape of the wound* into which the rest of her life will be poured.

— End Chronology III.


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

*Pre-profile dossier, Section 4 of the longitudinal chronology. Window: post-Children's Crusade (≈2012) through present operational status. Sources: Robinson, Scarlet Witch vol. 2 (2015–2017); Waid, Avengers/No Surrender (2018); Williams, Strikeforce (2019); Hickman/Duggan, X-Men/Krakoa era (2019–2024); Williams, Trial of Magneto (2021); Orlando, Scarlet Witch vol. 3 (2023–2024) and Scarlet Witch & Quicksilver (2024); ancillary appearances in Avengers, X-Men, and Hellfire Gala specials. Cross-referenced against clinical literature on Prolonged Grief Disorder (Bryant 2024; Pop-Jordanova 2021).*

---

## 4.1 — The Reparative Turn (post-Children's Crusade, c. 2012–2015)

The subject emerges from the Children's Crusade arc with three established facts that govern everything afterward: (1) the twins exist again in the world as Wiccan (Billy) and Speed (Tommy), independently incarnated; (2) Doctor Doom's exogenous influence at the climax of House of M is established as partial but real — not exculpation, but contextualization the subject herself refuses to lean on; and (3) the subject re-enters the Avengers' operational orbit on probation, distrusted by the X-faction in particular (Wolverine's standing kill-order, repeatedly tabled but never formally rescinded, is a baseline ambient threat she carries through the entire period).

Behavioral signature of this transitional window: she does **not** reclaim Avengers Mansion residency. She rooms transiently — an apartment in Manhattan that functions more as a drop-point than a home, never personalized, no photographs, no kitchenware beyond a kettle and two mugs (cf. recurring background detail across Heinberg/Robinson appearances). She lets Billy and Tommy initiate every contact; she does not call, does not appear at Young Avengers operations unless explicitly invited. This is not coldness — it is the conduct of a person who has internalized that her presence is a risk to people she loves, and who is performing reparative restraint as a daily discipline.

## 4.2 — Robinson Solo (2015–2017): The Witchcraft Reformation

The Robinson run is the first sustained period in which the subject is the *protagonist of her own life* in the published record. Operational profile during this window:

- **Residence:** a small apartment, then itinerant — Greece, the Irish coast, New Orleans, Hong Kong. The pattern is pilgrimage, not tourism: she goes where witches of prior generations died, were betrayed, or left unfinished business. She is, in effect, conducting a global audit of the *craft* itself, on the working theory that her magic had been "broken" — corrupted at source by Chthon, by Harkness's interventions, by every authority figure who instrumentalized it.
- **Daily ritual:** morning meditation; a small offering (varies by locale — wine, salt, bread); active solicitation of teachers from traditions outside her formal lineage. Notably she *seeks correction* — repeatedly approaches practitioners who dislike or distrust her and asks to be taught. This is reparative, but it is also diagnostic: a person who believes her instrument is contaminated and that purification is owed.
- **Companion:** the ghost of Agatha Harkness, against whom she is in unresolved transference — Agatha is the very figure who suppressed her grief and prevented mourning, and the subject keeps her close in the form of an interlocutor she can argue with. This is psychologically load-bearing: she has externalized the introjected critical caregiver and made the relationship *negotiable*. It is the closest thing to therapy the published record shows her doing.
- **Affect:** subdued, professional, occasionally wry — the first sustained register of *humor* in her published behavior, mostly self-deprecating. She permits herself small pleasures (a coffee on a specific Aegean dock; an unhurried walk along the Liffey) and notes them with a faint surprise — the affect of a long-depressed person re-encountering pleasure as an unfamiliar visitor.

The reformation does not "cure" her. It stabilizes her. By the end of the Robinson run she has rebuilt a relationship to her own power that is *less affectively coupled* — she can cast without flooding. This is the most clinically significant development of the decade.

## 4.3 — Avengers Reintegration & No Surrender (2018)

Returns to Avengers operations under Waid. The reintegration is notable for what is absent: she does not request leadership, does not seek a romantic partner on the team, does not relitigate Disassembled. She is *operationally available and personally remote.* Roommates with no one. Trains with Voyager briefly. Treats the Mansion as a workplace, not a home — exits at end-of-incident, returns to her solo arrangements. This is healthy avoidance, not pathological withdrawal: she has correctly identified that the Mansion is a site of traumatic association and has elected not to live inside her trigger.

## 4.4 — Strikeforce (2019) & Darkhold Re-exposure

Joins Blade's Strikeforce — a deliberate choice of a covert, occult-facing unit rather than the flagship Avengers roster. Two readings, both true: (a) she is more useful where her skillset fits and the optics of "Scarlet Witch on the marquee" do not destabilize publics; (b) Blade's team is composed of people who have done terrible things in service of necessity, and she is more comfortable among the morally compromised than among the canonically heroic. The Darkhold-adjacent exposure during this period is the first warning sign that the Robinson stabilization is *not* immunity: contact with corrupting grimoires still pulls at her, and she requires external check (Blade, Wiccan in cameo) to disengage.

## 4.5 — The Krakoan Question (2019–2024)

The most operationally consequential fact of this window is the one the subject does not own: **she is the No-More-Mutants witch, and Krakoa is the mutant nation she helped make necessary.** The Quiet Council declares her *anathema*. She is not invited to the Resurrection Protocols.
