**Operation, mild.** The "no more mutants" verbalization is displacement at psychotic intensity (see 7.4.3), but lower-grade displacement appears across her record: anger at Magneto displaced onto the Brotherhood-era enemies she fought without complaint; grief at the twins displaced onto over-protectiveness of the Young Avengers; resentment of the Avengers' early dismissal of her abilities displaced into self-doubt rather than confrontation.

### 7.3.6 Isolation of Affect

**Episodic.** During tactical operations she separates feeling from event with high fidelity — a sister-defense to suppression. The risk is when isolation of affect persists past the operation and becomes the steady-state, which is the pre-decompensation profile observed in the months before Disassembled: flat affect, normal cognition, no narrative complaint, then collapse.

---

## 7.4 — The Immature Tier (Vaillant Level II)

### 7.4.1 Idealization

**Operation.** Each successive caretaker is initially elevated to a position that the actual person cannot sustain. Magneto-as-rescuer (he was not); Pietro-as-protector (he was, partially, but also a captor); the Avengers-as-true-family (closer to true, but still a workplace); Vision-as-perfect-partner (the most defensible idealization, but still an idealization of his unflappability).

**Behavioral signature.** Early-relationship overestimation followed by long stretches of denying the idealized figure's documented behavior. She does not stop seeing what Magneto is; she stops *registering* it.

### 7.4.2 Identification with the Aggressor

**Operation.** Adoption of Magneto's framework of mutant exceptionalism during the Brotherhood era; later, more subtly, the adoption of the very tool of his violence (mass reality-alteration as policy) in House of M. The wish-world she constructs is, in structure, a Magneto-shaped solution — a top-down, single-actor remaking of reality for the benefit of an in-group. She critiques the man and then, under collapse, *thinks like him.*

**Failure mode.** The identification is unconscious and is one of the most dangerous mechanisms in her stack, because it routes her capability through her abuser's worldview at precisely the moment she is least equipped to notice.

### 7.4.3 Passive Aggression

**Largely absent.** She is not a sulker, a slow-walker, a withholder. The absence is striking and supports the diagnostic distinction from BPD: where Borderline structure would generate chronic interpersonal grievance discharged sideways, Wanda absorbs grievance and converts it (via reaction formation) into care. The cost is paid intrapsychically.

### 7.4.4 Acting Out

**Rare and event-bound.** Her two unambiguous acting-out episodes (the Disassembled rampage; the post-grief assault on Vision) are not character pattern — they are the lower tiers detonating. Outside of acute decompensation she does not act out. She is, between crises, behaviorally over-controlled to the point of stiffness.

### 7.4.5 Somatization

**Probable, under-documented.** Pseudocyesis itself can be read as somatization on the grandest scale her physiology could produce — the unmet maternal drive expressed in body before metaphysics intervened. Lower-grade somatic correlates likely include headache, insomnia, anorexia in stress periods; her file should track these prospectively as decompensation prodrome.

---

## 7.5 — The Psychotic Tier (Vaillant Level I)

This is the floor. When the upper three tiers fail, these are the mechanisms that catch her — and they are catastrophic both because they distort reality and because, uniquely in her case, *her reality distortions become other people's reality.*

### 7.5.1 Denial (Psychotic-Intensity)

**Operation.** The refusal to acknowledge an external fact that is incompatible with psychic survival. The literature (Pop-Jordanova 2021) flags disbelief/denial as a central feature of complicated grief, particularly after sudden/violent loss; in Wanda the denial response is amplified by capability to the point of enactment. House of M is denial *made physical:* the children exist, Vision is whole, Pietro is well, the mutants are ascendant. The wish-world is the cognitive structure of "this cannot be" extruded into spacetime.

**Behavioral signature in the denial state.** Calm. Eerily calm. Subjects in the House of M construct describe her demeanor as serene, maternal, slightly absent — the affect of a person whose pain has finally stopped. This is the diagnostic: when she is most peaceful in crisis, the denial defense is at peak load.

**Failure mode.** Denial cannot hold against direct confrontation by the loved object she has constructed (Wiccan, in the canon). When the construct collapses, the affect that denial had been holding back surges out as the next defense in the stack: distortion-via-omnipotent-rage.

### 7.5.2 Omnipotent Fantasy / Wish-Cognition

**Operation.** Magical thinking that, in her case, is not metaphor — wish becomes outcome at the limit of chaos magic. The defense exists in every patient; in Wanda it has a real-world output channel. The structural problem is that the defense was *adaptive in childhood* (a frightened mutant girl who could wish away danger and have it happen) and was never developmentally retired because it never had to be.

**Behavioral signature.** Under stress, her formulations become increasingly *declarative* — "no more mutants" is the limit case, but smaller versions appear throughout the record: she states what she wishes were true with the syntactic finality of a fact. The pre-decompensation linguistic shift toward declaratives is a tracking marker.

### 7.5.3 Distortion (Reality-Reshaping)

**Operation.** Gross reshaping of external reality to fit internal need, distinct from denial in that denial *negates* the unwanted fact while distortion *replaces* it with a constructed substitute. House of M is denial-plus-distortion: the loss is negated and the substitute reality is built around the negation. The "No More Mutants" pronouncement is distortion's discharge phase — the construct cannot be sustained, so the threat (the species whose existence was used to weaponize her) is removed instead.

### 7.5.4 Psychotic Projection

**Limited.** She does not chronically attribute her own impulses to others. The exception is the post-collapse self-loathing, in which she correctly identifies what she has done — this is not projection but accurate appraisal. The absence of projection is part of why her conscience remains hyperactive and why she does not slide into the villain-frame her actions would license.

---

## 7.6 — Compensatory Mechanisms (Behaviorally Observable)

Distinct from the defenses proper — these are the *constructed coping infrastructures* she has built on top of the defensive substrate.

**Positive (adaptive) compensations.**

- **The work-shop / open-door practice** (Orlando-era). A literal compensatory architecture: a place to be useful, a stream of strangers whose needs structure her days, a magical practice that channels capability into discrete, completable acts. Functionally a self-prescribed occupational therapy.
- **Chosen-family construction.** The Avengers, the Young Avengers, the post-resurrection mutant community. She rebuilds family of choice each time biology and history fail her. The repetition is not pathological; it is the compensation working.
- **Ritualized small domesticity.** Tea-making, garden-keeping, the maintenance of a personal aesthetic (the consistent red coloration, the careful hair, the quiet wardrobe). These micro-rituals stabilize the day when larger structures are absent.
- **Acceptance of consequence.** She does not flee accountability. This is a learned compensation, post-2005, and it functions as a brake on the lower tiers — knowing she will answer for what she does provides a tether that wish-cognition would otherwise sever.
- **Magical practice as containment.** Formal study under Agatha (despite the harm), later self-taught discipline — the work of *structuring* magic operates as a meta-defense against the unstructured magic that emerges in decompensation. Practice is prophylaxis.

**Negative (maladaptive) compensations.**

- **Power as affect-regulator.** Use of magical output to discharge feeling rather than to accomplish a goal. The signature is magic that *exceeds the task* — a hex larger than the threat, an alteration broader than the request. Each instance is a data point.
- **Substitute partners.** Wonder Man as Vision-template. The selection pattern reveals the compensation: she does not seek a new attachment; she seeks the lost one in different skin.
- **Caretaker-dependency.** Across decades, allowing a series of magically powerful older figures (Harkness, Doom in brief, others) to position themselves as her teacher, with insufficient discrimination. The compensation for the lost paternal object is the acceptance of new ones who resemble it.
- **Reality-revision as grief-bypass.** The most dangerous maladaptive compensation, because it works — briefly. The wish-world genuinely relieves the grief for the duration of its sustainment. The reinforcement schedule is the problem: relief, however brief, of grief that severe, is a powerful learning signal.
- **Self-punitive over-functioning.** The reparative arc, when fueled by guilt past the point of vitality, becomes its own pathology — she will work herself into collapse rather than accept that reparation has a ceiling.

---

## 7.7 — Defenses Ranked by Primitiveness (Operational Summary)

From most mature (top) to most primitive (bottom), with rough estimated proportional load at baseline (B) and under severe stressor (S):

1. **Sublimation** — B: 25% / S: 5%
2. **Altruism** — B: 15% / S: 5%
3. **Suppression** — B: 10% / S: 5%
4. **Humor** — B: 3% / S: 0%
5. **Reaction formation** — B: 10% / S: 5%
6. **Repression** — B: 15% / S: 10% (and fatiguing)
7. **Reparation-as-defense** — B: 15% / S: 10%
8. **Isolation of affect** — B: 5% / S: 10%
9. **Displacement** — B: 2% / S: 5%
10. **Idealization** — B: low / S: rises
11. **Identification with the aggressor** — B: latent / S: emerges
12. **Somatization** — B: subclinical / S: rises
13. **Denial (psychotic-intensity)** — B: 0% / S: up to dominant
14. **Omnipotent fantasy / wish-cognition** — B: 0% / S: up to dominant
15. **Distortion (reality-reshaping)** — B: 0% / S: catastrophic

The shape of the table is the warning. At baseline she is a Vaillantian Level IV/III presentation — a more mature defensive structure than the median Avenger. Under severe stressor the entire upper apparatus offloads to Level I within hours. There is no intermediate stable position. The architecture is **bimodal**, and bimodal defensive architectures in subjects with metaphysical capability are the single highest-yield risk category in this file.

---

## 7.8 — Clinical and Operational Implications

The defensive inventory yields three actionable readings.

**First**, the upper-tier defenses are genuine and worth protecting. Interventions that disrupt her sublimatory channels (closing the shop, removing her from her chosen family, denying her work) will not produce a calmer subject — they will accelerate the slide toward the lower tier by removing the energy sinks that keep the upper tier loaded. Her stability is *built of her work.*

**Second**, repression must not be reinforced. The Harkness intervention is the cautionary tale: every authority figure who has attempted to *manage* her grief by suppressing it has produced a larger eventual discharge. The clinical literature (Bryant et al. 2024) supports structured grief work — CBT-for-PGD — as the indicated treatment, and the indication is doubly strong here because the alternative (continued repression) has already been tested at scale and has already failed at scale.

**Third**, the early-warning signature of decompensation is *not* visible distress. It is the opposite: a deepening calm, increased declarative speech, magic that exceeds task, withdrawal into ritualized domesticity, and a faint smile that does not reach the eyes. Subjects with her defensive architecture do not telegraph collapse through agitation; they telegraph it through unnatural quietness. **Watch the calm.**

— End Section 7. Section 8 (Personality Synthesis) may proceed.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE — WANDA MAXIMOFF

*Section 5 of the UATU Intelligence Dossier. Decade-by-decade clinical mapping of affect regulation, cognitive style, and self-concept across the published behavioral record (1964–present). Frameworks used: attachment theory (Ainsworth/Main; Bartholomew & Horowitz four-category model), Vaillant's hierarchy of defenses, Linehan's affect-regulation model, Kernberg's structural interview taxonomy (identity diffusion / reality-testing / defensive organization), and the ICD-11 Prolonged Grief Disorder construct (Bryant et al., 2024; Pop-Jordanova, 2021). All inferences derived from cited behavioral record.*

---

## I. THE TRANSYLVANIAN / BROTHERHOOD PERIOD (c. 1964–1965 publication; subject in late adolescence / early twenties)

### Affect regulation
At first appearance (X-Men #4) Wanda's affect is **constricted, fear-modulated, and vigilance-driven**. She does not display the affective range that would be expected of a young woman of her age cohort — no flashes of humor, no anger directed outward at her circumstances, no adolescent rebellion against Magneto despite being placed in lethal field operations. Affect is registered almost exclusively through **somatic tells**: she clutches at her temples when casting (an early canonical motor habit, retained for decades), she startles, she looks to Pietro for emotional referencing before responding to any non-routine stimulus. This is the **affective signature of a child raised under threat** — emotion is internalized, monitored for safety-relevance, and externalized only as anxious recruitment of a protector.

She demonstrates **no observable mid-range affect**. She is either flat or frightened. The absence of irritation, sulkiness, ordinary peeve — the mundane affects of a normally regulated young adult — is diagnostically significant: the regulatory bandwidth was already narrow before the catastrophic losses arrived.

### Cognitive style
Intuitive-associative from the outset. Her power is described in this period as "hexes" — probability disturbances she does not understand and cannot articulate. She does not study magic in this period; she **experiences** it. Cognitively she is reactive, image-bound, and shows no evidence of strategic forecasting. When Magneto plans, Wanda is briefed; she does not contribute tactically. She is **content as the instrument**, which in cognitive terms means she has outsourced her executive function to the dominant male in her field.

### Self-concept
Borrowed, in two halves. **"Magneto's recruit"** and **"Pietro's sister."** There is no third descriptor she would have offered for herself. Identity is purely relational and purely subordinated. In Kernbergian terms: identity diffusion is *not* yet diagnosable because she has not been asked to author anything; the absence is structural, not characterological. Reality-testing is intact; defenses are neurotic-to-immature (idealization of Magneto-as-rescuer, identification with the aggressor in her tolerance of Brotherhood violence she does not endorse).

---

## II. THE EARLY AVENGERS / KOOKY QUARTET PERIOD (c. 1965–1972; mid-twenties)

### Affect regulation
First evidence of **affective broadening under conditions of safety**. With Captain America's stewardship she displays gratitude, tentative humor, and the early gradients of romantic feeling toward the Vision. The regulatory expansion is real but **conditional and supervised** — she calibrates her affective output to the team's tolerance, never expressing dissent when she has it (and she has it; her discomfort with Hawkeye's bickering is registered behaviorally — withdrawal, proximity-seeking to Pietro or Vision — but never verbally). This is the period that establishes her lifelong **accommodative baseline**.

### Cognitive style
Begins to acquire procedural team-cognition (call signs, formations, mission discipline) but never transitions to a strategic register. Her contributions in planning sequences are typically affective — *"are we sure?"*, *"can we save them?"* — the conscience function of the team rather than the tactician. Power use is still intuitive; she does not yet conceptualize what she does. This **failure to develop a theory of her own ability** is one of the load-bearing features for everything that follows: the gift was never indexed, catalogued, or limited by self-knowledge.

### Self-concept
**First authored identity element: "Avenger."** Surrogate-family belonging produces the first identity-from-inside, though it remains affiliative rather than individual. The marriage to Vision (Giant-Size Avengers #4, 1975, just past the period boundary) is the *first decision she makes without a male caretaker's approval* — Pietro famously rages against it. Behaviorally she holds the line, which is the earliest evidence of a stable self that can resist enmeshment. The shape of the choice is also diagnostic: she chooses a partner whose **affective flatness guarantees non-abandonment and non-rage**. The selection criterion is *safety*, not passion. The synthezoid is the regulated object her nervous system has been hunting for.

---

## III. THE DOMESTIC / WEST COAST / CATASTROPHIC LOSS PERIOD (c. 1982–1991; late twenties to mid-thirties)

This is the **structural fracture decade** — the decade in which the personality is broken and then magically taped shut without repair.

### Affect regulation in the lead-up (Vision & the Scarlet Witch, 1982/1985 maxiseries)
Wanda enters her most expansively regulated period of life. The Leonia house, the suburban domesticity, the experience of pregnancy (pseudocyetic or otherwise — see Medical §2) and parturition produce a **brief flowering of broad-band affect**: maternal warmth, irritation, ordinary marital negotiation. This is the only published period in which she displays the *mundane* affects. Cognitively she becomes more organized (managing infants, household, neighbors) — the executive scaffolding that a stable attachment system makes possible.

### The fracture itself (West Coast Avengers #42–52, Byrne, 1989)
Two losses arrive simultaneously: Vision is captured, dismantled, and rebuilt as a blank white affect-stripped version who **rejects her**; the twins are revealed as soul-fragments and are *unmade*. By any contemporary grief framework — Bryant et al.'s prolonged-grief construct, Pop-Jordanova's account of sudden/violent loss as trauma-intensifier — this is a *maximal* loss event: dual, simultaneous, sudden, ontology-violating (the children *never were*), and stripped of any cultural ritual that could metabolize it.

### Her response — the load-bearing event
**She does not grieve.** There is no funeral, no mourning sequence, no anger phase, no depressive trough. Instead, Agatha Harkness performs an **iatrogenic memory excision** of the twins. Wanda *consents* to this, in the trance-like accommodative register that is her default. The defense organization shifts in a single move from neurotic (repression, idealization) to **primitive (dissociation, splitting, magical undoing)**. This is the moment her defenses cross the developmental Rubicon. From this point forward the structural diagnosis is no longer "anxious-accommodative young woman" but **a personality organized around an encapsulated, unprocessed catastrophic loss kept out of awareness by exogenous magical force**.

### Self-concept end of decade
Surface: stoic Avenger, returning to fieldwork. Deep: hollowed out. The "mother" identity is gone; the "wife" identity is destroyed and then ghoulishly returned as a stranger; the twin-sister identity persists but Pietro himself is increasingly unstable. She emerges from this decade with **all her authored identities revoked except "Avenger,"** and with a buried wound the size of two children.

---

## IV. THE BUSIEK / HEROIC RETURN PERIOD (c. 1998–2003; late thirties)

### Affect regulation
Eerily, **functionally improved**. This is the deceptive plateau — the period a clinician would mistake for recovery and a surveillance file should flag as the **most dangerous false negative** in the longitudinal record. With the wound suppressed, her affect appears proportionate, her teamwork excellent, her competence at peak. She takes the Avengers chair, executes leadership functions, and presents as a mature, regulated woman in her professional prime.

The **only tell** in this period is the romantic entanglement with Wonder Man, whose brainwave patterns were the template for Vision's emotional matrix. Choosing the *source code of the lost object* as a substitute is not the behavior of a grieved-and-resolved person; it is the behavior of a person whose grief has been put in a box and whose object-hunger is still steering partner selection at the substrate level. The substitution logic is unconscious and exact.

### Cognitive style
Sharpest of her published life. She is operating with executive clarity, leading missions, integrating new powers. Critically, **this is the period in which Harkness retroactively reframes her abilities as "chaos magic"** — a vast expansion of her conceptualized capability without a corresponding expansion of self-knowledge or limits. The mismatch — capability without integrated theory — is widening even as the surface looks fine.

### Self-concept
"Avenger" stabilizes; "Chairwoman" is added; the unconscious "bereaved mother" exerts no conscious pressure but is doing all the partner-selection work. Identity coherent on the surface; **structurally a coiled spring**.

---

## V. THE DECOMPENSATION PERIOD — DISASSEMBLED THROUGH HOUSE OF M (2004–2005; early forties)

### Affect regulation — total failure
The repressed returns; in the Bendis Disassembled sequence Wanda's regulatory system collapses end-to-end in compressed time. Phenomenology: **fugue-like dissociation, affect flooding, no executive braking, no flight, no gloating, no strategy**. She kills Vision, Hawkeye, and Scott Lang in a state that meets phenomenologic criteria for brief psychotic episode with mood-congruent features (Kernberg: a temporary collapse of reality-testing under maximal stressor, in a personality structurally vulnerable but not chronically psychotic).

The diagnostic signature is the **absence of villain-affect**: no triumph, no organized hostility, no demand. The destruction is the *shape of the grief made externally visible* — Avengers Mansion, the surrogate family's house, is destroyed; the husband (Vision) is destroyed; the friends are killed. The geography of the rampage *is* the topology of the wound.

### House of M — denial at the scale of capacity
The Bryant 2024 / Pop-Jordanova frame applies almost surgically. Disbelief and denial are the central affective-cognitive features of complicated grief; House of M is **disbelief made world-sized**. Everyone Wanda loves has what they want. Steve Rogers grew old. Peter Parker has MJ and May. *She has Thomas and William.* This is not a power play, not an ideology, not a coup — it is **wish-cognition fused with capability**. Cognitively this is primary-process dominance — dream-logic at planetary scale. Strategic cognition is absent. There is no exit plan because there is no plan; there is a wish.

The terminal three words — *"No more mutants"* — are the **anger phase**, discharged at the category Magneto weaponized her for. Not anti-mutant ideology; anti-the-world-that-took-her-children, narrowed to the population her father made her the instrument of.

### Self-concept at decade's hinge
Annihilated. By the end of House of M she is the mutant who unmade mutants, the mother whose love killed her friends, the daughter who became her father's worst projection. **Identity collapses into pure negative content.**

---

## VI. THE WILDERNESS / AMNESIAC PERIOD (2005–2010; mid-forties)

### Affect regulation
Unknown by direct observation; she is **off the grid**, found later in Children's Crusade in an amnesiac state in Latveria. The functional picture on rediscovery is **flat, confused, gentle** — the affect of someone with the wound and the memory of the wound both off-line. This is the **second iatrogenic dissociation** of her life, this time by Doom (with attendant exploitation). The pattern repeats: a powerful older man "helps" by suppressing rather than treating.

### Cognitive style
Diminished; foggy; pre-reflective. She is functionally a fugue-state outpatient with no chart and no clinician.

### Self-concept
Erased and partially rebuilt by an exploiter. **Re-confirms the lifelong vulnerability to caretakers who soothe by editing.**

---

## VII. THE RECOGNITION / REUNION PERIOD (2010–2014; late forties)

### Affect regulation
Reunion with Billy (Wiccan) and Tommy (Speed) — soul-reincarnated fragments of the lost twins — produces an affect signature unique in her record: **tentative, guilt-saturated, almost penitent, sustained over months rather than spiking**. She does not perform joy; she behaves like someone who knows she is not entitled to it. The regulation here is *better* than at any prior point because there is a *real attachment object on the other side of the wound* — the grief now has somewhere to go.

### Cognitive style
Re-emergent self-reflection. For the first time in the record she **looks at her own history and names it**. The Heinberg-era dialogue establishes the beginning of an autobiographical narrative — the precondition for any actual mourning work.

### Self-concept
First emergence of an authored, self-aware identity: **"a woman who did monstrous things in grief and must answer for them."** This is structurally an advance over every prior self-concept because it is the first one she generated rather than received.

---

## VIII. THE REPARATIVE PERIOD — SOLO RUNS AND KRAKOA (2015–present; fifties)

### Affect regulation
Re-broadened, but **organized around the reparative axis**. The Robinson solo run shows her traveling, accepting cases, addressing magical injuries one by one — controlled, modulated, available. The Orlando solo run formalizes this: a door that opens for anyone in magical need. Affect is warm, contained, attentive, and **chronically tinged with low-grade guilt**. There is no record in this period of irritation expressed at clients, of refusal, of self-protective boundary-setting. The accommodative baseline is intact, now serving a reparative ideology.

### Cognitive style
The most integrated of her life. She has finally **theorized her own power** (chaos magic as a discipline, witchcraft as a tradition she belongs to and studies). She seeks teachers, reads texts, codifies practice. The cognitive maturation lags her capability by forty years but it has arrived.

### Self-concept
**"Witch."** Authored, individual, traditional, locatable in a lineage. For the first time her identity is not purely relational — it is a *vocation*. Layered on top: "mother of Billy and Tommy" (now consciously held), "daughter of Magneto" (consciously reckoned with rather than passively borne), "the woman who said the three words" (carried as accountability rather than denied).

### The Trial and resurrection (2021)
Death and resurrection adds a final layer: **post-resurrection hyperactivity and near-manic reparative drive**. Clinically this is the risk vector of the present era — the reparative campaign is **affectively over-charged**, and over-charged reparation in a personality with her loss history is *fragile*. The structure looks like recovery; the structure is a recovery propped up by two living children and an absence of fresh catastrophe.

---

## IX. CROSS-DECADE SYNTHESIS — WHAT EVOLVED, WHAT DID NOT

### What evolved
- **Self-concept**: from purely relational and borrowed → to relational-and-vocational, partially self-authored.
- **Cognitive integration of power**: from intuitive-only → to theorized, lineage-located, partially limit-aware.
- **Autobiographical coherence**: from segmented (suppressed twins era) → to integrated narrative including the worst acts.
- **Defensive repertoire**: now includes higher-order defenses (sublimation through reparative work, altruism, intellectualization via magical study) layered over the still-present primitive ones.

### What did not evolve
- **Accommodative baseline**: she still cannot refuse a wounded person.
- **Affect-power coupling**: chaos magic remains affectively gated; the limbic safety interlock has never been installed.
- **Vulnerability to exploitative caretakers**: the Magneto template remains live; any sufficiently paternal manipulator with a plausible rescue narrative can still get inside.
- **Mid-range affect deficit**: she still does not sulk, complain, or express ordinary irritation. The container is wider but still binary at the extremes.
- **The encapsulated catastrophic loss**: better held, narratively integrated, but **not metabolized**. Bryant et al.'s grief-work protocols were never administered. The wound is dressed; the wound is not closed.

### The structural prediction
A personality organized for forty years around an unprocessed grief, partially integrated in the last decade through real attachment to the reincarnated twins and a reparative vocation, with primitive defenses still on standby beneath higher-order ones. **The recovery is real and is load-bearing only as long as both pillars hold**: (1) the continued existence and safety of Billy and Tommy; (2) the absence of a fresh catastrophic loss event. Remove either and the regression vector is steep — not necessarily to House of M baseline, because the cognitive integration and the authored "witch" identity are genuine gains, but to a decompensation whose ceiling is set by capability, not by intent.

She is, in clinical summary, **a woman who has done thirty years of grief work in the last ten and is not finished**, whose power requires her to finish, and whose handlers — every paternal figure who has ever stood near her — have systematically prevented the work from beginning.

— *End Section V. Proceed to Section VI: Relational Map.*


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — SUBJECT: WANDA MAXIMOFF

*Classification: UATU Dossier, Section 4 of 7. Independent clinical synthesis derived from the longitudinal behavioral record (1964–present). Clinical provenance cited in §4.9.*

---

## 4.1 Framing the Assessment

Before any diagnosis is offered, three framing constraints must be made explicit, because they shape every clinical inference that follows.

**First**, the subject's symptomatology cannot be cleanly separated from her capability. Most decompensations leave a person curled on a bathroom floor; hers depopulate a species. The phenomenology of the underlying disorder is, however, ordinary — what is extraordinary is the amplifier. A clinical reader must hold both: the disorders below are *common,* the consequences are *singular.*

**Second**, decades of her clinical course were corrupted by an iatrogenic event of the first magnitude. Agatha Harkness's magical excision of the memory of the twins (Vision and the Scarlet Witch arc; subsequently re-litigated through Avengers Disassembled and Children's Crusade) is best understood, in modern terms, as a *forced dissociative amnesia performed by a treatment provider.* No legitimate clinical course can be reconstructed without naming that event as the corruption-point. Everything afterward unfolds in a body whose grief was sealed in by a caregiver.

**Third**, the subject is a poor historian regarding her own internal states across precisely the periods of greatest clinical interest. Post-Disassembled, post-House of M, post-resurrection: she presents amnesia, partial recall, or affective flattening when asked to narrate. The dossier therefore reconstructs course *behaviorally,* which is the appropriate epistemology for any patient whose autobiographical access has been compromised.

---

## 4.2 Primary Diagnosis — Prolonged Grief Disorder (ICD-11 6B42; DSM-5-TR 309.89)

The primary diagnosis is **Prolonged Grief Disorder (PGD).** It is the load-bearing condition; nearly every other finding in this dossier is either a precursor to it, a defense against it, or a consequence of it.

**Index losses, in chronological order of clinical impact:**

1. The biological parents (childhood; pre-record). Loss is implied across the canonical retcons (Whizzer/Miss America fiction; later Magda/Django-Marya substrates; the Maximoff/Eisenhardt arrangement). The specifics are mutable, but the *fact* of early parental loss is invariant across every version. This is the priming event.
2. The twins Thomas and William (Vision and the Scarlet Witch #12 and successors). This is the *index complicated loss.* Onset of pathology proper.
3. The Vision, dismantled by the government, rebuilt without affect, withdrawn from her as a partner (West Coast Avengers, Byrne). Second wave; partner-loss compounding child-loss.
4. The Avengers as institutional family (Disassembled). Third wave; loss of surrogate-family object.
5. Pietro, repeatedly — through his pathology, his manipulations, and ultimately his death and the fractured aftermath. Fourth wave; loss of the twin/secure-base object.
6. Her own life (Trial of Magneto). The dead-and-resurrected sequence functions as a fifth, paradoxical loss — the loss of her pre-mortem self.

**PGD criteria mapping** (ICD-11 6B42 / DSM-5-TR 309.89, condensed):

- *Persistent and pervasive longing for or preoccupation with the deceased,* exceeding social/cultural norms and persisting beyond expectable timeframes (>6 months ICD; >12 months DSM): **Met, profoundly.** The twins are the organizing preoccupation across nearly every storyline from 1989 forward — even when she does not consciously remember them, the *shape* of the preoccupation surfaces (the choice to mother Wonder Man's reconstituted Vision, the obsessive maternal stance toward the Young Avengers, the door-always-open practice of the Orlando-era solo run).
- *Intense emotional pain* (sadness, guilt, anger, denial, blame, difficulty accepting the loss, feeling of loss of part of self): **Met.** All sub-affects on record.
- *Significant impairment in personal, family, social, educational, occupational, or other important areas of functioning:* **Met,** in a category of its own. The functional impairment includes the unmaking of the mutant species.
- *Symptoms not better explained by another mental disorder, substance, or medical condition:* This is where the clinician must work. See §4.4–4.7.

**The two cited references are dispositive.** Bryant et al. (2024) establish PGD as a discrete, treatable disorder with grief-cognition and depression as core, and identify CBT-for-PGD as the empirically supported intervention — *which she has never received.* Pop-Jordanova (2021) catalogues disbelief, denial, and anger as central features, with sudden/violent loss intensifying the trauma layer — a near-exact phenotype of the twin loss (sudden, unnatural, ontologically violating) and its sequelae. "No more mutants" is the **anger phase of complicated grief, discharged at capability scale.** House of M's wish-world is the **denial phase, rendered as architecture.** These are not metaphors; they are the symptoms as listed in the literature, with the dial turned to her output ceiling.

**Specifiers to apply:**

- *With prominent denial features* (the constructed reality is the symptom).
- *With traumatic features* (sudden, violent, ontologically destabilizing index loss; iatrogenic interference with mourning).
- *Recurrent course* (incomplete remission; re-decompensation at each subsequent loss).
- *In partial reparative remission* (current status; see §4.8).

---

## 4.3 Secondary Diagnosis — Dissociative Disorder, Unspecified (ICD-11 6B6Z; DSM-5-TR 300.15)

A dissociative disorder is comorbid and clinically central, not incidental. Evidence:

- **Dissociative amnesia, iatrogenic and recurrent.** The Harkness erasure is the index event. Subsequent amnestic episodes follow Disassembled and House of M (she is found wandering, without continuous autobiographical access, in the lead-up to Children's Crusade). The pattern — amnesia surrounding the highest-affect events — is textbook.
- **Depersonalization/derealization episodes.** Observable across the Disassembled sequence: the destruction of Avengers Mansion is performed in an affectively distant, almost somnambulant register. She is *present and not present.* Witnesses describe her face as wrong — affect-incongruent, blank-then-flooded.
- **Identity disturbance with dissociative flavor.** Distinct from the identity *fragility* discussed under personality (§5 of the larger dossier): there are periods in which she behaves as if *the woman who did the act is not the same woman now standing,* and this is not pure defensiveness — it has the cadence of genuine dissociative discontinuity.

A formal Dissociative Identity Disorder diagnosis is **not** supported. There are no consistent, named, switched alters with distinct autobiographical memory across stable contexts. The presentation is better captured as Dissociative Disorder Unspecified, with prominent amnestic and depersonalization features, *secondary to* and *interlocking with* the PGD.

---

## 4.4 Tertiary — Brief Psychotic Disorder, Recurrent, With Marked Stressor (DSM-5-TR 298.8; ICD-11 6A23)

Two episodes meet phenomenologic criteria for psychotic decompensation:

**Episode A — Avengers Disassembled (2004).** Acute onset following the return of repressed memory of the twins. Duration: hours to days. Features: delusional misidentification (perceives teammates as threats / instruments), grossly disorganized behavior, affective flooding, reality-testing failure. Resolution: spontaneous, with post-episode amnesia.

**Episode B — House of M (2005).** Acute onset under combined stressors (Illuminati deliberation regarding her containment; Pietro's destabilizing intervention; sustained grief reactivation). Duration: days to weeks. Features: systematized delusional construction (a coherent alternative reality), wish-fulfillment thought structure, suggestibility to influence from attachment figures (Magneto, Pietro), terminal disorganization with the three-word command. Resolution: with external intervention; post-episode confusion and partial amnesia.

Both episodes are **stress-bound, affect-congruent, time-limited, and leave no residual negative symptoms or formal thought disorder.** They satisfy criteria for Brief Psychotic Disorder with marked stressor, recurrent. They do **not** satisfy criteria for any disorder on the schizophrenia spectrum (see §4.7).

The exogenous-influence question (Doom siphoning chaos magic at the climax of House of M; Mephisto's involvement in the twin's substrate) is real and partially mitigating but **not exculpatory and not diagnostic-erasing.** A patient who is more susceptible to manipulation while in psychotic decompensation does not thereby fail to have been in psychotic decompensation. Vulnerability to exogenous influence is, if anything, a *feature* of the condition.

---

## 4.5 Quaternary — Complex Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (ICD-11 6B41)

C-PTSD is comorbid and developmentally upstream of the PGD. The criteria mapping:

- **Exposure to prolonged or repeated traumatic events from which escape is difficult or impossible.** Met: childhood displacement; coerced affiliation with Magneto's Brotherhood (the original "you owe me" recruitment that pressed her, frightened and uncomprehending, into terrorist activity she did not endorse); the long arc of being instrumentalized by a paternal figure whose love was conditional on weaponized compliance.
- **Core PTSD cluster** (re-experiencing, avoidance, sense of current threat): present in the Brotherhood-era flashback material across decades of canon; avoidance of Magneto-coded contexts in stable periods.
- **Disturbances in self-organization** (affect dysregulation, negative self-concept, interpersonal disturbance): all three present and chronic. The negative self-concept is particularly load-bearing — she does not *argue* with the label of monster; she preemptively concedes it.

C-PTSD explains the *substrate* into which the later grief catastrophes landed. A non-traumatized person who lost two children would suffer grievously; a person with her trauma history loses two children *into a self-concept that was already organized around being a danger and an instrument.* The grief lands in a body that has nowhere uninjured to put it.

---

## 4.6 Quinary — Major Depressive Episodes, Recurrent, in the Context of Grief (DSM-5-TR 296.3x)

Distinct from the grief-related depression that is *part of* PGD, there are discrete major depressive episodes documented across the record: the post-West Coast Avengers withdrawal; the long quiet between Disassembled and her rediscovery; periods within the Robinson solo run characterized by anhedonia, hypersomnia, and worthlessness cognitions presented as journal-voice narration. These are recurrent, moderate to severe, and have remitted between episodes — supporting MDD recurrent rather than persistent depressive disorder.

---

## 4.7 The Rigorous Differential — What She Is Not, and Why

This is where dossier rigor lives. The error-modes in assessing this subject are predictable and consequential; each must be named and refuted.

### 4.7.1 NOT Schizophrenia Spectrum Disorder (ICD-11 6A20; DSM-5-TR 295.x)

**Refutation:** Her psychotic episodes are stress-bound (not insidious-onset), affect-congruent (not bizarre or affectively incongruent), wish-shaped (not paranoid or persecutory in primary structure), and time-limited (not chronic). She exhibits **no negative symptoms** between episodes — no avolition, no alogia, no anhedonia outside of MDD contexts, no flat affect outside of dissociative episodes. She exhibits **no formal thought disorder** — her speech is coherent, goal-directed, syntactically intact across decades of documented dialogue. The duration criterion (≥6 months of disturbance for schizophrenia; ≥1 month for schizophreniform) is not met for any episode. **Diagnosis excluded.**

### 4.7.2 NOT Bipolar I Disorder (ICD-11 6A60; DSM-5-TR 296.4x)

**Refutation:** The reality-warping episodes superficially resemble manic decompensation — grandiose scope, decreased need for sleep during the construction, goal-directed activity at species scale. But the structure is wrong. There is no sustained elevated/expansive mood; the affective driver is grief, not euphoria. There are no documented hypomanic prodromes, no pressured speech, no flight of ideas in the technical sense, no sexual disinhibition or financial impulsivity. The "manic" appearance is the *grief-and-psychotic-denial* presentation viewed through a power amplifier. **Diagnosis excluded;** specifier of "with reparative hyperactivity" considered for post-resurrection period but does not meet criteria.

### 4.7.3 NOT Borderline Personality Disorder (ICD-11 6D11.5; DSM-5-TR 301.83)

**Refutation:** This is the *closest miss* in the differential and deserves the longest refutation. The surface fits: attachment instability, identity disturbance, reality-distorting episodes under abandonment stress. But:

- BPD requires **a pervasive pattern across contexts and over time, beginning by early adulthood.** Her instability is *event-driven,* not characterological. Between events she presents with stable, even over-controlled, affect.
- The frantic-efforts-to-avoid-abandonment criterion is not met. She *accepts* abandonment with terrible quietness. She does not call at 3 a.m.; she does not threaten; she does not cycle through devaluation/idealization within a relationship. Her idealizations are sustained for decades.
- Impulsivity in self-damaging domains (substance, sex, spending, reckless driving, binge eating) is **absent across the entire record.**
- Recurrent suicidal behavior, gestures, threats, or self-mutilation: absent.
- Chronic feelings of emptiness: present, but better accounted for by C-PTSD and PGD.
- Inappropriate intense anger: rare; when present, it is grief-rage, not the characterological storm of BPD.

**Diagnosis excluded.** The error of assigning BPD here is the dossier-reader's error of confusing *catastrophic episodic decompensation in a high-capability subject* with *characterological dysregulation.*

### 4.7.4 NOT Narcissistic Personality Disorder (ICD-11 6D11.4; DSM-5-TR 301.81)

**Refutation:** Grandiosity is absent. She does not require admiration; she requires *forgiveness.* Her reality-warps are wish-driven (for others as much as for herself — House of M is *everyone's* wish-world, not hers alone), not status-driven. She accepts blame instantly and disproportionately. She has no documented exploitation of others for self-aggrandizement, no envy pattern, no entitlement complaints. **Diagnosis excluded.**

### 4.7.5 NOT Antisocial Personality Disorder (ICD-11 6D11.2; DSM-5-TR 301.7)

**Refutation:** Conscience is *hyperactive.* The reparative arcs that define her post-2005 career are incompatible with ASPD. No history of childhood conduct disorder. No deceitfulness pattern. No reckless disregard for others — quite the opposite, a chronic over-regard at the cost of self. **Diagnosis excluded.**

### 4.7.6 NOT Histrionic Personality Disorder

**Refutation:** Attention-seeking is absent; she defaults to withdrawal. Affect is *under-displayed* at baseline. **Diagnosis excluded.**

### 4.7.7 NOT Schizotypal or Schizoid

**Refutation:** Magical thinking is operational, not pathological, in her phenomenology (she lives in a universe where it works). Eccentricity of dress and speech is not present. Capacity for and pursuit of close relationships is robust. **Diagnosis excluded.**

### 4.7.8 NOT Delusional Disorder (ICD-11 6A24; DSM-5-TR 297.1)

**Refutation:** The wish-realities are time-limited and embedded in psychotic decompensations with affective features, not chronic non-bizarre delusional systems in an otherwise intact subject. Duration criterion (≥1 month of delusions without other psychotic features) is not met by structure — the episodes are polymorphic, mood-saturated, and resolve. **Diagnosis excluded.**

### 4.7.9 NOT Substance-Induced Disorder

**Refutation:** No substance use history. The endogenous "intoxicant" is chaos magic itself, which is better conceptualized as a *capability that scales with affect* (§2 of the larger dossier) than as a substance. **Diagnosis excluded.**

### 4.7.10 NOT Factitious or Malingered Presentation

**Refutation:** The losses are documented; the affective phenomenology is consistent across decades and across observers with no secondary gain. **Diagnosis excluded.**

### 4.7.11 NOT a Primary Possession/Influence Disorder, Despite Exogenous Contributions

The Doom/Mephisto/chthonic-entity-of-the-week interventions across canon would, in a less rigorous file, prompt a primary diagnosis of "possession" or full exogenous attribution. The dossier rejects this. Exogenous actors have **exploited** her pathology; they did not **create** it. The grief is hers; the children were hers; the wish was hers. The hands that reached for the levers found the levers already built. **Primary exogenous attribution rejected;** acknowledged as aggravating factor.

---

## 4.8 Course Over Time

- **Pre-morbid (childhood–early adulthood).** Trauma-loaded substrate; C-PTSD developing. No grief disorder yet.
- **Brotherhood and early Avengers (1964–~1974).** C-PTSD active; defenses of compliance, identification, idealization of new family. Grief disorder not yet seeded.
- **Vision-marriage to twin-loss (1975–1989).** Quiescent baseline; brief reparative attempt at chosen family; catastrophic loss event; **iatrogenic suppression seals the wound.** PGD becomes latent.
- **Latent period (1989–2004).** PGD present but symptomatically masked by Harkness intervention; surface stability with subtle escalations (power expansion, "chaos magic" re-framing, Wonder Man substitution behavior).
- **First major decompensation (2004–2005).** Return of repressed → Brief Psychotic Episode A (Disassembled) → Brief Psychotic Episode B with systematized denial construction (House of M) → catastrophic discharge ("No more mutants").
- **Post-decompensation amnestic/fugue period (2005–~2010).** Dissociative wandering; partial recovery via reunion with Wiccan and Speed.
- **Reparative phase (2010–2021).** Active restitution; partial Decimation reversal; door-always-open service practice; chronic guilt-driven over-functioning meeting criteria for recurrent MDD.
- **Death and resurrection (Trial of Magneto, 2021).** Paradoxical loss-of-self; post-mortem reparative hyperactivity.
- **Current (2023–present, Orlando run and after).** Partial reparative remission of PGD. Dissociative features quiescent. C-PTSD chronic, managed. MDD intermittent. **No psychotic episodes since House of M.** Functional, productive, *but the remission is conditional* — on Wiccan and Speed's continued existence, on the absence of fresh catastrophic loss, and on the continued availability of reparative outlets.

---

## 4.9 Clinical Provenance

1. **Bryant et al. (2024).** *Cognitive Behavior Therapy vs Mindfulness in Treatment of Prolonged Grief Disorder: A Randomized Clinical Trial.* JAMA Psychiatry 81(7):646–654. DOI: 10.1001/jamapsychiatry.2024.0432. PMID: 38656428. **Application:** establishes PGD as a discrete, empirically defined, treatable disorder with grief-cognition and depression as core; defines the intervention (CBT-for-PGD) the subject has never received and which the dossier identifies as the appropriate first-line treatment.
2. **Pop-Jordanova (2021).** *Grief: Aetiology, Symptoms and Management.* Pril (Makedon Akad Nauk Umet Odd Med Nauki) 42(2):9–18. DOI: 10.2478/prilozi-2021-0014. PMID: 34699700. **Application:** grounds the denial-response phenomenology and the worsening trajectory under sudden/violent loss; supports the reading of House of M as the denial phase and "No more mutants" as the anger phase of complicated grief at capability scale.

---

## 4.10 Single-Sentence Synthesis

She is a Prolonged Grief Disorder patient with comorbid Dissociative Disorder, recurrent Brief Psychotic Episodes under stressor, C-PTSD, and recurrent MDD — held in partial reparative remission by the existence of her recovered children and the availability of restitutional outlets, and amplified at every decompensation by a capability that converts private symptom into public catastrophe.

— *End Section 4. Proceed to Section 5: Personality Synthesis & Operational Profile.*


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: WANDA MAXIMOFF

*Volume III of the UATU dossier. Cross-reference with §1 (History) for episode citations and §4 (Psychiatric) for the affective substrate underlying the patterns catalogued below. This atlas is observational and inferential, derived from sixty years of recorded conduct; it is organized by behavioral state, then within each state by channel (somatic, verbal, motoric, magical, social, decisional).*

---

## I. BASELINE — The Calm State

The calm Wanda is the Wanda observers most often misread. She presents as composed, slightly remote, attentive to others to a degree that registers as warmth but is, on close measurement, **vigilance shaped to look like warmth.**

**Somatic baseline.** Resting posture is small-framed: shoulders rolled slightly inward, weight on the back foot when standing, hands often clasped at the abdomen or resting on her own opposite forearm — a self-touch loop that recurs across every era of the record (Englehart panels through Orlando's run). When seated she folds: ankles crossed, knees together, one hand at the collarbone or the base of the throat. The throat-touch is among her most reliable tells; it appears when she is about to speak in a room she does not feel safe in, and disappears entirely in conversations with the twins, with Vision, or alone with Pietro before the rupture.

**Eye behavior.** Sustained eye contact when listening; broken eye contact when speaking. The break direction is consistent — down and to her left, the classic recall-mode lateralization — which over decades has the side effect of making her appear shy or evasive. She is neither. She is **rehearsing.** Wanda composes sentences before delivering them at a rate suggesting she is checking each one against an internal monitor for what the room can tolerate.

**Voice.** Mid-register, breath-supported, slow cadence. Trailing phrases rather than declarative endings. Pre-speech inhalation is audible to anyone within a meter — a small catch before complex statements. Accent traces (the Transian/Romani inflection of the early canon, the European softness retained through Englehart and Robinson) emerge under fatigue and disappear under combat.

**Hands.** The signature. At rest, her hands are never quite still — fingers test the air at hip-height as if checking the temperature of the magic. This is unconscious; she has done it since the Brotherhood era. When concentrating she will rotate the heel of one palm against the other in a slow, deliberate circle. When happy and unguarded (rare; recorded chiefly in domestic Vision-era scenes and in moments with Billy) the hands go still and she touches her own face — a thumb to the jaw, a knuckle to the cheek.

**Decision habits at calm.** Defers preference in low-stakes choices (food, route, seating) and is *grateful* when others decide. Initiates only in two domains: (1) acts of service to a specific person in distress, and (2) aesthetic micro-decisions — the arrangement of a room, the light level, the placement of objects. She is a compulsive *adjuster* of environments: candles re-positioned, a chair turned three degrees, a curtain pulled half an inch. The Orlando-era shop reads as the maximal expression of this — an entire establishment arranged so that strangers in trouble can find her.

**Sleep and circadian.** Late-night functioning, slow mornings. Repeated record of Wanda awake after the household sleeps, walking interior perimeters, making tea. The tea-making is ritual rather than appetite — heating water she does not always drink. Insomnia is conditional, not chronic: she sleeps well beside a trusted body (Vision in his sleep-cycle mode; Billy as an infant in the lost continuity), poorly alone after any event that disturbs her affective baseline.

**Dress.** Across continuities, a near-pathological consistency of *red.* The color is not vanity; it is **self-identification through a single fixed signifier** in a life where every other identity marker has been revoked or reissued. When she is well, the red is muted and integrated (a sash, lining, embroidered detail). When she is unwell, the red saturates and the silhouette sharpens — the headdress reappears, the cape lengthens. The costume escalates with the symptom. A field handler should treat any sudden re-saturation of the red palette as a clinical sign.

---

## II. UNDER MILD STRESS

Mild stress for Wanda is the daily background of being looked at by people who remember House of M. Her response is a tightening, not a loosening.

**Somatic shift.** The self-touch loop accelerates. The throat-hand appears earlier in the conversational arc. Breathing becomes shallower and moves higher in the chest. Shoulders rise approximately a centimeter — visible in any side-on photograph if one has prior frames to compare. She begins to **angle her body away** from the stressor while keeping her face turned toward it, a half-second flinch arrested by manners.

**Verbal shift.** Sentences shorten. Qualifiers multiply: *I think,* *perhaps,* *if you'd like,* *only if it helps.* She becomes grammatically smaller. The accent traces strengthen. She apologizes for things she did not do — a reflex that has been documented from the Englehart Avengers through the Krakoa-era X-titles.

**Withdrawal pattern.** Removes herself from group settings on a plausible errand (tea, fresh air, "I should check on—"). Re-emerges within ten to fifteen minutes, composed. This is not avoidance; it is **regulation through solitude**, brief and effective. Interrupting the withdrawal is the second-fastest way to escalate her — *blocking her from leaving a room* is taken by her nervous system as a threat cue.

**Magical shift.** Output becomes slightly less precise — hex effects acquire a halo of secondary phenomena (lights flickering, small objects shifting unbidden). She herself notes this in Robinson's run as a tell she watches in herself; it is also visible to trained mages around her. Magic at mild stress is **leaky** rather than dangerous.

**Service escalation.** Mild stress paradoxically increases her caretaking behaviors toward others. She will offer to make food, to listen, to help with an unrelated task. The mechanism is straightforward: in the role of helper she has a script; without one she is exposed.

---

## III. UNDER MODERATE STRESS — Interpersonal Conflict, Betrayal, Public Scrutiny

The moderate-stress Wanda is the one most often weaponized against by her enemies, because the somatic compliance reads, falsely, as compliance of will.

**Somatic.** Skin pales at the throat and across the upper chest; flush at the cheekbones (the autonomic split visible in close panels from Disassembled forward). Hands cool. A near-constant fine tremor in the fingers — visible when she gestures, masked when she clasps. The throat-touch becomes a throat-*hold,* fingers spread across the clavicle as if physically containing something. Jaw set; she begins to swallow more often than baseline.

**Verbal.** Long silences. She will let an accusation hang and decline to defend herself, which her interlocutors typically misread as guilt or as contempt. It is neither — it is the **rehearsal monitor at full load.** When she does speak, she speaks slowly and tells the truth, often the truth that hurts her position. She does not lie under pressure; she **omits.** The omission tell is a half-second pause before a pronoun.

**Eye behavior.** Eye contact lengthens past comfort. Where calm Wanda breaks gaze to speak, moderate-stress Wanda holds gaze and goes still. The stillness is the signal; if the hands also stop moving, escalation is imminent.

**Magical.** Ambient warping of her immediate vicinity: low-grade probability shifts (a glass cracks, a light fails, a door that was closed is open). She does not intend these and is often the last in the room to notice. The reliable indicator: **red micro-discharges at the fingertips,** dim enough to be missed in daylight, unmistakable in shadow. Across the record, anyone who has spent time near her learns to watch the hands first.

**Decisional.** She becomes radically *concrete.* Abstract debate is intolerable; she will redirect toward the next physical action — *let me get him out of here first, then we can talk about it.* This is a strength under field conditions and is repeatedly the behavior that ends crises early. The moderate-stress Wanda is, operationally, often the most useful Wanda.

**Affiliation pattern.** Under moderate stress she will physically move toward whichever person in the room she trusts most — usually within arm's reach, often touching their sleeve or back. If no such person is present, she moves toward a child, an injured party, or an animal. If none of those is present, she moves toward a wall.

---

## IV. UNDER THREAT — Direct Combat, Imminent Physical Danger

Threat resolves her ambivalence. The dithering vanishes.

**Posture.** Spine straightens, shoulders drop, weight shifts forward to the lead foot. The headdress (when worn) frames the face; the cape becomes part of the silhouette. She becomes **taller** by perceptible inches without changing footwear — a postural unfolding that long-time observers (Cap, Steve Rogers, in multiple recorded incidents) have learned to read as the all-clear-for-violence signal.

**Hands.** Open, raised to mid-chest or above the head depending on scale of working. Fingers spread, palms outward. The signature ring-and-middle-finger curl with the index and pinky extended (a gesture stabilized across artists from Pérez forward) is her **default firing stance**; deviations from it indicate either improvisation or a larger working.

**Voice.** Drops half a register. Cadence becomes clipped and declarative. Commands rather than requests. Polite forms drop entirely — she will use bare imperatives with people she normally addresses with deference. The accent recedes; her diction becomes neutral and unaccented in mid-combat, returning only in the aftermath.

**Targeting behavior.** **She does not strike first.** Across the record this is among the most consistent patterns — she gives a verbal warning, often two, before acting. The warnings are unornamented: *Stop. Don't.* When she does act, she prefers **disabling** to lethal force: a binding, a sleep, a probability collapse that makes the opponent's weapon fail. Lethality is reserved for threats to specific protected persons (the twins; in extremis Vision and Pietro).

**Decisional tempo in combat.** Fast intuitive selection, slow tactical adaptation. She is not a chess-player; she is a **goalie.** Reactive excellence, proactive hesitation. Pair her with a strategist (Cap, Strange) and her ceiling is essentially uncapped; leave her in command and she will default to defensive postures and protection of non-combatants.

**Bystander behavior.** Will interrupt her own offensive action to shield a civilian. Will accept tactical disadvantage to do so. This is consistent across every continuity and is the single most reliable pattern in her combat profile.

**Post-combat.** Hands go to her own face, then to her own hair. She checks her body for injury after she checks the others — a sequence that field-medic types around her have learned to invert by asking her directly. She is **slow to disengage from the threat scan;** she will keep looking at the doorway, the window, the body on the floor, for one to two minutes after others have stood down.

---

## V. IN INTIMACY — Romantic, Familial, Trusted-Friend Conditions

The intimate Wanda is the one most of the record never sees and the one her enemies most consistently fail to model.

**Somatic.** The self-touch loop transfers to the trusted other. With Vision: hand on his forearm, fingers tracing the seam of the synthezoid plating — a tactile checking-in that doubles as comfort to herself. With the twins (in the lost domestic continuity and after their reincarnation as Billy and Tommy): she touches their hair, the backs of their necks, the crowns of their heads. With Pietro: forehead-to-forehead, a Romani-coded gesture preserved across continuities and emphasized in Robinson's run.

**Voice.** The rehearsal monitor disengages. Speech becomes faster, less qualified, more humorous. Wanda has a dry, slightly self-deprecating wit that surfaces *only* in safe company; outside it she is mistaken for humorless. With Vision she is recorded teasing him about his color, his vocabulary, his earnestness — the only consistent register in which she initiates rather than receives.

**Eye behavior.** Sustained, soft, with frequent blinks and small smiles. The downward-left gaze-break disappears entirely. She looks *at* the trusted face for long stretches without speaking — a behavior that has been mistaken, by hostile observers reviewing surveillance, for distress. It is the opposite.

**Disclosure pattern.** Discloses *retroactively* — she tells trusted others about old fears once they have passed, rarely about current ones. The trusted other learns of the fear only after the danger is gone. This is a containment behavior, not a trust failure; she protects those she loves from the weight of her own interior weather.

**Conflict in intimacy.** Avoids it past the point of utility. Will absorb minor injuries (criticism, neglect, dismissal) from intimates without comment, then **address them weeks later** in a single quiet sentence that the recipient often does not realize is the conclusion of a long internal process. Vision learned to listen for these sentences; Pietro never did.

**Physical proximity.** Sleeps better with a body in the room. Will arrange herself slightly behind the trusted other when walking in unfamiliar space — a half-step lag that gives her line of sight on the other's flanks. With the twins, this inverts: she walks behind them when they are in front, in front of them when they are behind, always interposed between them and any unmapped vector.

---

## VI. IN GRIEF

Grief is the central state. Every other state is a defense against it. When grief breaks through the defenses, the presentation is **bimodal** and the modes do not blend.

**Mode A — Contained grief.** Eerily quiet. Face blank or near-blank; movements economical. She will perform routine tasks (tidying, cooking, brushing her hair) with abnormal precision and abnormal slowness. Sentences become very short or disappear. The throat-hand becomes constant. She does not weep in this mode; she **does not produce affect output at all,** which is its diagnostic feature. This is the mode after the twins' first loss (Byrne, West Coast Avengers) under Harkness's suppression; it is also the mode in the days after Vision's dismantling.

This mode is **dangerous in proportion to its quietness.** The pressure does not dissipate; it accumulates. Handlers who see Mode A and infer recovery are reading the chart upside down.

**Mode B — Decompensated grief.** The pressure escapes. Affect floods. Magic uncouples from intent. This is Disassembled; this is the moment before House of M; this is recurrent in miniature throughout her record after any sufficient trigger. Phenomenology: she speaks in fragments, often about the lost object as if present; reality around her becomes plastic (lights, weather, the structural integrity of nearby objects); she may not be able to identify her location or the current date. Mode B episodes have a typical duration of hours to a few days; the longer the prior Mode A containment, the longer and more destructive the Mode B release.

**Transitional tells (Mode A → Mode B).** This is the most operationally critical observation in the entire atlas. The transition is signaled by a small cluster: (1) **she begins to speak about the lost object in the present tense**; (2) **the red saturates** in her dress and ambient discharges; (3) she stops eating and stops sleeping in a 48-hour window; (4) she seeks out **objects associated with the loss** (the Vision's components, the twins' belongings, photographs); (5) **the rehearsal monitor fails** — she begins to say what she actually thinks. Any three of these in a 24-hour window warrants intervention by a trusted intimate, ideally one of the twins, ideally with Strange or Harkness on call.

**Anniversary effects.** Documented across the record. She is degraded around dates associated with the lost children and around the date corresponding to the Vision's destruction. The degradation is subtle — irritability, withdrawal, sleep disturbance — and recurs.

---

## VII. IN VICTORY

Victory is, paradoxically, a destabilizing state for her. She does not know how to occupy the winner's role.

**Somatic.** Stillness. While others celebrate she will stand to one side, often near a wall or a doorway, hands clasped. A small, closed-mouth smile that does not reach the eyes. She accepts congratulations with a nod and a quiet thanks; she does not narrate her contribution.

**Verbal.** **Credits others.** Reliably. Across decades and across teams she will, in after-action discussion, name the contributions of every other party before her own, and often omit her own entirely. This is not modesty performance; it is a real cognitive feature — she does not encode her own decisive actions as decisive.

**Decisional.** In victory she becomes more reparative, not more confident. She will use the post-victory window to attend to whatever damage was done — the wounded, the displaced, the property destroyed. The Orlando shop is built into this rhythm; victory creates the calm in which she serves.

**Risk window.** A subtle one: after sustained victory she becomes mildly **expansive**, and the expansiveness can drift toward magical experimentation she would not undertake at baseline. The Robinson run records small instances. The risk is not dramatic but is real — confidence is the affective key that unlocks workings she normally keeps shelved.

---

## VIII. IN DEFEAT

Defeat is the state for which she is most thoroughly trained, by life.

**Somatic.** Visible decrease in physical occupancy of space — the small-frame posture deepens, head drops, hair falls forward. She accepts handcuffs, restraints, magical bindings without resistance. She will go willingly into custody. In multiple recorded events (post-Disassembled, post-Decimation, after Trial of Magneto) she **offers herself for consequence** before it is demanded.

**Verbal.** Direct. Defeat is the one condition under which she speaks plainly and completely about her own actions. The qualifiers drop. She will name what she did and what it cost. This is rare and clinically significant: she is **most truthful at her lowest**, which inverts the typical pattern of subjects who confess least when most threatened.

**Decisional.** She defers to the judgments of others — the Avengers, the X-Men, the courts of magic. She will accept disproportionate punishment. She must be **prevented** from over-accepting consequence; left unsupervised, she will agree to exile, depowering, or self-isolation that exceeds the actual moral debt and that, over time, deepens the pathology.

**Recovery trajectory from defeat.** Slow, asymmetric. She does not bounce; she **rebuilds, brick by brick, through service.** The reparative campaigns of the post-M and post-Krakoa periods are the visible architecture of this recovery pattern. The intermediate state — between active reparation and renewed personhood — is the state in which she is most exploitable by caretaker-coded handlers (Magneto's recurrent re-approaches; Doom's House of M maneuver), because in defeat she is most receptive to anyone offering her a useful role.

---

## IX. CROSS-STATE HABITS AND RITUALS

A residue of repeated behaviors that recur across all states and serve as **identity anchors** in a life of identity disruption.

**The tea.** Hot water with herbs of European, often Eastern European, provenance. Prepared by hand, never by machine. The ritual is more important than the consumption.

**The walk.** Late-evening solitary walks, route-variable but always **looping back to the place of origin** rather than reaching a destination. The loop is the function.

**The arrangement of small objects.** Candles, cards, stones, photographs. She maintains small altars — never named as such — on bedside tables, kitchen counters, windowsills. The objects rotate; the practice does not.

**The hand-check.** Before sleeping, before any working of consequence, before any conversation she expects to be difficult: she will hold her hands up before her face, palms toward her, and look at them. This is a **calibration**, conscious in some eras (Robinson's run shows her describing it), unconscious in others. It is among her oldest behaviors in the record.

**The naming.** Under stress she will silently name the people she loves. Lip-readers in surveillance contexts will recover, repeatedly: *Billy. Tommy. Pietro. Vision.* The list is short, fixed, and ordered.

**The apology.** She apologizes constantly and reflexively, for small things. The apologies are not performative; they are a continuous low-grade restitution behavior, the background hum of a conscience that has been over-loud since 2005.

---

## X. SUMMARY OBSERVATIONS FOR HANDLERS AND OBSERVERS

Wanda Maximoff is, behaviorally, a study in **the mismatch between containment and capacity.** Every habit catalogued above is, at root, an attempt by a chronically grief-injured person to keep herself smaller than her power. The tells of escalation are reliable and well-documented; the windows for intervention are narrow but real. The intimate-state behaviors are the truest read of who she is; the threat-state behaviors are the most operationally legible; the grief-state Mode-A presentation is the most consistently misread.

The atlas's single most important entry, if only one is to be retained: **watch the hands, watch the red, listen for the present tense.** When all three indicate escalation, the available window is hours, not days, and the appropriate first responder is not a tactical asset but a person she loves.

— *End Behavioral Atlas. Continue to Volume IV: Network and Affiliation Map.*


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS — SUBJECT: WANDA MAXIMOFF

*What a week of continuous surveillance would actually record. Granular reconstruction from canonical behavior across the Robinson solo run (2015-17), the Orlando solo (2023-24), Krakoa-era residence patterns, and inferred from forty years of consistent micro-tells.*

---

## 1. The Architecture of a Day

Subject does not live on a clock. She lives on a **rhythm of arrivals and departures** — her own and other people's. The constant across every era is that her day is shaped less by appointments than by *thresholds*: doors opened, doors closed, people received, people seen out. The Orlando-era arrangement — a literal door that opens anywhere in the world for anyone who needs her — is not an aesthetic choice. It is the externalization of how she has always organized time: in interruptible service blocks, with the interruption *being* the point.

**Wake.** Early but not punitive. Surveillance would record her awake before sunrise in roughly 70% of observed days — not from discipline but from poor and shallow sleep (see §6). She does not use an alarm. She does not roll over and check a phone; she rarely keeps one on her nightstand. The first observable action is almost always the same: she sits up on the edge of the bed for between forty seconds and two minutes before standing. Eyes open, hands flat on the mattress beside her thighs, head slightly bowed. To a watcher this looks like prayer or meditation. It is neither. It is the daily, unconscious **inventory**: is the world still the world I went to sleep in. A tell that survives across decades and across every domicile.

**First hour.** Water before anything else — a full glass, slowly, standing at the kitchen window or its equivalent. She does not eat in the first hour. She washes her face with cold water; she does not shower immediately. She lights something — a candle, a stick of incense, the gas under a kettle. The lighting of a small controlled flame is ritualized and near-universal. Hand to the wick or burner, a pause that lasts a half-beat too long, then she moves on. A surveillance team would log this as "flame ritual, ~6-12 sec, daily, all locations." It reads as superstition or witchcraft. It is closer to a control-check: a deliberate small act of magic-adjacent will to confirm that the will is hers and that small things still respond to small intentions.

**Morning work block.** Whatever the era — Avengers tower, the Robinson-era apartment in New York, the cottage in upstate (Orlando run), Krakoan accommodations, the door-shop — the morning is reserved for things that do not require other people. Reading. Letter-writing (yes, by hand; she is consistent about this from the 1980s through the present — see §3). Tending to plants, of which there are always too many. Cooking something low and slow for later. Mending. She is in a recognizable category of person who *makes the day useful before the day asks anything of her,* because that morning of useful private work is the only part of the day she is sure she will get.

**Midday and afternoon.** Open. Service-shaped. This is when the door opens, when clients arrive, when the team calls, when a sister-witch needs a consultation, when one of the twins texts (yes — she does keep a phone for them, see §5). The afternoon is *given.* She does not protect it. A surveillance log of a typical Orlando-era week would show three to seven unscheduled human contacts per day in this window, most lasting between twenty minutes and two hours, most ending with her walking the visitor to the threshold and standing in the doorway until they are out of sight.

**Evening.** Quiet, slow, and protected — the one block she does defend. Cooking for herself or for one to three guests. Wine, sometimes — a single glass, rarely two, never more (see §6 on substance patterns). Music low. Reading. If the twins are in town, dinner runs long. If not, the evening collapses earlier than an outside observer would predict; she goes to bed not when she is tired but when the silence in the apartment becomes louder than she can tolerate.

**Late night.** Insomnia is the rule, not the exception. A watcher would log lights on between 02:00 and 04:00 in something like 40-60% of nights. She does not call anyone. She does not eat. She reads, or she sits by a window, or she walks the perimeter of the residence in stocking feet. The pacing is silent and slow and ends, always, in the same room: whatever room the children's photographs (or the small altar described in §4) live in.

---

## 2. Habits of Place

She does not live large. Across every period of independence — between Avengers tenancies, after House of M, in the Robinson solo, in the Orlando run — her residences share a stable signature:

- **Small.** One to three rooms used. Even when she has access to more, she occupies less.
- **Warm-lit.** Lamps, not overheads. Surveillance would record her actively turning *off* overhead lights upon entering a room and turning *on* the table lamps. Consistent across decades.
- **Textile-heavy.** Throws, rugs, hangings, shawls draped over chair backs. The visual reads as bohemian or "witchy"; the functional truth is sensory: she damps hard sound and hard light at every opportunity.
- **Plants.** Many. Disproportionately herbs and night-bloomers. She talks to them — not theatrically, just under her breath, in passing. A boom-mic operator would catch fragments: "all right, all right," "more sun for you, then," sometimes a phrase in Romani or in Sokovian-cadenced English that does not parse to either.
- **Kitchen as command center.** Not the desk, not the living room. If you want to know where she actually spends time, watch the kitchen. The kettle is on or recently on for most waking hours.
- **At least one window she returns to.** Every residence has a "watching window" — she gravitates to it unconsciously, several times a day, stands and looks out for between thirty seconds and several minutes. Hands often crossed at the wrists in front of her, or one elbow cupped in the opposite palm. This is a self-soothing posture (see §7).
- **The threshold is dressed.** Salt, ash, an herb bundle, a sigil under the mat — something. Always. Not ostentatious. She does not advertise it. But the door is *prepared.* Anyone reading the residence as a magical practitioner's would see it immediately; anyone else would miss it entirely.

**She does not decorate with photographs of herself.** There are no images of her on her own walls — not Avengers press shots, not wedding portraits, nothing.
