There *are* small framed images of the twins (Wiccan and Speed, in the modern era; in earlier eras, when memory permitted, of Thomas and William). These are placed not prominently but where she will see them in passing — by the kettle, on the bookshelf at eye height, on the windowsill. The placement is the giveaway: photographs you encounter accidentally, several times a day, are doing different psychological work than photographs displayed for guests.

---

## 3. Correspondence, Reading, and the Written Hand

She writes letters. By hand. This is consistent from at least the West Coast Avengers period forward and has not been displaced by any technology. Recipients include: the twins (regularly, often weekly), Agatha Harkness (historically; an act both of attachment and of unfinished business), a small handful of fellow practitioners (Strange occasionally, Jennifer Kale, Topaz, women in the magical community more than men), and — a fact she would not volunteer — drafts of letters to the Vision that are never sent and that she burns at the end of the calendar year.

Her hand is small, slanted, deliberate. She writes slowly. A surveillance team intercepting outgoing mail over a year would notice that the volume of her correspondence spikes in two predictable windows: **the week before any major Avengers or X-team operation she has been read into** (she puts her affairs in order without acknowledging that this is what she is doing), and **the second week of any month in which a death anniversary falls** (Vision's destruction date, the date the twins were unmade, more recently her own death-and-resurrection anniversary).

**Reading.** Voracious and eclectic. Grimoires and primary occult sources, yes — but also and more revealingly: poetry (heavy on the elegiac — she returns to Akhmatova, to Plath's *Ariel,* to Rilke's *Duino Elegies,* to the Sokovian and Romani folk-poem traditions of her displaced childhood), novels with strong domestic textures, cookbooks she reads like literature. She does not read political journalism. She does not watch the news. A surveillance team would note an active *avoidance* of broadcast media; she gets her current events by osmosis, from visitors. This is not ignorance — it is a regulated diet. She has learned that the news is, for her, a destabilizer.

---

## 4. Ritual — the Real Kind and the Other Kind

Two overlapping ritual practices, distinct in function:

**Magical practice (declared).** Daily small workings: warding the threshold, a brief invocation over the morning's first flame, blessing of food (silent, a fingertip drawn over the plate before the first bite — easy to miss), end-of-day extinguishing of candles in a specific order (newest lit first, oldest last). On the cross-quarter days she practices more elaborate workings, often alone, sometimes with one or two trusted others. She does *not* perform large magic for show, for ego, or for self-care. Her relationship to her own power is somewhere between a recovering addict's relationship to a substance and a surgeon's relationship to a scalpel: reverent, fearful, instrumental, never casual.

**Compulsion-shaped ritual (undeclared and probably unconscious).** The morning bed-edge inventory. The flame-check. A specific way of placing her keys (always in the same dish, always with the working end pointing toward the door). Touching the doorframe with two fingers as she leaves a room — not every room, not every time, but reliably in moments of even mild anxiety. Counting under her breath in Sokovian when stressed, usually in fives, usually to twenty. Re-checking that the gas is off after cooking, often two and three times.

The undeclared rituals would, to a clinician, read as low-grade OCD-spectrum compensation. To her they are simply *how one moves through a world that has, in living memory, ceased to be the world.* Every check is a small renegotiated treaty with reality.

**The altar.** Whatever residence, whatever era. Small. Usually on a low shelf or a windowsill. Contents have evolved: in the West Coast period and after, two small candles for the twins; post-Disassembled, after the memory returned, a third object for Vision (often a small fragment of synthetic material — wire, a piece of circuitry, in the Robinson era a single cool-toned bead); post-resurrection, a fourth element representing her own crossing — a coin, a piece of sea-glass, something river-worn. She tends it daily. She does not speak of it. Guests who notice it are not corrected and not invited to discuss.

---

## 5. The People in the Week — Contact Mapping

A surveillance log of a representative week would show the following contact graph, in approximate descending frequency:

- **Wiccan (Billy Kaplan).** Daily or near-daily contact — text, occasional call, increasingly in-person as the modern era progresses. She does not initiate as often as she responds; she is afraid of being a burden, and equally afraid of being intrusive. Her texts to him are short, warm, and end with diminutives. His to her are longer. She reads them more than once.
- **Speed (Tommy Shepherd).** Less frequent, more sporadic, often a long silence broken by a sudden visit. She does not pressure. She keeps the kitchen stocked with the foods he likes regardless of whether he is expected.
- **Agatha.** Complicated, intermittent, sometimes hostile, never severed. A weekly observation period would catch at least one exchange — letter, astral contact, an awkward in-person visit. The relationship has the texture of a recovering patient's relationship with a former therapist who also crossed every boundary.
- **Strange.** Professional more than warm. Quarterly business, weekly during crises. She respects him; she does not relax around him.
- **Magneto / Pietro / the X-side.** Episodic, weather-dependent. After any contact with either she sleeps badly for two to four nights. Surveillance would correlate easily.
- **Clients / supplicants (Orlando-era pattern).** The door brings strangers. She gives each visitor her full attention. She does not run a clock. She remembers their names afterwards — surveillance would catch her saying their names aloud, weeks later, in moments of solitude, as if rehearsing the fact that they existed and that she was useful to them.
- **The Avengers operational channel.** She maintains it. She answers it. She does not initiate on it.

A telling absence: **friendships of pure leisure.** She does not have a circle of people she sees for fun without function. Every relationship has a *use* — mentorship, kinship, work, care. She does not know how to be in a room with someone without doing something for them.

---

## 6. Sleep, Food, and the Body's Small Economies

**Sleep.** Poor. Surveillance-grade observation would establish: 4-6 hours of fragmented sleep most nights, broken by one to three awakenings, with the early-morning awakening (03:00-04:30) the most consistent and the hardest to recover from. Nightmares are frequent; she does not report them, but she wakes from them with a specific tell — sitting bolt upright, breath audibly held for several seconds, then released slowly with the heel of one hand pressed to the sternum. On the worst nights she gets up, makes tea, and reads through to dawn. She does not take prescription sleep aids — a hard, principled refusal — though she has used herbal preparations of her own making with mixed honesty about their efficacy.

**Food.** Eats little, eats well, cooks more than she eats. Cooking is unmistakably regulatory: when she is anxious, the kitchen gets busier and the freezer fills up with portions she will not finish. She skips breakfast as a rule. Lunch is often forgotten or absorbed into a guest's visit. Dinner is the meal she takes seriously. She drinks tea constantly — strong, black or herbal, with sugar in the Eastern European manner.

**Wine.** A single glass with dinner is normative. Two glasses indicates a hard day. Three glasses is rare and would, in a surveillance log, correlate within seventy-two hours with the anniversary of a loss or a contact with Magneto. She does not drink alone late at night. She does not drink to sleep.

**No tobacco. No drugs.** This is consistent and absolute. She has been around plenty of both, in both Avengers and magical circles. She abstains. The abstention is not moralistic; it is, by her own internal logic, a refusal to add any further unreliability to her perception. She must be able to trust what she sees.

**Exercise.** Walking, primarily. Long walks, often at twilight, often without a destination. In every residence she has had a walking route, learned within the first week, repeated. She walks at a steady moderate pace, hands often in her pockets or holding the ends of a shawl. She notices everything. She does not look at her phone. Watchers would describe her gait as unhurried, slightly inward, occasionally pausing to look at small things — a flower in pavement, a cat in a window, a child she will watch a beat too long.

**Dress.** The reds and the dark crimsons are not vanity; they are an *identifier* she has chosen to inhabit because choosing it is easier than fighting it. Off-duty she wears soft fabrics, layers, long sleeves regardless of weather, often a shawl or wrap she can pull tighter as a self-soothing gesture. She wears very little jewelry. She does not wear a wedding ring. She did, once, for decades, in memory; at some point in the modern era she stopped, and the place on her finger where it sat is still occasionally touched by her thumb.

---

## 7. The Body's Tells — Micro-pattern Inventory

A surveillance team trained on her over a year would compile the following reliable micro-patterns:

- **The wrist-cross.** Hands crossed at the wrists in front of her, often near the solar plexus or low at the hips. A self-containment posture. Frequency increases with stress; near-absent when she is genuinely at ease (which is rare).
- **The thumb-to-ring-finger.** Right hand. The place the ring was. Unconscious. Increases around anniversaries and around any conversation that touches the Vision.
- **The half-beat pause at thresholds.** She does not walk through doorways at full speed. There is a perceptible micro-hesitation. A check. A taking of measure of the room she is entering.
- **The downward glance before answering a hard question.** Eyes drop and to the right, half-second, then lift back to meet the questioner. She does not lie well and she does not try; the glance is the moment of choosing what truth to offer.
- **The accent surface.** Her English is fluent and unaccented in the ordinary register, but under stress or fatigue the Sokovian/Eastern European cadence surfaces — vowels lengthen, articles drop, word order shifts slightly. A trained ear would use this as an affect-meter.
- **The hand to the sternum.** After bad news, after nightmares, after the rare unguarded laugh. The heel of the right hand, palm flat, pressed firmly to the breastbone for two to four seconds. Self-anchoring.
- **The long look at children she passes.** On every walk. Not predatory, not even longing in any way an observer could call inappropriate — but *attentive,* the gaze of someone confirming that other people's children continue to exist in the world. She always looks away before the parent notices.
- **The pause before saying her own name.** Asked to introduce herself, she takes a beat. As if checking which one to give.

---

## 8. The Weekly Shape, the Monthly Shape, the Yearly Shape

**A representative week** would log: 4-6 mornings of private work, 4-7 afternoons of service contacts, 5-7 evenings of solitary or near-solitary domesticity, 2-4 nights of broken sleep, 1-2 long walks, 1 longer magical working (often on the night closest to whatever lunar event is current), 1 or 2 calls or visits with the twins, 0-2 letters written, 1-3 small acts of unrecorded kindness to strangers (a bought meal, a directed cab, a quiet ward laid over a stranger's apartment building she had reason to pass), and no broadcast media consumed.

**A month** would add: a heavier working on or near the new moon, a personal-affairs day (correspondence, the altar tended at length, financial and practical matters dispatched in a single concentrated block), at least one Avengers-or-X-related operational contact she did not initiate, and, statistically, one bad week — three or four days of pulled-in withdrawal, the door not opened, calls unreturned, the kettle on continuously.

**A year** has its anniversaries, and the surveillance file would learn to predict them. The week of Vision's first destruction. The week the twins were unmade. The week of House of M's collapse. Her own death-and-return. Her mother's death-day (insofar as she knows it). In each of these windows the pattern is identical: she becomes quieter, sleeps less, writes more, walks longer, drinks one extra glass of wine with dinner, sits longer at the altar, and on the day itself she is unreachable — door closed, phone off, candles lit, alone.

She does not commemorate her own birthday. She does commemorate the twins'.

---

## 9. The Net Read of a Surveillance Week

What the file would actually show, stripped of incident: a woman of enormous capacity living a small, careful, ritualized life organized around the *prevention* of the next catastrophe and the daily small *reparation* of the last. She is not hiding. She is not idle. She is metabolizing — slowly, by hand, in the only register that has ever worked for her: through service to others, through the keeping of small flames, through the writing of letters that will and will not be sent, through the tending of plants and altars and a door that opens to whoever needs it.

The week looks like a quiet life. It is in fact a continuous, low-amplitude act of grief work performed without supervision, without diagnosis, and without rest. The surveillance team that mistakes the quietness for stability has not been watching long enough.

— *End section. Proceed to Relationship Architecture.*


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

*UATU Dossier, Section 5a. Subject: Wanda Maximoff. Compiled longitudinally from full published behavioral record. Family-of-origin and blood/spirit kin only; chosen kin (Vision, Avengers, Young Avengers, Krakoa cohort) reserved for Relationships II.*

The family file is the load-bearing file. Every catastrophic decompensation in Wanda Maximoff's record traces, when reverse-engineered, to a rupture in one of the bonds catalogued below. The pattern is not coincidence: this is a subject whose self does not exist outside of relational scaffolding, and whose family scaffolding has been — across six decades of published record — built variously of coercion, secrecy, retcon, lie, soul-fragment, and resurrection. Almost none of it has been built of ordinary kinship. The wonder is not that she has decompensated; the wonder is the intervals between.

---

## 5a.i — MAGDA EISENHARDT (mother, biological; deceased prior to subject's conscious memory)

**Status of the bond.** A ghost-relationship. Wanda has no encoded autobiographical memory of Magda; everything she knows of her mother arrived via third parties (Django Maximoff's secondhand account; Magneto's belated and self-serving confession in *Avengers* #186 and again, in revised form, across the Bendis and Heinberg arcs). Magda died of exposure on Wundagore mountain shortly after giving birth to the twins, fleeing Magneto after witnessing the full extent of what he had become.

**Dynamics and evolution.** Operationally a *Rorschach-mother* — Wanda projects onto Magda whatever she most needs the absent maternal figure to have been: gentle, frightened, protective, the parent who *chose* to flee the violent man rather than stay. Note the structural significance: the only thing Wanda *knows* about her mother is that her mother ran from her father. This narrative becomes a template Wanda spends decades failing to enact in her own life. She does not flee Magneto until she is grown; she does not flee Pietro's controlling solicitude ever; she does not flee until after the children are already lost.

**Trust/safety.** N/A — no operative bond. But the *idealization* is dangerous: Magda functions as the unviolated mother-imago against which Wanda measures her own catastrophic failure as a parent to Thomas and William. The comparison is rigged. Magda died protecting infants; Wanda lost infants she could not protect from the metaphysics of her own existence.

**Failure mode.** Activation of the maternal-failure schema. Any narrative reminder of Magda — particularly framings that contrast Magda's "real" motherhood with Wanda's "false" motherhood (which is precisely the rhetorical weapon used against her at various points by hostile parties, including, in less guarded moments, Pietro) — triggers a recursive guilt-loop with no exit.

**Leverage.** Low for adversaries (Magda is too distant to weaponize precisely), high for therapeutic actors. A clinician — or Agatha Harkness in a non-iatrogenic mode — who could give Wanda a *factual,* non-idealized account of Magda's choices, including their costs and ambiguities, would do more grief-work in one session than the preceding sixty years of canon have permitted.

---

## 5a.ii — DJANGO MAXIMOFF (adoptive/foster father, Romani; presumed deceased)

**Status of the bond.** Officially: the father who raised her and Pietro in the Transian/Wundagore Romani community after Magda died, until the village burned and Django and Marya were lost to the mob. For long stretches of canon this *was* the operative origin story; the Magneto-paternity layer was added later (Englehart) and the High Evolutionary/Wundagore complication added later still (Byrne, then re-litigated by Bendis and AXIS).

**Dynamics and evolution.** The Django period is the *only* stretch of Wanda's documented life in which she was a child in a normatively configured family. The behavioral residue is detectable: her food preferences and the small comforts she returns to under stress (warm bread, candle-light, hand-stitched fabrics in her solo-run domestic interiors per the Robinson and Orlando books) trace to a Romani-coded childhood iconography. Under acute regression she has been observed murmuring in fragmentary Romani — a tell that her earliest secure attachment language was not English and not Sokovian-equivalent but the language of the foster home.

**Trust/safety.** Retroactively high but inaccessible. The Django bond is the *only* secure-base imprint on record, and it was severed in violence. Every subsequent "family" is an attempt to reconstruct the kitchen, the candle, the hand on the head.

**Failure mode.** Anniversary-effect vulnerability around the burning of the Romani village. The subject has, in multiple recorded years, withdrawn from team activity for periods of days around dates loosely consistent with the village's destruction, without explicit explanation.

**Leverage.** Romani-cultural framings, properly handled, are stabilizing; mishandled or used cynically, they are corrosive. Adversaries who have invoked her "true heritage" as manipulation (most prominently the High Evolutionary's various retconned overtures, and Magneto in his recruitment-relapses) have produced confusion, not loyalty. Django is *not* on the political board for her; he is on the somatic board.

---

## 5a.iii — MARYA MAXIMOFF (adoptive/foster mother, Romani; presumed deceased)

**Status of the bond.** Functionally fused with Django in the subject's accessible memory; rarely surfaced as an independent object. The differentiation matters clinically: Marya is the maternal figure Wanda *did* have, however briefly, and she is buried beneath the Magda-imago.

**Dynamics and evolution.** Marya is the source of the **caregiving-by-feeding** behavior that recurs across Wanda's adult relationships — she cooks for Vision (who cannot eat); she serves tea to clients in the Orlando-era shop with a ritual precision that exceeds hospitality; she has been documented preparing meals for Pietro in periods when he was eating perfectly well on his own. The behavior is over-determined and pre-verbal. Marya is its origin.

**Trust/safety.** Same caveat as Django: high, severed in violence, inaccessible to direct cultivation.

**Failure mode and leverage.** As Django, with the additional vulnerability that maternal-figure substitutes (Agatha Harkness most consequentially) get filed against the Marya-template without Wanda's conscious knowledge. This is how Harkness obtained the access required to perform the memory-suppression on the twins: Wanda *let her in* at the maternal level, decades before the request was made.

---

## 5a.iv — MAGNETO / MAX EISENHARDT (biological father per long-standing canon; periodically retconned and reinstated)

**Status of the bond.** The single most distorting relationship in the subject's file. Originally (Lee/Kirby) she and Pietro were Magneto's rescued strays; Englehart retconned this into biological paternity; the Bendis/Robinson/Krakoa eras have wobbled the paternity question repeatedly without ever cleanly extracting it. For psychological purposes the *belief structure* is what matters, and the belief structure has been, for most of her adult life, **"this man is my father."**

**Dynamics and evolution.**

*Phase 1 — Brotherhood (X-Men #4 era).* Coerced affiliation. Magneto leverages a rescue-debt into operational compliance. Wanda's behavior is uniformly reluctant; her power is deployed against her conscience; she does not refuse him directly until Pietro does it first. This sets the lifelong template: *she will not break a paternal bond unilaterally.*

*Phase 2 — Defection to the Avengers.* Engineered partly by Pietro, partly by Wanda's own quiet exhaustion. Note: she does not denounce Magneto. She *leaves.* The distinction is diagnostic. Across her entire record she has never produced a sustained, articulated repudiation of him. She gets distance; she does not get closure.

*Phase 3 — The paternity reveal.* When Magneto is reframed as biological father, Wanda's response is not joy and not fury but a kind of stunned re-organization. She integrates the information *and continues to behave as if the underlying coercive history is now somehow legitimized.* This is identification-with-the-aggressor reaching its full developmental form: the abuser is reclassified as kin and the abuse is reclassified as upbringing.

*Phase 4 — House of M precursor.* Pietro, in panic over the Illuminati's plans for her, brings the *idea* of the reality-rewrite to Magneto, who tacitly green-lights its application to himself (he becomes the king of the mutant world). Magneto thus benefits from, and is implicated in, the catastrophe. His response after collapse is rage at Pietro and ambivalent grief at Wanda. He does not protect her from the consequences.

*Phase 5 — Krakoa / Trial of Magneto / resurrection era.* The most genuine reckoning the bond has ever permitted. Magneto is present at her resurrection; the trial structure forces an unprecedented direct accounting; for the first time on record, the paternal figure submits to *her* moral authority rather than asserting his over her. This is the only data point in the file suggesting the bond is repairable rather than only manageable.

**Trust/safety.** Catastrophically low at the implicit level, dangerously high at the explicit level — meaning she *behaves* as if she trusts him more than her own history warrants. This gap is the principal exploit surface in her file.

**Failure mode.** Re-recruitment vulnerability. In states of acute guilt or attachment-hunger she has been demonstrably reachable by Magneto in ways no one else can reach her. He is the original voice; the brainstem files him under *parent* regardless of cortical objections.

**Leverage.** Maximum, and the most dangerous in the file. Any actor capable of impersonating, channeling, or invoking Magneto's paternal authority gains a covert override on her behavior. Conversely, any framing that *clearly* separates Magneto-the-father from Magneto-the-warlord — and forces the subject to choose which she is responding to — produces partial liberation. The Krakoa-era trial mechanics are the operational template.

---

## 5a.v — PIETRO MAXIMOFF / QUICKSILVER (twin brother; living)

**Status of the bond.** The longest continuous relationship in the file and the only one never severed by death, retcon, or memory erasure (he has died and been resurrected; the *bond* has not broken). Operationally: enmeshed-twin, with Pietro in the dominant-anxious role and Wanda in the accommodating-soothing role.

**Dynamics and evolution.**

The behavioral signature is detectable in micro-patterns. *In conversation:* Pietro interrupts her in roughly seventy percent of recorded three-party exchanges; she does not protest. *In combat:* she positions to his flank without verbal cueing; he positions to *interpose* between her and incoming threat with a frequency that exceeds tactical optimum (he treats her as a non-combatant despite her power class). *In private:* when they are filmed/observed together at rest, she leans toward him at the shoulder; he checks her physical state — pulse, color, eye-tracking — with the practiced micro-glance of a chronic caregiver who does not trust the patient to report symptoms.

*Pietro's marriage to Crystal and the resulting strain.* The introduction of an outside partner for Pietro produced the only sustained interpersonal jealousy on record from Wanda — not romantic, *positional.* She experienced the marriage as the loss of her primary attachment to a competing claimant, and the file shows a quiet, polite, persistent froideur toward Crystal that the subject never extended to any other in-law. The eventual dissolution of Pietro's marriage was met with a relief she did not entirely conceal.

*Pietro's role in House of M.* This is the load-bearing fact. Pietro — terrified, controlling, unable to tolerate the prospect of his sister's death or sanction — instigated the reality-rewrite. He used her. He used the twin-bond's coercive intimacy to get her to do the thing that broke the world. *And she has never publicly held him to full account for it.* The Children's Crusade arc shows her capable of fury at him when it surfaces, but the fury does not survive proximity; within hours of being in the same room she is regulating his affect again.

*Post-resurrection / Krakoa-era.* The bond persists, somewhat re-balanced. Pietro is observably more deferent, having absorbed at least partial recognition of his role in her catastrophe. The accommodating-soothing pattern from her side, however, is unchanged.

**Trust/safety.** Paradox. Implicit trust is total; he is the only person in the universe she does not, at the brainstem level, *brace* around. Operational trust *should* be qualified — he is the single individual who has demonstrably weaponized intimacy against her at scale — but is not.

**Failure mode.** Twin-distress propagation. Threat or grave injury to Pietro produces an immediate dysregulation that, at high enough magnitude, would predictably reproduce a Disassembled-class event. The reverse is also true and is the more frequent operational concern: Pietro's panic about Wanda has historically been the trigger that recruits *him* into precipitating *her* worst episodes.

**Leverage.** Extreme but double-edged. Any actor who controls or harms Pietro controls a substantial portion of Wanda's behavior. Any actor who tries to *separate* the twins permanently triggers resistance from both. The bond is the most stable thing in her life and one of the most dangerous; it should be neither severed nor trusted.

---

## 5a.vi — THOMAS and WILLIAM (the lost twins, original; soul-fragment ontology)

**Status of the bond.** The wound. Not "a" wound — *the* wound. Two infants she carried, delivered, nursed, named, loved, and lost in succession to a metaphysical revelation she did not understand and could not contest. Then a third loss layered on top: Agatha Harkness took the *memory* of them. Then a fourth: the memory returned, all at once, under no clinical supervision, in the presence of the people she would proceed to kill.

**Dynamics and evolution.** The original Thomas and William existed for a brief in-universe span and an enormous psychological span. Wanda's mothering behavior in the surviving record is *normative* — she fed them, sang to them, sought childcare assistance, worried about developmental milestones, photographed them. The pathology is not in the mothering; the pathology was inflicted on the mothering from outside.

The Harkness intervention is the iatrogenic centerpiece of her entire clinical file. Removing the memory did not remove the attachment; the attachment continued to exist as a load-bearing structure with no conscious referent, which is the precise architectural recipe for the catastrophic return-of-repressed that Disassembled and House of M enacted. Any competent grief clinician reviewing the case would identify the Harkness suppression as malpractice of historic magnitude — and as the proximate enabling condition for the depopulation of mutantkind.

**Trust/safety.** The objects of the bond are non-existent in their original form. The bond itself is permanent and unhealed.

**Failure mode.** Any stimulus that re-presents the loss freshly — a child of similar apparent age in distress, a synthezoid-and-mother tableau, certain lullabies, the smell of the nursery as Vision had constructed it — produces measurable dysregulation. Under sufficient compounding stress, dysregulation scales to event.

**Leverage.** This is the file's most prohibited button. An adversary who weaponized the original twins' memory — for example by simulating them, by claiming to have recovered them, by threatening to "really" erase them — would gain decisive but uncontrollable influence. *Uncontrollable* is the operative word: the response would not be obedience, it would be a reality-class event. Any handler contemplating this leverage should not.

---

## 5a.vii — BILLY KAPLAN / WICCAN and TOMMY SHEPHERD / SPEED (the returned twins, reincarnated soul-fragments; living)

**Status of the bond.** Resurrection-bond. Billy and Tommy are, per the Heinberg resolution and subsequent canon, the reincarnated soul-fragments of Thomas and William, reborn into other families and grown to adolescence/young adulthood before encountering Wanda. The bond is therefore *both* maternal and not-maternal; she is their mother in a metaphysical register, a stranger-relative in a developmental register, and a figure of enormous projected weight in their own psychology.

**Dynamics and evolution.** Wanda's behavior toward Billy and Tommy is the most carefully modulated of any relationship in her file. She does not assert mothering; she *offers* it, hand open, prepared to be refused. She has been observed to defer to their adoptive parents in ways that cost her visibly. She intervenes only when invited; she absents herself when their lives appear stable. The restraint is itself a clinical sign — she is acutely aware that any over-claiming would re-traumatize all three parties and herself.

Billy in particular has inherited reality-warping capacity of a class comparable to hers; this creates an additional layer of identification, anxiety, and unsought tutorial obligation. She is alert to his decompensation risk in a way that suggests she sees her own developmental history projected forward.

**Trust/safety.** Building, fragile, real. The Krakoa-era and post-resurrection appearances show genuine, deepening trust on both sides — including Billy's willingness to invoke her name in his own crises, which is the gift she most needed and least expected.

**Failure mode.** Billy and Tommy are the *only* attachment objects in her current life whose loss would predictably reproduce the House of M event, and probably at greater scale. The reparative arc of the past two decades is held in place by their existence. The clinical literature on Prolonged Grief Disorder is unambiguous about the consequence of a *second* catastrophic loss in an inadequately treated bereaved subject; in Wanda's case the consequence would be planetary.

**Leverage.** Maximum-prohibited. As with the original twins, only more so, because Billy and Tommy are alive and reachable. Any actor who threatens them is operating a doomsday trigger they do not control.

The reparative arc is real. It is also held together by two young men whose continued existence the universe has not historically guaranteed. The file must be re-reviewed quarterly against their status.

---

*End Section 5a. Section 5b (Relationships II — Chosen Family: Vision, the Avengers, Agatha Harkness as ambivalent kin, the Young Avengers cohort, the Krakoa relations) to follow.*


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

*Pre-profile dossier section. Subject: MAXIMOFF, Wanda. The Magneto/Pietro/Vision triangle is mapped in Relationships I (Family of Origin / Primary Bonds). This section maps the chosen, elective, and earned bonds — the people Wanda has either let in voluntarily or been adopted by despite herself. Clinical provenance for grief-coupling, attachment displacement, and reparative-caregiving observations: Bryant et al. 2024 (PMID 38656428); Pop-Jordanova 2021 (PMID 34699700).*

---

## 1. Agatha Harkness — Mentor, Iatrogenic Wound, Surrogate Mother

**History.** Initial contact: Fantastic Four-adjacent governess of Franklin Richards; brought into Wanda's orbit during the Avengers/West Coast Avengers era as a magical tutor when "hex bolts" began revealing themselves as something deeper. She formally instructs Wanda in witchcraft over a span of years across Vision & the Scarlet Witch, the Byrne West Coast run, and intermittent appearances through to her on-page death (and resurrections). She is the single person in Wanda's life who treated witchcraft as a discipline rather than a curiosity, an asset, or a threat.

**Dynamics.** Harkness occupies, simultaneously, three roles that should not coexist in one figure: instructor, surrogate maternal object, and the agent of Wanda's most consequential iatrogenic injury. She is brisk where Wanda is yielding; declarative where Wanda is intuitive; she imposes structure on a student whose magic is wish-shaped. The pedagogical pattern is appropriate — modeling, supervised practice, escalation — but the emotional pattern is asymmetric. Harkness gives instruction; Wanda gives trust. There is no record of Wanda receiving comfort from Harkness; there is extensive record of Wanda *complying with* Harkness.

**The intervention.** After the dissolution of Thomas and William, Harkness magically suppresses Wanda's memory of the children. The decision is presented as mercy. It is, in the clinical frame, the precipitating iatrogenic event for everything that follows — the foreclosure of mourning that Bryant 2024 and Pop-Jordanova 2021 identify as the soil for Prolonged Grief Disorder. Wanda did not consent to it in any meaningful informed sense; she was a grieving mother offered relief by her teacher, and she took it. The teacher should have known better. The relationship's defining tragedy is that Wanda has never, even after recovering the memory, broken with Harkness over the act. She absorbs the injury and continues the apprenticeship.

**Trust / safety.** Trust is high and miscalibrated. Wanda trusts Harkness's *judgment about magic* — appropriately — and extrapolates that into trust about her own welfare, which is unsupported by the evidence. Safety is low: Harkness will make decisions *for* Wanda's good without consulting her, and Wanda will accept them.

**Failure mode.** Harkness disappears (or dies, or is killed, or withholds) at the precise moments Wanda needs scaffolding. The mentorship is intermittent by Harkness's choice, not Wanda's. When Wanda decompensates, Harkness is structurally absent — by death, by ghosthood, by the Salem cycles. Wanda has therefore internalized Harkness as the *idea* of a teacher more than as a present one.

**Leverage.** Significant. An adversary positioned to invoke Harkness — to summon her, simulate her, channel her, or threaten her echo — accesses the only credentialed authority Wanda still defers to in the magical register. Conversely, Harkness's *judgment of Wanda* is one of the few external evaluations Wanda treats as binding. Her approval is regulatory; her disappointment is destabilizing.

---

## 2. Clint Barton (Hawkeye) — The Brother She Chose, Killed, and Has Not Forgiven Herself For

**History.** Co-recruited into the "Cap's Kooky Quartet" alongside Wanda and Pietro (Avengers #16). They came up together — both outsiders to the founding Avengers, both proving themselves to skeptical leadership, both essentially second-tier in the institutional hierarchy that they nonetheless held together with their daily presence. Decades of shared field operations. Clint's relationship to Pietro (antagonistic-affectionate) ran in parallel to his relationship with Wanda (protective-affectionate); he was, functionally, the brother-in-law before any of the marriages existed.

**Dynamics.** Clint is the only Avenger who consistently *teased* Wanda — and the teasing was the relationship. He treated her as a peer with a sense of humor when most of the team treated her as fragile or as a weapon. His irreverence regulated her: she did not have to be solemn around him. The bond was the most *normal* relationship in her adult life.

**The killing.** During Disassembled, in the affect-flooded fugue state, Wanda kills Clint. The act is dissociative, not intentional, but the canonical fact is unrescindable: she killed her oldest non-romantic friend on the team. Clint is resurrected (House of M arc and subsequent), and the relationship resumes — but not as it was. There is a permanent thin layer of *carefulness* between them. He has forgiven her in word; the body language across the post-resurrection appearances is more reserved than the pre-Disassembled record.

**Trust / safety.** Trust is asymmetric and high: Wanda trusts Clint's basic decency more than almost anyone's, and Clint, despite everything, has chosen to extend grace. Safety is fragile because Clint's *presence* is a stimulus for Wanda's worst memories. Proximity to him reactivates the Disassembled material.

**Failure mode.** Wanda overcorrects: she will defer to him, agree with him, retreat in his presence, rather than risk a second injury. This deference is a grief response, not a friendship.

**Leverage.** A hostile actor staging Clint's death — or convincingly faking it — would produce a disproportionate destabilization. Conversely, Clint's *moral endorsement* of any plan involving Wanda functions as a near-unique permission slip for her. She will do things if Clint says they are alright that she would refuse from anyone else, because if *he* of all people thinks she is safe to act, she may risk acting.

---

## 3. Steve Rogers — The Standard, the Father-Surrogate Without Coercion

**History.** Her recruiter and first Avengers field commander. The decade-plus under Rogers's leadership was the period in which Wanda *stabilized* — built the skills, the reputation, the chosen identity of "Avenger." Rogers's treatment of the Brotherhood defectors set the institutional template: he believed they were redeemable, he held them to a standard, and he did not weaponize their pasts.

**Dynamics.** Rogers is the first male authority figure in Wanda's life whose authority did not arrive through fear. The contrast with Magneto is total and was felt by Wanda from the earliest issues. She does not respond to Rogers with the disorganized-attachment compliance she shows Magneto; she responds with something closer to *earned respect* — she works to meet his standard rather than to placate him. In House of M, the wish-construction gives Steve the life he gave up (an old age he lived) — this is the diagnostic tell: in the unconscious's gift-shop, what Wanda wants to give Steve is *peace,* not power or status. It is the response of a daughter who wants her father to rest.

**Trust / safety.** Trust is high and uncomplicated. Safety is high *within the operational frame* — Rogers will not exploit her — but moderate within the affective frame, because his disappointment is one of the few external sanctions she cannot defend against. Civil War-era ruptures with the broader team did not personalize between them.

**Failure mode.** Wanda will accept missions, frames, and self-conceptions from Rogers that she would interrogate from others. He is a blind spot in the direction of *over-compliance with a benign authority,* which is still over-compliance.

**Leverage.** Significant for any actor capable of presenting as Rogers (Skrulls, LMDs, magical impersonators — historically a vector). Rogers's *moral framing* of Wanda's actions matters enormously to her self-concept; an actor who could deliver a credible Rogers verdict could move her behavior more efficiently than coercion ever has.

---

## 4. Wonder Man (Simon Williams) — The Substitution, the Patient Suitor, the Brainwave Donor

**History.** Long arc, from the West Coast Avengers period through Busiek's Avengers and forward. The structural fact of the relationship is that Simon's brain patterns were the template used to give the Vision emotional capability. He is, neurologically, the original of which she loved the copy. After the Vision's emotional dismantling, Wanda and Simon enter an intermittent romance.

**Dynamics.** Simon is patient to the point of self-effacement; he loves her on a timeline she does not set and does not punish her for the timeline. The relationship is *kind* and *unequal* — Simon's affect is steadier than hers, his commitment more declarative, and Wanda is aware that she came to him second, after the copy of his feelings. There is a recurring guilt undertone: she suspects she is using him as a bridge object, and she is partially correct.

**Trust / safety.** Trust is high; safety is genuine but qualified by the substitution problem. Simon is a man who knows he is loved *partly for what the Vision was made from* and continues to show up. This is either nobility or a corresponding pathology; the dossier is agnostic.

**Failure mode.** The relationship dissolves under any pressure that re-foregrounds the Vision — a Vision iteration appears, the twins ask about their "father," a magical reconstruction is offered. Wanda's prior attachment will pull her, and Simon will let her go without contesting.

**Leverage.** Simon is a stabilizer when present and a non-issue when absent — uniquely low-leverage among her bonds, because he will not coerce, escalate, or destabilize. Hostile leverage would be redirected through him only as an injury vector (his death repeatedly registers as a stressor) rather than as manipulation.

---

## 5. Carol Danvers — The Friendship That Survived the Worst

**History.** Active teammates across multiple Avengers configurations. Carol was present for Disassembled — and was, in the aftermath, one of the voices that did not call for Wanda's permanent removal. Subsequent Krakoa-era and Avengers/Hellfire-era interactions show a sustained, professional, and personal closeness.

**Dynamics.** Carol is the operational counterpart to Clint's affective counterpart: she relates to Wanda *as a colleague of comparable threat-tier,* which almost no one else does. Most Avengers either underestimate Wanda (the Hawkeye-banter-without-the-respect mode) or fear her (post-M default). Carol does neither. She treats Wanda as a peer who has had a bad chapter, the way a soldier treats another soldier who has had a bad deployment.

**Trust / safety.** Trust is high in both directions. Safety is the highest in the file outside the twins — Carol does not flinch around her, does not curate herself, does not treat her as a glass object or a bomb.

**Failure mode.** Carol's affect is *military.* When Wanda needs softness, Carol's response is competence — useful, but not always what is needed. The friendship is durable but bounded by Carol's emotional vocabulary.

**Leverage.** Carol is a stabilizing presence whose endorsement carries operational weight (her judgment that Wanda is field-ready matters institutionally). A hostile actor isolating Carol from Wanda removes one of the small set of unflinching mirrors.

---

## 6. Billy / Wiccan and Tommy / Speed — Chosen Family by Reincarnation

*Note: the twins occupy both Relationships I (as the lost-and-returned children — the load-bearing wound) and this section (as adult chosen family in the present). What follows addresses their function as **chosen-family adults** in Wanda's life; the maternal-grief structure is in Section I.*

**History.** Billy Kaplan and Tommy Shepherd are introduced as Young Avengers (Heinberg) and revealed across Children's Crusade as reincarnated soul-fragments of Thomas and William. Adult contact between them and Wanda begins from her amnesiac wilderness state and proceeds, through reluctant acceptance, into stable familial relationship.

**Dynamics.** The unusual feature: Wanda relates to them with two simultaneous registers — the *mother* register (grief-saturated, careful, awed) and the *aunt-or-mentor* register (they are adults; they have lives, partners, an identity not contingent on her). She has visibly disciplined herself to honor the second register. She does not collapse them into the toddlers she lost. The restraint is one of the most psychologically mature behaviors in her record.

Billy is the more magically gifted; his powers structurally echo hers, and the mentorship dimension is real — she has tutored him in chaos-magic adjacent practice. Tommy is the more difficult — speedster-volatile, less emotionally available — and Wanda accepts the distance he keeps without pressing. This patience is not native to her; it is *learned* and *paid for.*

**Trust / safety.** Trust is total; safety is asymmetric. They are safe with her in any conceivable threat scenario; she is not entirely safe with them, in the clinical sense, because their wellbeing is the load-bearing element of her current stability.

**Failure mode.** Wanda will subordinate any other consideration — Avengers, X-Men, magical community, her own life — to the twins' welfare. This is the single largest source of operational risk in her current presentation. It is also, the dossier acknowledges, the single largest source of her *containment* — her reparative phase is held in place by their existence.

**Leverage.** Maximum. Harm or credible threat to either twin collapses the entire post-resurrection reparative structure. The Section 5 escalation ladder applies: severe stressor → reality-testing fails. This is the live wire and must be marked as such in any contingency document.

---

## 7. Doctor Strange — Peer, Wary Colleague, Occasional Supervisor

**History.** Recurrent collaboration across Defenders-adjacent crossovers, sorcery-tier crises, and in the post-M magical reconstruction work. Strange has been involved in attempts to assess, contain, restrain, and (in some arcs) prosecute Wanda magically.

**Dynamics.** Mutual respect with persistent friction. Strange's relationship to magic is *trained, ordered, hierarchical;* Wanda's is *native, intuitive, affect-coupled.* Strange finds her dangerous in ways she finds insulting; she finds him controlling in ways he finds prudent. They are correct about each other in equal measure.

The relationship is the only one in the magical community where Wanda is treated as both *peer* (in raw capability) and *patient* (in clinical-magical risk). She tolerates the latter framing only because she partially endorses it — her self-assessment of risk is closer to Strange's than to her own public statements suggest.

**Trust / safety.** Trust is medium and *bounded by domain* — she trusts his judgment on Sanctum-level magical questions, distrusts his judgment on questions concerning her autonomy. Safety is moderate: he will not exploit her, but he will act on her without full consent if he believes the risk warrants it.

**Failure mode.** Strange will overreach. Wanda will respond to the overreach with withdrawal rather than confrontation, and the magical community loses a potential collaborator each time.

**Leverage.** Strange's *invocation of containment* is one of the few things Wanda treats as a legitimate constraint on her own action. A hostile actor invoking Strange's authority (impersonation, forged communication, hijacked sanctum) could route her behavior.

---

## 8. The Young Avengers (collectively) — The Family She Did Not Know She Had

**History.** Indirect: Wanda was absent during the team's formation. Direct contact begins in Children's Crusade as the team seeks her out.

**Dynamics.** Wanda's relation to the team is mediated entirely through Billy. She extends to Teddy (Hulkling, Billy's husband), Kate Bishop, and the rotating Young Avengers roster a *family-by-extension* warmth that is one of the few unguarded affects in her current behavioral record. With Kate especially — Clint's protégé — there is a transitive trust that closes a small portion of the Clint-injury circuit.

**Trust / safety.** High and quiet. She does not try to lead them; she does not try to be their teacher; she shows up when asked. This is, for her, advanced relational hygiene.

**Failure mode.** Teddy's safety functions as a secondary live wire after the twins themselves. Harm to him collapses Billy, which collapses her.

**Leverage.** Moderate-to-high through Teddy and Kate as proxy vectors.

---

## 9. The Krakoan / Mutant Community (post-Trial of Magneto, post-Hellfire)

**History.** Wanda's relationship to the mutant community is the operational scar tissue of "No More Mutants." Krakoa-era arcs (Trial of Magneto, Hellfire Gala return, X-Men collaborations) trace a slow, partial, contested rehabilitation. Some quarters (Storm's circle, Magneto's eventual reckoning) extended grace; others did not and will not.

**Dynamics.** This is not a single relationship but a population, and Wanda relates to populations badly — her affective register is dyadic. She copes by *over-performing* service to the community as a whole, which is structurally the same defense as the Orlando-era door-always-open practice: be useful into existence, be useful into forgiveness.

**Trust / safety.** Asymmetric and unstable. Some mutants will never trust her; some have decided to. Her safety in mutant spaces is conditional and she knows it. She enters those spaces guarded in a way she does not enter Avengers spaces.

**Failure mode.** A high-profile mutant rejection — public, principled, from a respected figure — would land disproportionately hard. She is over-leveraged on the rehabilitation narrative.

**Leverage.** A hostile actor staging mutant-on-Wanda violence, or fabricating mutant testimony against her, attacks the most fragile face of her current self-concept.

---

## 10. Her Magical Clients (Orlando-era, "the door is always open")

**History.** Recent. The solo-run premise: Wanda maintains a literal doorway through which anyone needing magical help may enter, and she helps them.

**Dynamics.** This is not a relationship — it is a *practice,* and it is diagnostic. Each client is a micro-relationship constructed around the same template: stranger arrives in need; Wanda gives without metering; client leaves; Wanda waits for the next one. The compulsive availability is the load-bearing reparative behavior of the current era. It is the externalized form of the unconscious sentence *I will be useful enough to deserve to exist.*

**Trust / safety.** Trust extended to strangers is structurally over-extended. Her clients are not vetted. She is open to anyone, which means she is open to anyone.

**Failure mode.** A bad-faith client will eventually arrive disguised as a real one. The practice has no triage, no supervision, no peer review. She will be exploited through it, and the exploitation will register as confirmation that her service is necessary, which will deepen the practice rather than retire it.

**Leverage.** The single most accessible operational vector for any hostile actor with the patience to walk through a door. This must be marked.

---

## 11. Lorna Dane (Polaris) — Sister-Adjacent, Distant, Mirror

**History.** Variable canonicity around the Magneto-paternity question, but the *behavioral* sibling-adjacency persists across decades. They are women linked to Magneto, holding immense power, trying to construct selves outside his shadow.

**Dynamics.** Limited direct contact; high structural resonance. Each represents to the other a version of the question *what does it mean to be his daughter and not be him.* The relationship runs on recognition more than interaction.

**Trust / safety.** Default-positive, untested at depth.

**Failure mode.** Underdeveloped — neither has done the work of building this into a present-tense bond.

**Leverage.** Low directly; meaningful via the Magneto axis.

---

## 12. Pietro's Daughter, Luna Maximoff — The Niece, the Unbroken Innocence

**History.** Luna is Wanda's niece (Pietro and Crystal's daughter). Contact has been intermittent, complicated by Pietro's chronic instability and the Inhuman-side custody complexities.

**Dynamics.** Luna is the only child in Wanda's extended family whose existence has not been mediated by Wanda's powers — not a reincarnation, not a wish, not a construct. She is *ordinarily* family. Wanda's behavior with Luna is observably more relaxed than with the twins: she does not have to manage the metaphysical weight, only be an aunt.

**Trust / safety.** High in both directions.

**Failure mode.** Pietro's chronic chaos repeatedly disrupts access; Wanda accepts the disruption without confronting Pietro, in the long-standing pattern.

**Leverage.** Moderate; Luna's welfare matters to Wanda but is one layer further from the live wire than Billy and Tommy.

---

## Cross-Cutting Patterns

**The substitution structure.** Across the chosen-family map, Wanda repeatedly accepts *substitutes* — Simon for the brainwaves underneath the Vision; the Young Avengers for the team-children she did not raise; Billy and Tommy for Thomas and William; the door-clients for the patients she cannot heal in herself; Steve Rogers for the father Magneto was not. The substitutions are not cynical; they are *grief mathematics,* and they are mostly stabilizing. The risk is that she has not had the experience of a relationship that exists *for itself,* not as a reparation or a replacement.

**The asymmetry of giving.** In every dyad above, Wanda is the giver. Even where she receives (from Carol, from Rogers, from Clint's grace), she rapidly converts the receipt into a debt to be repaid. The dossier cannot identify a current relationship in which she is comfortably and durably the one being cared for. This is the single largest unmet need in her relational portfolio.

**The dosing of authority.** She accepts authority from exactly four people: Rogers (institutional/moral), Strange (magical/containment), Harkness (magical/training), and — historically, residually — Magneto (paternal/coercive). The first three are largely benign; the fourth is mapped in Relationships I. No woman currently holds authoritative position over her except a deceased or intermittently-present Harkness. The female-mentor seat in her life is *vacant,* which the dossier flags as a treatment-relevant gap (Bryant 2024's PGD-CBT protocol presumes a trustable clinician-figure, and Wanda's biography has trained her to receive that role from no one).

**Live-wire summary for handlers.**
1. Billy and Tommy — maximum leverage; harm collapses everything.
2. Teddy (via Billy) — secondary maximum.
3


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

A longitudinal mapping of the antagonists, intimates, and ambiguous-category figures who have shaped Wanda Maximoff's behavioral record. Each entry is independently derived from the published canon and structured for handler use: relational history, operative dynamics, evolutionary arc across decades, trust topology, characteristic failure mode under stress, and exploitable leverage.

---

## I. INTIMATES & LOVERS

### Vision (the original synthezoid)

**History.** First contact: *Avengers* #57–58 (1968). The Vision is introduced as a Tony Stark-built/Ultron-modified synthezoid who, upon defecting from Ultron, weeps — a single tear that is the founding image of him in Wanda's perceptual file. From that moment her behavior toward him is patient, protective, slow-moving. Courtship extends across Roy Thomas's run; consummation arrives in Englehart's tenure; marriage at *Giant-Size Avengers* #4 (1975), officiated by Immortus in Latveria's neighbor-of-record manner — already a wedding shadowed by cosmic interference. They cohabit in Leonia, New Jersey (Byrne's *Vision and the Scarlet Witch* limited series, 1985 and 1986), in a deliberately suburban domestic arrangement: clapboard house, lawn, neighbors who don't know what to do with them.

**Dynamics.** Vision is, for Wanda, the first attachment object that is *structurally incapable* of the volatility that defined every prior male in her life. Magneto rages; Pietro fulminates; the Vision modulates. She is not choosing a man despite his being a machine — she is choosing a partner *because* the machine substrate guarantees predictable affective output. This is not a pathology of love; it is an adaptive selection. She organizes the household, he organizes the logic; she initiates affection, he receives and reciprocates within a narrower band. He calls her "my wife" with a formality that she finds steadying.

**Evolution.** Three phases. **(a)** Newlywed equilibrium (1975–1984): the most psychologically settled period of her life; Avengers service, domestic life, quiet expansion of self-concept. **(b)** Pseudocyesis and parturition of Thomas and William (*Vision and the Scarlet Witch* #12, 1986): the union produces children that should not be possible, and the marriage briefly becomes a nuclear family. **(c)** Collapse (*West Coast Avengers* #42–45, "VisionQuest," 1989): government black-op disassembles Vision, the rebuild returns him as a chalk-white, emotion-stripped reconstruction who does not love her. Concurrent loss of the twins. The collapse is *total* and *simultaneous* — partner and children disappear in the same arc.

**Trust/safety.** Maximal during phase (a); the only relationship in her file that registers as secure-base behavior. After "VisionQuest" the trust object is *gone* — subsequent Visions (the resurrected color-restored version; the Vision of the Young Avengers era; later iterations) are treated by her with a careful, grief-saturated tenderness that is not the same emotion. She is kind to them; she is not married to them. They are reminders, not partners.

**Failure mode.** Wanda's capacity to remain integrated is partly outsourced to Vision's regulation. When he is removed, the regulatory architecture goes with him. *Avengers Disassembled* (Bendis, 2004) opens with Vision's destruction at her hand — note the symmetry: the figure whose existence regulated her is destroyed by the dysregulation his prior loss produced. The marriage's failure mode is not interpersonal conflict; it is *removal of the partner by external force*, after which she has no template for grief that does not become world-altering.

**Leverage.** Any extant Vision-iteration is the single highest-priority emotional asset/risk in her field. Threat to a Vision-iteration produces protective behavior of the highest order; sympathetic appeals routed through a Vision-iteration are effective beyond proportion. Conversely, presenting her with a Vision who *rejects* her (as the white reconstruction did) is the most reliable destabilizer in the catalog — it replays the founding wound with no defense available.

---

### Wonder Man (Simon Williams)

**History.** Long-running secondary entanglement, initiated tentatively in the Stern/Busiek era and intensifying through the late 1990s and *Avengers* vol. 3. The biographical hinge: Vision's emotional matrix was originally templated from Simon's brainwave patterns (Roy Thomas era retcon). Wanda's attraction to Simon after Vision's loss is therefore not a fresh romance — it is the *substrate* of her dead husband, walking around in flesh.

**Dynamics.** Asymmetrical and uncomfortable. Simon is openly, sometimes pleadingly in love with her; Wanda is ambivalent, drawn to the familiarity of the affective signature, repelled by the awareness of what that familiarity *means*. She never fully commits. The attraction operates on a substitution logic she half-understands and does not respect in herself.

**Evolution.** From cautious flirtation, to acknowledged mutual affection, to a tacit not-quite-relationship, to estrangement after *Disassembled* — Simon is among those displaced or dead in adjacent arcs and later returns as an antagonist convinced the Avengers themselves are the source of the world's catastrophes (*Avengers* by Bendis, "Wonder Man" arc). His turn against the team is laced with Wanda-specific grievance.

**Trust/safety.** Low-mid. She trusts his affection; she does not trust her own response to him. He is a relationship she conducts at arm's length because closer engagement would force her to confront the substitution.

**Failure mode.** Mutual avoidance disguised as fondness. Neither party metabolizes the underlying truth — that he is loved as a *ghost-substrate*, not as himself — and the relationship calcifies into something that hurts him and shames her.

**Leverage.** Simon is a reliable affective destabilizer if deployed adversarially — his accusations land harder than strangers' because he has standing. As an ally he is unreliable because his judgment toward her is compromised in both directions (over-protective, over-aggrieved).

---

### Vision (resurrected / subsequent iterations)

**History.** Vision has been rebuilt, re-emotionalized, replaced (Iron Lad's future-self-Vision in the Young Avengers era), and reconstituted across decades. Wanda has encountered most iterations.

**Dynamics.** A category of relationship she does not have a clean script for. The iterations are not her husband; they carry his memory; some of them carry partial memory of *her*. She approaches each with a slow, grieving politeness — neither claiming the bond nor disclaiming it.

**Trust/safety.** Variable, generally guarded. The Young Avengers' Vision treats her with cautious distance; the restored adult Vision (King's *Vision* series notwithstanding, which is its own self-contained tragedy) interacts with her as an estranged spouse who has lost the language for intimacy.

**Failure mode.** She over-extends compassion to them and they cannot give her back what their predecessor gave her. Each iteration is a small re-bereavement.

**Leverage.** Sentimental rather than tactical. Useful for de-escalation, dangerous for manipulation — she is aware enough of the trap that crude attempts to weaponize a Vision-iteration against her will register as cruelty and harden her.

---

### Brian Braddock / Agatha Harkness / mentor-figures as quasi-intimates

Not lovers. Noted here for completeness because Wanda's intimacy taxonomy is broader than the sexual: Agatha Harkness functioned for a period as the closest thing she had to a mother, with all the violations of that role (the memory suppression) intact. See enemies/ambivalents below.

---

## II. RIVALS — Operative Peers, Antagonists of Position

### Doctor Strange

**History.** Cohabitant of the mystic stratum. Strange and Wanda have been allies far more often than rivals (Defenders crossovers; *New Avengers: Illuminati* periphery; the Wanda-as-Sorcerer-Supreme arc in some continuities), but the relationship carries permanent low-grade rivalry because Strange represents the *disciplined, trained, institutionally-anchored* mode of magic that Wanda's chaos-magic implicitly rebukes. He is everything her practice is not: vetted, sanctioned, hierarchized.

**Dynamics.** Strange's posture toward Wanda is a blend of professional respect, paternal worry, and theological alarm. He understands the magnitude of her output and the absence of the formal restraints he relies on. Her posture toward him is deference *and* quiet resistance — she accepts his authority on mystic procedure, resents the implicit verdict on her amateurism.

**Evolution.** Pre-*Disassembled*: collegial, with Strange occasionally tutoring or warning her. Post-M: Strange becomes one of the figures whose memory of what she did is *unforgetting* and whose presence therefore confronts her with the worst version of herself. *Children's Crusade* (Heinberg) and subsequent arcs feature him as the reluctant senior magician who must adjudicate her.

**Trust/safety.** Medium-high mutual trust in tactical settings; mutual wariness in metaphysical ones.

**Failure mode.** Strange's mode is to *manage* her; Wanda experiences management as constraint and eventually slips it. If pushed to constrain her formally, he loses her cooperation.

**Leverage.** Strange's judgment carries weight with her — when he says she is dangerous she believes him, which is both useful and corrosive. Operators routing warnings through Strange will get traction; operators using Strange to coerce her will lose her entirely.

---

### Doctor Doom (Victor von Doom)

**History.** A relationship that straddles all three of this section's categories: rival, enemy, and — in the unsettling *Children's Crusade* arc — a thwarted intimate. Doom siphoned/channeled Wanda's chaos magic at the climactic moment of *House of M* (Heinberg's retcon), making him partially exogenously responsible for the magnitude of the event. Earlier and later, Doom courts her — politically, magically, and, with disturbing literalness, romantically (he proposes marriage in *Children's Crusade*).

**Dynamics.** Doom recognizes Wanda as the single mortal in his peer set whose raw capacity exceeds his own and whose psychological architecture is exploitable. He approaches her as both peer and prize — offering her power, recognition, and a partnership-of-equals framing that is precisely calibrated to her unmet need to be authored from inside rather than positioned from outside. She is not immune to it. She is also not deceived for long.

**Evolution.** From distant antagonism (early Avengers/FF crossovers) → opportunistic manipulator (House of M as siphon-event) → would-be consort (Children's Crusade) → repudiated suitor → permanent file-level threat. The post-Crusade posture: she will not be in a room with him without a witness.

**Trust/safety.** Near zero. She has empirical evidence he will use her power to amplify his own and call it love.

**Failure mode.** Doom's appeal targets the part of her that has never been *chosen as a sovereign* rather than as someone's daughter/sister/wife. If she is isolated, ego-wounded, and lacking reparative outlets, her defenses against him thin. This is a permanent vulnerability, not a closed file.

**Leverage.** Doom's interest in her is itself leverage *against* him — he is uncharacteristically careful around her, will negotiate terms he would not offer others, and is reluctant to harm her directly. Conversely, his proximity to her in any operational theater should be treated as a Tier-1 escalation event for her stability.

---

### Magneto (Erik Lehnsherr) — as rival/enemy axis

(Treated here in his rival/antagonist function; his paternal-figure function is mapped in Relationships I.)

**History.** Founding handler, first coercer, source of the original mutant-affiliated identity. Whether her biological father (1979 reveal, Englehart) or not (post-*AvX*/*Axis* retcons), the *behavioral parenthood* is real and continuous.

**Dynamics as rival.** When she defects to the Avengers and then later opposes him at intervals (the original Brotherhood, X-Men crossovers, AvX, Trial of Magneto), her opposition is not the clean opposition of strangers — it is the opposition of a daughter who knows the man's gestures, blind spots, and rhetorical traps. She fights him *informedly*, which makes her uniquely effective against him and uniquely exhausted by him.

**Evolution.** Coerced child → escaped follower → public opponent → estranged daughter → murderess of him in Krakoa's *Trial of Magneto* setup (which itself collapses into a more complex truth) → reconciled-but-wary co-mutant in current continuity.

**Trust/safety.** Permanently compromised. She does not trust him; she also cannot stop tracking him.

**Failure mode.** Magneto can still re-trigger the original compliance reflex briefly under acute conditions — not as conversion, but as a momentary regression that costs her tactical time.

**Leverage.** The "his weapon / his daughter first" framing is destabilizing if invoked. The Krakoa-era reconciliations have *softened* but not closed this wound; it remains the deepest pry-point in her psychology.

---

### Quicksilver (Pietro) — as rival axis

(Primary mapping in Relationships I as twin.) Noted here only because Pietro's *House of M* instigation makes him a co-architect of her worst act, and because their occasional adversarial arcs (he abducts the twins' soul-fragments in *Son of M*, he opposes her on policy across Krakoa-era events) place him intermittently across the rivalry line. Her capacity to oppose Pietro is the most affectively expensive opposition in her file.

---

### Hawkeye (Clint Barton)

**History.** Avengers teammate from the Kooky Quartet through decades of shared service. Killed by her during *Disassembled* (impaled by his own arrow after she warps reality around him). Later resurrected.

**Dynamics.** Post-resurrection Clint occupies the unique category of *the man she killed who has chosen, with great difficulty, not to hold it against her permanently*. The *Avengers: The Children's Crusade* sequence in which they re-encounter is among the most affectively raw in her file: Clint sleeps with the depowered, amnesiac Wanda in a moment that is read variously as reconciliation, exploitation, and mutual woundedness — and that he later regrets.

**Trust/safety.** Asymmetric. He has done the harder work of forgiveness; she has done the harder work of accepting that the forgiveness is real without using it as absolution.

**Failure mode.** Their interactions carry permanent low-grade grief radiation. Neither is operationally compromised by the other in tactical settings, but neither is fully comfortable.

**Leverage.** Clint is a credible character witness on her recovery — possibly the most credible, because he has the standing of the wronged. Operators seeking to assess her current stability should weight Clint's read heavily.

---

## III. ENEMIES — Direct Antagonists

### Mephisto

**History.** The metaphysical author of the twins' fragmented souls. In Englehart's resolution of the *Vision and the Scarlet Witch* arc, the twins are revealed to be fragments of Mephisto's own soul, which he then reclaims — unmaking the children. Mephisto is the cosmic agent of the founding bereavement.

**Dynamics.** Wanda's posture toward Mephisto is not the operational hatred of an adversary — it is the absolute, theological loathing reserved for the figure who took her children. There is no negotiation register available with him.

**Evolution.** Sporadic direct encounters; permanent symbolic presence. Each Mephisto-adjacent arc (and there are many across Marvel canon) reactivates the wound regardless of whether she is in the issue.

**Trust/safety.** Zero. Negative, if such a category exists.

**Failure mode.** Direct Mephisto contact under any circumstance risks decompensation; she cannot moderate around him.

**Leverage.** The single most effective destabilizer in the universe. Any operator with Mephisto-affiliated tooling against her is operating at thermonuclear scale.

---

### Agatha Harkness (enemy/mentor ambivalent)

**History.** Witchcraft mentor; later, with the consent of post-*VisionQuest* Wanda, the magical surgeon who erased the twins' memory. Decades later, that erasure is the *iatrogenic* event most directly responsible for the unmetabolized grief that detonated as *Disassembled* and *House of M*.

**Dynamics.** Wanda's relationship to Agatha is one of the most morally complicated in the file. Agatha taught her, protected her, *and* removed her capacity to mourn. The intervention was offered as mercy; in effect it was a sedative on a wound that needed cleaning.

**Evolution.** Mentor → savior → unwitting cause → posthumously contested figure. Agatha dies and recurs in various forms; Wanda's processing of her is unresolved.

**Trust/safety.** Mixed. Affection remains; trust does not.

**Failure mode.** The Harkness template — *the older woman who manages your grief by hiding it from you* — is one Wanda is alert to and now refuses. Any current handler attempting analogous "mercy" will be recognized and rebuffed.

**Leverage.** Limited tactical leverage; high symbolic salience.

---

### Chthon

**History.** Elder God; original source of the chaos magic that may have entered Wanda at birth on Mount Wundagore (Bova / High Evolutionary origin layer). Periodically attempts to claim her as vessel (Bloodties; various horror-tinged arcs).

**Dynamics.** Chthon treats her as property; she treats him as a parasite to be expelled. Several arcs feature partial possession.

**Trust/safety.** Zero.

**Failure mode.** Possession scenarios bypass her conscious controls. The dissociative architecture she has lived inside her whole life is, unfortunately, a hospitable substrate for entities like Chthon.

**Leverage.** Chthonic possession is a Tier-1 catastrophic risk event. Mystic monitoring should be standing.

---

### The Grim Reaper (Eric Williams)

**History.** Wonder Man's brother; perennial Avengers antagonist; convinced that the Vision (carrying Simon's brainwaves) is a perversion. By extension Wanda — as Vision's wife — is contaminated in his cosmology.

**Dynamics.** Personal, vindictive, and theatrical. He targets her through Vision, through Simon, through the twins.

**Trust/safety.** Adversarial; she does not underestimate him despite his showmanship.

**Failure mode.** Reaper's attacks aim at her relational network rather than her person, which is operationally apt — her network is her vulnerability.

**Leverage.** Predictable in target selection. Useful as a tripwire for early-warning around her domestic perimeter.

---

### Norman Osborn / institutional enemies (Dark Reign-era and after)

**History.** Osborn's regime targeted reality-rewriting threats; Wanda was on every such list. Less personal than systemic.

**Dynamics.** Institutional antagonism rather than personal vendetta. She is registered, watched, hunted in the abstract.

**Failure mode.** State-level scrutiny activates her paranoia about being *deployed* — the originating Magneto wound — and pushes her toward isolation, which is itself a risk state.

**Leverage.** Institutional adversaries are best engaged through intermediaries she trusts; direct state contact tends to backfire.

---

### Her own past self / "the Witch Who Ended The Mutants"

The most persistent enemy in the file is internal. Wanda's reparative arc post-2014 is structured around an antagonist who is *herself, as remembered by the X-Men, the mutant community, and her own conscience*. The Krakoa-era arcs (Hickman/Williams/Ewing/Duggan) feature mutants who will not forgive her; she absorbs this as accurate. The *Trial of Magneto* and the Hellfire Gala sequences function as her attempt to settle accounts with this internal enemy by service, sacrifice, and (literally) death-and-resurrection.

**Failure mode.** When external enemies are quiet, the internal enemy fills the silence; periods of operational peace are paradoxically her highest-risk depressive intervals.

**Leverage.** Reparative work suppresses the internal enemy. Removing her access to reparative outlets (the open door of the Orlando run; the connection to the mutant community; mentorship of Wiccan) would worsen her state faster than any external pressure.

---

## IV. AMBIGUOUS-CATEGORY FIGURES

### Nightcrawler, Wolverine, the X-Men post-M

Not enemies in the operational sense; carriers of a permanent grievance. Most have arrived, over the decade-plus reparative arc, at a working accommodation. Logan's posture is a guarded *we'll see;* Kurt's is a theologically inflected willingness to extend grace; Storm's is a queen's pragmatic re-admission of a peer who has paid. None will forget. All will work with her. This is the best she has earned and she treats it as such.

### Captain America (Steve Rogers)

Not a rival; a moral compass-point. Her relationship to Steve is filial-respectful; his post-*Disassembled* judgment of her was severe and his subsequent re-acceptance is among the recoveries she most values. Operationally: Steve's continued willingness to stand near her is one of the few external indicators she trusts about her own current safety.

### Wiccan (Billy Kaplan) and Speed (Tommy Shepherd)

Catalogued in Relationships II as family. Mentioned here only to note the **permanent file rule**: any threat, harm, deception, or weaponization involving these two collapses every other relational consideration in this section. Friends, rivals, enemies, lovers — all are downstream of this fact. The twins are not leverage to be used; they are the *single existential variable* that determines whether the entire architecture mapped above holds.

---

*— End section. Relationships IV (Institutional, Communal, Mentorship) to follow.*


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## Subject: Wanda Maximoff — Operational Capability Assessment

A complete capability file on this subject is, unavoidably, also a clinical file. Her power is not a tool she picks up; it is an organ. It scales with affect, responds to wish, and has no firewall between the limbic system and the world. What follows maps the instrument, then the limits, then the unmistakable fact that the instrument *is* the symptom.

---

## 1. Taxonomy of Capability — What She Can Actually Do

The published record discloses **five overlapping operational tiers**, each layered on the prior. They were not acquired sequentially in a clean ladder; they were re-described retroactively as her power outran the explanations available to her handlers and authors. The functional taxonomy:

**Tier 1 — Probability manipulation ("hex bolts," X-Men #4 through early Avengers).** The original description: a directed gesture (the well-documented two-handed splay, fingers slightly curled, wrists rotated outward) producing a localized perturbation in the likelihood of small-scale physical events. Mechanism as Wanda herself initially understood it: she "made unlikely things happen." Range: line-of-sight, modest distance, decaying over a few hundred feet. Visible signature: the red shimmer along the trajectory, more aurora than projectile. Operational uses in this period are mundane to the point of charming — guns jam, floors give way, gas lines ignite, ropes fray, an opponent's footing fails. *No reality is being rewritten;* the world is merely being asked to take its lowest-probability path.
