**Tier 2 — Direct kinetic/energetic discharge.** By the Englehart and early Byrne runs the hex has stopped pretending to be statistics. She throws force. Walls come down. Vehicles flip. A discharge can be sustained as a continuous beam rather than a bolt. The somatic tell — the two-handed splay — persists, now functioning more like a barrel-sight than a probability-channel. This is the form most reliably available to her under combat conditions and the form she still uses when she wants to look like an Avenger rather than a witch.

**Tier 3 — Formal sorcery (post-Harkness apprenticeship; Vision and the Scarlet Witch ltd.).** Agatha Harkness's tutelage installs the disciplined craft layer: warding, sigil-work, divination, summoning, banishment, the Latin/Romani/Romanian incantatory register, and — critically — *containment* protocols she had never possessed. This is the period in which Wanda becomes literate in her own medium. Witchcraft as taught: rule-bound, costly, reversible. The instructor's project was to give her the safeties her mutancy lacked.

**Tier 4 — Chaos magic (retconned active by Busiek, foregrounded by Bendis).** The recharacterization that broke the ceiling. "Chaos magic" is presented as a primal force tied to the disorder underlying ordered reality; Wanda is its preeminent — at intervals, sole — Earth-side conduit. Operationally this manifests as: probability-warp without gesture, telekinesis without effort, energy projection without aim, transmutation, levitation, teleportation across continental scale, telepathic and empathic perception, life-restoration in narrow circumstances, and the ability to instantiate *living matter* that did not previously exist (Wiccan and Speed in their original phenomenology; later, the twins as resurrected/reincarnated; arguably much of House of M's population).

**Tier 5 — Reality revision.** The terminal tier. Demonstrated three times unambiguously in the modern record: the constructed home with the twin sons (Vision and the Scarlet Witch); the global reconstruction of House of M; the three-word terminal command **"No more mutants."** Mechanism: spoken (or, in the home-with-the-twins case, *wished*) sentence-level edits to the consensus world-state, applied globally, retained until contradicted or until the speaker collapses the construct. There is no known upper bound to a single revision's scope; the practical limits are duration, cost to the operator, and the operator's coherence at the moment of speech.

---

## 2. Mechanism — How It Actually Works

The mechanism evolves, and the evolution matters because each redescription is a story she and her handlers told themselves to make the next escalation tolerable. The honest synthesis from the behavioral record:

**The power is affectively coupled.** Output magnitude tracks arousal, not intention. In a calm laboratory or training context she throws hexes the size of her thoughts. In acute distress she throws hexes the size of her *feelings.* The Disassembled rampage and the House of M construction were not maximum-effort sorcery; they were affect leakage at maximum amplitude. This is the single most operationally relevant fact in the file.

**The power is wish-shaped, not plan-shaped.** Strange casts; Doom engineers; Wanda *wants.* When she works deliberately, she does so by formulating an image of a desired end-state and pushing through. This is why House of M reads like a dream rather than a dictatorship — everyone she loved received the wish-fulfillment version of their own life because the construction protocol was *give them what they would want.* The cognitive style is primary-process: condensed, image-driven, associative, mood-congruent. This is the *psychology* of the magic; the magic does what her unconscious does, only out loud.

**Speech-act amplification.** From late Bendis onward her highest-order workings are verbal. "No more mutants." "I love you." "No more Avengers." The terminal tier requires utterance. Inferred mechanism: declarative speech imposes the cognitive specificity her wish-style otherwise lacks; once specified, the wish becomes executable as a world-edit. Handler implication: her *language* is the trigger, not her gestures. A hand restraint is irrelevant if her mouth is free.

**Energy economy — diffuse, not metered.** There is no observed mana pool, no clear fatigue curve, no consistent overdraw symptom. What there is, repeatedly: post-event dissociation, amnesia, and somatic collapse after maximum workings. The cost appears to be paid in **psychic integration** rather than in joules. Each terminal-tier act fragments her further. The House of M aftermath — amnesia, recovered in stages over years — is the canonical example.

**The mutant/witch overlap.** Whether her capability is genetic (X-gene), inherited witch-line (the Scarlet Witch as a recurrent metaphysical office), or exogenously sourced (Doom's siphon during House of M's climax; demonic templating in the original twin pregnancy) has been answered differently in different decades. The behavioral file does not require resolution: regardless of substrate, the *coupling to grief and the wish-driven execution profile are invariant.* Every redescription of the source has left the symptom-shape unchanged.

---

## 3. Range, Resolution, Duration

**Spatial range.** Tier 1–2 hex work: hundreds of feet, line-of-sight preferred but not required. Tier 3 sorcery: bounded by the standard sorcerous geometries — circles, sympathetic links, named targets. Tier 4 chaos work: planetary at demonstrated maximum (Decimation); intercontinental routinely. Tier 5: global, single-pass, on the published record.

**Resolution.** She can be exquisitely fine (restoring a specific person's specific memory; instantiating two distinct children with distinct temperaments; opening a door at a precise threshold in the Orlando-era shop) and catastrophically coarse (a three-word edict that did not specify *which* mutants, *which* powers, *which* aspects of the gene to retain). The resolution tracks her affective state. Calm Wanda is a scalpel; grieving Wanda is a guillotine.

**Duration.** Hexes are instantaneous; sorcerous workings persist as long as their sustaining structure does; chaos-magic constructs persist until the operator collapses them or external intervention dismantles them. The House of M reality persisted until *she herself* spoke its undoing. The Decimation has persisted in canon — partially reversed only by sustained, deliberate, multi-arc reparative effort across the Krakoan era. **Wanda's edits do not decay on their own.** They have to be argued with by another act of comparable magnitude.

---

## 4. Growth Over Time — The Escalation Curve

The growth curve is not skill acquisition; it is *containment failure.*

- **1964–early 1970s:** Hex-bolts, modest. Mentor: none meaningful. Containment: external (Magneto, then Avengers protocols).
- **Mid 1970s–1980s:** Sorcery added under Harkness. Containment: instructor-imposed, the most stable period of her operational life.
- **Late 1980s (Vision/Scarlet Witch ltd.):** First documented reality-instantiation (the twins). Containment: collapses; Harkness intervenes with iatrogenic memory suppression — symptom removed, pathology preserved.
- **1990s–early 2000s:** Power redescribed as chaos magic. Containment: nominal; the surface stabilizes; the suppression is doing the work, not any actual integration.
- **2004–2005 (Disassembled, House of M):** Containment annihilated. Tier 5 capability demonstrated and weaponized by grief.
- **Post-2005 wilderness:** Power apparently quiescent during amnesia. *Inference:* the capability and the self are co-located; when the self is fragmented, the capability is too.
- **2014–present:** Reintegration arcs. The reparative phase shows a Wanda who can do almost anything she did at peak — but now with conscience as the throttle and a compulsive availability (the open-door shop) as the channel. The power has not shrunk; the operator has rebuilt around it.

The honest reading of the curve: **she has not gotten more powerful. She has gotten less repressed.** Each ceiling-break in the published record coincides with a defense-mechanism collapse, not with training.

---

## 5. Skills (Non-Magical)

Often understated in the threat literature, persistently relevant in the operational record:

- **Languages.** Native Sokovian/Transian register; fluent English; functional Romani; ritual Latin and the cobbled Romanian-Latinate incantatory dialect of Harkness's tradition.
- **Hand-to-hand.** Avengers-trained basics; competent but not elite. She does not enjoy fighting and does not seek it.
- **Tradecraft.** Decades of operating in and around Magneto, the Brotherhood, the Avengers, the X-office, and various magical orders have given her serviceable situational awareness, threat triage, and the ability to read a room's politics quickly.
- **Caregiving.** Underrated as a skill. She is genuinely competent with frightened civilians, traumatized children, and the magically injured. The Orlando-era practice exists because she is good at it.
- **Ritual craft.** Drawing, candle-work, sigil construction, divination by tarot and by scrying — Harkness's legacy, maintained.

---

## 6. Signature Applications — The Way She Actually Uses It

Total-surveillance pattern recognition, drawn from across the record:

- **The two-handed splay.** The combat gesture. Fingers slightly curled, wrists rotated outward, elbows bent. Persistent across every era including the chaos-magic period when it is no longer mechanically necessary. *It is a self-cue, not a channel.* She does it to remind herself she is the one doing this.
- **The whispered preface.** Before a major working she often murmurs — sometimes a name, sometimes Romani, sometimes nothing identifiable. Inferred function: priming the speech-act apparatus; she is warming up her instrument.
- **Red as signature.** The aurora-red signature is *constant* across tiers, which is unusual — most magical practitioners' visible signatures vary by working. Hers does not. The color is identity-coded; the magic is *of her,* not just *through her.*
- **Construct-by-image.** When she builds — houses, children, a world — she works from an emotional image rather than a schematic. The constructions are textured with sentiment (the home with the twins was furnished with the *feel* of a home she had never had).
- **Restoration as preferred mode.** Given a choice, she would rather fix than destroy. The post-2005 record is dominated by restorations: of memories, of mutants, of relationships, of selves. This is character expressed as operational preference.
- **The reluctant escalation.** She moves up the tier ladder under duress, almost never voluntarily. Operators have seen her take damage at Tier 2 levels rather than reach for Tier 3. She is, in her own assessment, dangerous, and she behaves accordingly.

---

## 7. Limits — Hard, Soft, and Self-Imposed

**Hard limits (demonstrated).**
- *Death.* She has died; she required external resurrection. The power did not save her at the terminal moment.
- *Coherence threshold.* The terminal-tier workings cost integration; she cannot stack them. Post-House of M, she could not have immediately performed another comparable working.
- *Speech requirement at maximum.* Major edits require articulation. A gagged or unconscious Wanda is not a Tier 5 threat.
- *Specificity failure.* Her edits do what she says, including what she did not realize she was saying. "No more mutants" was operationally precise and morally catastrophic precisely because she did not specify.

**Soft limits (defeatable but reliable).**
- *Affective coupling.* Calm her and the ceiling drops; provoke her and the ceiling vanishes. Handlers who manage her affect manage her power.
- *Counter-magic.* Strange, Doom, Selene, the Asgardian register, and certain Krakoan/Arakkii practitioners can interfere with her workings, though rarely overpower her.
- *Anti-magic environments and technology* (limbo zones, certain Stark-class neutralizers) reduce but have not historically negated her.
- *Mystic contracts and prior compacts.* She will honor a binding; she has done so even when it cost her.

**Self-imposed limits — the most important category.**
- *She does not kill in the calm state.* The kills on her record are decompensation events.
- *She does not coerce minds when she is herself.* House of M is the exception that proves the rule, and she has spent two decades atoning for it.
- *She refuses scale.* In the reparative phase she works at one-client-at-a-time resolution by deliberate choice. She is rationing herself.
- *She avoids the verbal terminal-tier register.* She does not speak in declarative cosmic edicts in the modern era. This is conscious. It is also the single most load-bearing safety she has, and it is held in place by her own will, which is held in place by the existence of her sons.

---

## 8. The Symptom-as-Signature Reading

This is where the capability file and the clinical file fuse, and where the dossier earns its keep.

**The power is the pathology, externalized.** Every clinical feature documented in the workup — the affect coupling, the primary-process cognition under stress, the wish-as-cognition style, the dissociative response to overload, the catastrophic denial of intolerable realities, the reparative compulsion — has a one-to-one operational analog in how the magic behaves. This is not coincidence and it is not metaphor. **The magic is doing, at scale, what her psychology is already doing internally.**

- *Affect dysregulation* → output scales with arousal; no limbic firewall.
- *Wish-cognition* → constructs take wish-shape, not plan-shape; House of M is a dream made consensus.
- *Repression and dissociation* → power quiesces during amnesia; capability and self co-located.
- *Denial response to catastrophic loss* (the clinical literature's central feature of complicated grief — Bryant et al. 2024; Pop-Jordanova 2021) → reality revision as the terminal-tier symptom. House of M is *the denial phase of prolonged grief disorder, executed with planetary capability.*
- *Anger phase* → "No more mutants," discharged at the species her father weaponized her for.
- *Reparative phase* → the Orlando-era open door; the Decimation reversals; the compulsive availability that is, clinically, guilt-driven over-functioning.

**The signature gesture is a containment ritual.** The two-handed splay is, read clinically, a *self-grounding behavior* — a body-cue she uses to keep herself the agent of the act rather than the medium of it. Its persistence into the chaos-magic period, when it is mechanically unnecessary, is the giveaway. She is reassuring herself, every time, that she is the one doing this. The day she stops doing it is the day to worry.

**The red is identity.** Other practitioners' magic varies in color by working; hers does not. The capability is not an external resource she draws on. It is *her,* discharged. Which means any clinical destabilization is a capability destabilization, and vice versa. There is no separating the woman from the weapon, and any handler protocol that pretends otherwise will fail at the worst possible moment.

**The terminal-tier register is the grief register.** She has only ever spoken at Tier 5 under conditions of catastrophic loss or its imminent return. The capability is *grief-locked* in its highest mode. This is the most important operational fact in the file: she does not need to be made angry to become a planet-scale event. She needs to be made to grieve.

**Therefore the operational ceiling tracks the grief baseline.** As long as Wiccan and Speed are alive and reachable, as long as no fresh catastrophic loss is inflicted, the ceiling holds at reparative — itself an extraordinary capability profile, but a *bounded* one, voluntarily bounded by her. Remove either condition and the ceiling is not just raised; it is removed. The capability reverts to what House of M demonstrated, and the only restraint then is whether the surviving fragment of her self can still hold the splay-gesture and remember she is the one doing this.

— End capability assessment. The instrument and the operator are the same person; treat the file accordingly.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT — SUBJECT: WANDA MAXIMOFF

*UATU dossier, Section 5 of working file. Operational, not psychological — though with this subject the membrane is thin and we will note where it bleeds through. All inferences derived from longitudinal observation of the published behavioral record.*

---

## 1. Decision Architecture

Wanda Maximoff does not decide the way an operator decides. She does not run options, weight outcomes, or model second-order effects. She **arrives** at action through a three-stage internal process that is observable across every major engagement on file:

1. **Affective intake.** She reads the emotional weather of a situation before she reads its facts. Her first orientation is to *who is hurt, who is afraid, who is alone in the room.* Tactical geometry (numbers, weapons, exits) is processed second, sometimes not at all.
2. **Image-formation.** A desired end-state crystallizes as a picture — not a plan. The "wish" is the operational unit. Witnesses to her preparation phase (Vision, Agatha Harkness, Wiccan) describe her as going still and looking past the speaker. She is *composing,* not deliberating.
3. **Discharge.** Capability is released against the image. Precision is a function of affective integration: calm Wanda is surgical (the careful magical interventions of the Orlando-era walk-in practice); flooded Wanda is climatological (Disassembled, House of M, the partial Decimation reversals).

**Operational implication.** She is not a planner-class threat. She is a *manifestation-class* threat. The relevant intelligence question is never "what is she planning" — it is "what does she presently wish were true, and how integrated is her affect right now."

**Decision latency.** Short when affect-driven, very long when conscience-driven. Reparative decisions (rebuilding the mutant population, opening the witch-road shop, accepting resurrection's terms) are stretched over months and years of deliberation; reactive decisions (pulling a child out of danger, striking at a perceived threat to attachment objects) are sub-second.

**Override conditions.** Wanda can be talked down by exactly four categories of person: Wiccan/Speed (the twins); Vision in any of his iterations (residual transference); Agatha Harkness (the inverted-mother, both threat and authority); and, situationally, Steve Rogers (clean moral authority she does not perceive as exploitative). Magneto can *destabilize* her decision process but cannot reliably *steer* it — a critical distinction that the Brotherhood, the X-Men, and the Avengers have all learned at cost.

---

## 2. Tradecraft — How She Actually Works

### 2.1 The Magical Praxis

Her working style has evolved across three identifiable phases:

- **Hex-bolt era (1964 – mid-1980s).** Gestural, narrow-cast, plausibly deniable as "luck." Wanda in this period operates the way a person who does not trust her own hands operates — small, contained, with the bolt thrown almost apologetically. Tell: she would often *raise the hand and immediately lower it,* discharging the hex with minimal follow-through.
- **Chaos magic era (Harkness tutelage onward).** Larger gestures, two-handed sigils, Romani-inflected verbal components she did not previously use. The vocalization is real tradecraft, not flourish: under Harkness she was taught to externalize intention through speech as a *braking mechanism* on the wish-discharge.
- **Witchcraft-integrated era (Robinson solo onward, deepened in Orlando run).** A formal magical practice — circles, ritual tools, the consultation of older witches (Agatha, the Witches' Road network, the spirit of her aunt Natalya). Wanda now *does the work* in the way a working witch does: research, preparation, consultation, deliberate inscription. This phase represents the most regulated and least dangerous version of her operational signature.

The diagnostic tell across all phases: **her power output is coupled to her respiration and pupil diameter.** Operators who have stood close to her in working condition (Vision, Strange) note breath-shortening, slight pupillary dilation, and a temperature drop at the skin in the seconds before discharge. She is, in this sense, somatically legible — the body publishes the work before the work occurs.

### 2.2 Verbal Tradecraft

She uses very few words to do very large things. The pattern is consistent across her career:
- **"No more Vision."** (Disassembled, paraphrased intent.)
- **"No more mutants."** (House of M.)
- **"I love you."** (post-Decimation, to Wiccan, accompanying real-world causal effect.)

The compression is not stylistic. It is *operational economy:* when the wish is the weapon, articulation must be minimal or the wish drifts. She has learned — possibly not consciously — that long sentences leak intention. Her most catastrophic acts are three-word sentences.

In non-magical communication she is by contrast verbose, courteous, and Eastern-European-inflected in syntax (subject-fronting, occasional dropped articles when tired or under stress — a stress tell discussed below).

### 2.3 Cover, Concealment, and Movement

Wanda's lifelong default is **passing as unremarkable.** Civilian clothes during travel, no public-facing social presence, cash where cash is functional, train or walking over flight where geography allows. She is comfortable in working-class environments — the legacy of the Transian-Romani upbringing — and conspicuously uncomfortable in stratified social settings (Stark galas, diplomatic functions).

Her safehousing pattern is rural-and-old: cottages, brownstones, isolated estates, the Avengers Compound only as institutionally required. She prefers structures with *worked stone, exposed beams, a hearth.* This is not aesthetic — these are environments she can warded, and she instinctively chooses surfaces that hold a ward (organic materials over poured concrete and glass).

Movement signature: she walks. Even when teleportation is available to her, she will *walk into a town* before doing the work there. This appears to be a grounding ritual — she reads a place on foot before she imposes anything on it. Surveillance teams have repeatedly lost her by overcommitting to vehicular or aerial coverage.

### 2.4 Counter-Intelligence Habits

She does not sweep for surveillance in any conventional sense and does not appear to consider electronic intrusion meaningful. She does, however, **feel watched** with high reliability — she has detected Stark satellite tasking, telepathic touch from both Xavier and the Cuckoos, and at least one S.W.O.R.D. observation envelope, all without instrumentation. The mechanism appears to be a low-grade ambient probability awareness: surveillance perturbs the local field, she registers the perturbation as a somatic prickle (she touches the back of her neck), and adjusts.

Operationally, this means: **you cannot covertly observe her at close range for sustained periods. You can observe her behavior at distance through human-source reporting and after-action artifact analysis, which is the basis of this file.**

---

## 3. Resources

### 3.1 Financial

Wanda is, by the standards of her cohort, **poor and indifferent to the fact.** She has at various points drawn an Avengers stipend, sold artifacts and services through the Orlando-era walk-in practice (cash and barter, no records), and lived on the hospitality of the Maximoff/Lehnsherr family network and the X-line during Krakoan residence. She has never:
- maintained known investment holdings;
- registered a business entity in her own name;
- engaged a financial intermediary at the level of complexity that Stark, Richards, or even Murdock employ.

She moves money the way someone raised in displacement moves money: in small amounts, often, with a strong preference for tangible exchange. The witch-shop in the Orlando run accepted *favors, objects, debts of service* as freely as currency — this is not bohemian affectation, it is the pre-modern economy of the Romani working witch, and it is her native frame.

**Operational implication.** She is not vulnerable to financial coercion. There is nothing to freeze, leverage, or audit. Conversely, she is structurally incapable of mounting a sustained logistics tail and is dependent on institutional support (Avengers, X-Men, Strange's network) whenever an operation exceeds the scale of a single working.

### 3.2 Material

- **Magical implements:** a working set of athame, chalice, bell, and a personal grimoire (composite — partly Natalya Maximoff's inherited book, partly her own additions). She is observed to *not* require the implements for combat working; she requires them for sustained ritual and for delicate reparative work.
- **Wardrobe-as-armor:** the red garments are functionally a uniform and almost certainly enchanted — she has been observed taking impacts in costume that should have ended her, with the garments themselves retaining integrity. She does not discuss this and it is likely not something she consciously maintains; the clothes have been with her long enough to have *acquired* the warding through proximity to her practice.
- **Crown / tiara:** ceremonial, used inconsistently. Appears in periods of heightened public identity (Avengers leadership tenures, Hellfire Gala). Functions as a *self-cue* to be the public Scarlet Witch rather than the private Wanda.

### 3.3 Network

This is where her real resource base lies. Mapped concentrically:

- **Inner ring (load-bearing):** Wiccan, Speed, Vision (current iteration), Agatha Harkness (adversarial-adjacent), Pietro (intermittent, fraught).
- **Second ring (high-trust operational):** Steve Rogers, Clint Barton (post-reconciliation), Doctor Strange (professional respect, mutual caution), Magik (Krakoan adjacency, sister-witch alliance), Natasha Romanoff (historical).
- **Third ring (institutional access):** the standing Avengers roster, the X-Men senior council, the witch networks of the eastern seaboard and Transia.
- **Hostile or transactional:** Doom (a relationship of mutual exploitation in which she is usually the exploited party), Mephisto (the original buyer of the soul-fragments, never fully repaid), the Wrecking Crew and other low-tier antagonists who have learned to fear her name.

She does not run agents, does not pay informants, does not maintain dead drops. Her network is held together by personal bond and historical debt, in both directions. **The currency of her tradecraft is loyalty, paid in service.**

---

## 4. Infrastructure

She maintains no fortress, no sanctum, no orbital platform. The closest things to operational infrastructure on file:

- **The witch-road door.** In the Orlando-era practice, a magical threshold that opens onto her shop from any door anywhere, given the right knock. This is the closest she has ever come to a deployable asset — a *publicly-available* point of contact for anyone in magical need. The choice to make it open, rather than concealed, is deeply characterological: she has built her one piece of infrastructure as an *availability mechanism* rather than a defense.
- **Ancestral sites in Transia / Wundagore.** Periodically returned to. Function as both pilgrimage and recharge — she will be observed at family graves before major workings.
- **The hearth, wherever she is living.** She lights a fire. She keeps things on a mantel. This is not décor; it is a working surface that travels with her.

There is no command structure subordinate to her. She has briefly led teams (Avengers field leadership, occasional X-line tactical command) and acquits herself competently in those roles but does not seek them and disengages from them as soon as institutionally permitted.

---

## 5. Patterns of Action

### 5.1 The Operational Calendar

Across decades the observable cadence has been:

- **Long quiet periods** (months to years) of low-visibility domestic life, teaching, magical practice, or institutional team service.
- **Acute engagement bursts** (hours to days) of high-magnitude action when an attachment object is threatened or when a moral debt comes due.
- **Reparative campaigns** (years) following any major destructive event — the post-Decimation arc, the post-resurrection arc, the post-Trial reconciliations.

She does not operate continuously. She is not a campaigner. She is a *responder,* and her response architecture is the structure that any handler or adversary needs to understand.

### 5.2 Escalation Ladder (Operational)

1. **Verbal engagement, courteous.** Initial contact almost always begins with an attempt at conversation. She talks first.
2. **Withdrawal and request for non-engagement.** "Please leave." If she gives this warning, she is already past her preferred resolution.
3. **Defensive working.** Shields, redirections, probability nudges — non-lethal, non-permanent.
4. **Offensive working, targeted.** Discrete hex bolts, immobilizations, transformations. Reversible.
5. **Area working.** Environment alteration, weather effects, large-scale probability inversions. Begins to threaten bystanders.
6. **Reality-class working.** Three-word sentence territory. Doctrinal threshold. Has been crossed twice on the record. Once crossed in a given engagement, cannot be re-contained from outside without catastrophic cost.

The ladder is climbed slowly under controlled grief and jumped under acute grief. The intelligence value of identifying which rung she occupies at any moment cannot be overstated.

### 5.3 Target Selection

When she selects targets — which is rare; she is almost always reacting to selection by others — the pattern is:
- **Persons who took from her** (the Avengers, in the Disassembled fugue; reality itself, in House of M; Magneto, in Trial; her own crimes, in the reparative arcs).
- **Persons threatening the children.** No deliberation, no warning, no ladder. Full discharge.

She does not target institutions for ideological reasons. She does not target the wealthy for class reasons. She does not target oppressors for political reasons, despite the occasional rhetoric — her actions sort by *attachment-relevance,* not ideology.

---

## 6. Signature Operational Tells

For the file, in descending diagnostic value:

- **The respiratory shift.** A long exhale, then a held breath, three to seven seconds before any significant working. The single most reliable predictor of imminent discharge.
- **The lowered chin, raised eyes.** Combat-posture tell. She does not square shoulders or widen stance; she drops her head fractionally and looks up. Witnesses report it as *unsettling at distance, terrifying at conversational range.*
- **The hand-touch to the locket / pendant / collarbone.** Self-soothing under stress; when she does this in conversation, she is metabolizing something difficult and the conversation should be redirected.
- **The dropped article in English speech** ("I am going to *the* store" becomes "I am going to store"). Stress tell. Native syntax surfaces when cognitive load is high.
- **The half-step back before a hex.** A vestige of the early-career reluctance. She still gives ground before she throws — a courtesy to the universe that she would prefer not to do this.
- **The post-working stillness.** After any significant discharge she will not move for a measurable interval — three to fifteen seconds — eyes unfocused. This is **the single greatest operational vulnerability on her body.** Any actor with the means and the will could end her in this window. That no one has is a fact about the people around her, not about her.
- **The avoidance of mirrors after a working.** She will not look at her own reflection in the minutes following large magic. Read this as guilt-affect peaking; she is most approachable, most truthful, and most likely to accept correction in this state.
- **The naming of the children.** She says "Billy" and "Tommy" rather than "Wiccan" and "Speed" when she is regulated. When she uses the code-names she is in operational mode and the affective channel is closed.
- **The fire-tending.** In any domestic setting with a hearth, she will rise from conversation to tend it without breaking the sentence. This is a containment ritual; the fire is a proxy for the magic she is *not* doing.
- **The refusal to swear.** Across sixty years of record, profanity is essentially absent from her speech. When she swears — almost always in Romani or Transian — the operational situation has become extreme.

---

## 7. Net Operational Assessment

She is not an operator in the trained sense. She has no formal tradecraft education, no institutional clandestine training, no doctrine. She is something both less and more dangerous: a profoundly capable person who *manifests her interior life directly into the world,* whose tradecraft is the management of her own affect, and whose infrastructure is a hearth, a door, a handful of people she loves, and a book she did not entirely write.

She can be tracked through human sources and aftermath. She cannot be tracked covertly at close range. She cannot be coerced through resources because she has none worth coercing. She cannot be deterred by escalation; escalation is precisely the input that drives her up her own ladder.

She can, however, be **engaged** — by people who treat her as a person before they treat her as a capability, by interlocutors who do not stand between her and the children, and by adversaries who understand that the relevant intelligence collection on Wanda Maximoff is not signals, not financial, not pattern-of-life in any conventional sense, but **the careful, continuous, longitudinal reading of her grief.**

That is the file's working operational premise. The rest of the dossier proceeds from it.

— *End Section 5. Continue to Section 6: Relationships & Network Mapping.*


## Worldview & Operational Code

# Worldview & Operational Code — Wanda Maximoff

*Section 5 of the UATU dossier. Derived from the longitudinal behavioral record; substantiated from canon; written as an intelligence product, not a character study.*

---

## 5.1 The Foundational Axioms

Every operator carries a small set of pre-rational beliefs — propositions so old they are no longer experienced as beliefs, only as the shape of the world. Wanda's are unusually legible, because each was forged at a discrete catastrophe and each has been re-tested, against her will, in public.

**Axiom 1 — Reality is provisional.** This is the load-bearing premise of her entire cognitive architecture, and it is not a philosophical position; it is an *experiential certainty.* She has lived inside a world she herself rewrote (House of M). She has held children who were and then weren't (Vision and the Scarlet Witch #12). She has been told her species-history, her abilities' origin, even her own parentage were retconned by a hand other than hers (the Wundagore / High Evolutionary revelations; Doom's siphoning revealed in Children's Crusade). For most people reality has the texture of bedrock; for Wanda it has the texture of weather. The operational consequence is decisive: she does not, at depth, believe consensus reality is *sacred.* She believes it is *negotiated,* and the negotiation is *expensive,* and she now knows the bill.

**Axiom 2 — Love is the only durable value.** Institutions take loved ones away. Ideologies (mutant supremacy, government oversight, the X-Men's nation-building, Avengers' policing) are instruments people wield to that end. Individual attachment — to a spouse, a sister, a son, a friend — is the only category of meaning that has survived every revision of her cosmology. She therefore weights private fidelity above public obligation in every contested decision on record. She broke with the Brotherhood for the Avengers; broke with the Avengers (functionally) at Disassembled; broke with Magneto repeatedly; has never broken with Pietro, Vision-as-memory, or the twins.

**Axiom 3 — She is the variable, not the constant.** She has internalized — correctly, by her own evidence — that *she* is the perturbation in any system she joins. The Avengers are stable until she is in them and grieving. Mutantkind is stable until she is the daughter weaponized against it. Her ontology of self is *contagion model*: I am the part of any equation that, sufficiently stressed, makes the equation untrue. This belief drives the door-always-open shop of the Orlando run as much as it drives her chronic readiness to accept blame; she is preemptively distributing antidote because she believes she is the venom.

**Axiom 4 — Power did not arrive as a gift.** It arrived as a draft notice. Every escalation of her capability — mutant probability bolts, then chaos magic, then Life Force, then the Scarlet Witch title's metaphysical weight — has coincided with someone needing her to be larger than she wanted to be. She therefore does not relate to her power the way Strange relates to his (as a discipline) or Doom to his (as a sovereignty). She relates to it the way a draftee relates to a rifle: with competence, with dread, and with a permanent low-grade conviction that the right thing would have been to never pick it up.

---

## 5.2 How She Reads the World

**Other people are first read affectively, then cognitively.** Wanda enters a room and registers the emotional weather before she registers the agenda. This is not empathy as virtue; it is empathy as primary perceptual channel. She knows who in the room is frightened, who is performing, who is carrying a wound. She frequently *cannot* tell you who is lying about facts. She can almost always tell you who is lying about feelings. Operational consequence: she is poor counter-intelligence against a cool sociopath who genuinely doesn't care, and uncannily good against any deceiver whose deception costs them something internally.

**Institutions are read as weather systems with intent.** She does not have the political mind. She does not parse the Avengers as a chartered body with sub-committees and funding streams; she parses it as a *family with a flag.* She does not parse the X-Men's Krakoa as a sovereign experiment in mutant law; she parses it as *the room her father built.* This is a limitation she has not corrected and probably cannot. It means she consistently misreads bureaucratic threats (the Vision's government dismemberment caught her unprepared) and consistently overreads interpersonal ones.

**Conflict is read as grief in disguise.** This is the most distinctive feature of her phenomenology. Where Captain America sees a fight as a moral contest, where Stark sees it as a system to optimize, where Strange sees it as a metaphysical equation, Wanda sees it as *what people do when they have lost something they cannot name.* She is therefore reflexively oriented toward what the antagonist is *bereaved of* — not as a tactic, but as her native frame. It is why her late-period interventions (Orlando run; her engagements on Krakoa) tend toward the restorative rather than the punitive, and why she repeatedly accepts negotiation from figures (Doom, Magneto, even Mephisto-adjacent presences) whom a more strategic operator would refuse on principle.

**Risk is read in two registers.** Risk *to others* she calculates obsessively, with the over-vigilance of someone who has produced the worst-case outcome at planetary scale and remembers it. Risk *to herself* she does not meaningfully compute. The asymmetry is total. She will not perform a working with a 1% chance of collateral; she will perform one with a 90% chance of killing her without hesitation if the alternative is harm to a ward. This is not heroism in her own self-concept — it is the math of someone who has unconsciously priced her own continued existence as a net liability.

---

## 5.3 The Operational Code — How She Acts

**On trust.** Trust is extended *fast* to the wounded and *slow* to the institutional. She will believe a frightened stranger's story before she will believe a Council's. The pattern is consistent from the Brotherhood years (she trusted Magneto's victim-framing of mutants long after she stopped trusting him) through the present (the Orlando run's clientele are unvetted by design — the door is open *because* vetting is the wrong instrument). Counter-intelligence implication: she is asymmetrically penetrable by hostile actors willing to perform vulnerability. She has been exploited this way more than once. She has not corrected for it, because correcting for it would require becoming someone she does not wish to be.

**On control.** She does not seek it and she does not respect it. She has been controlled by Magneto, by Immortus, by Doom, by Chthon — and in each case she emerged with a reinforced conviction that *control over another person is the original sin.* She will therefore decline command roles even when offered (note: she has never sought leadership of any team she has served on; this is structural, not modest). When she does exercise authority — over Wiccan, over the magical clients of her solo run — it is via *availability,* not direction. She makes herself a resource and lets the petitioner choose the use. This is the inverse of how power normally organizes itself, and it is doctrinally consistent.

**On secrets.** She holds them poorly and reluctantly. Her decompensations are precisely the return of repressed material. She has learned, slowly, that *suppression is the mechanism of her catastrophes* — and her current operational posture is therefore biased toward disclosure, sometimes to a fault. She will confess when she does not need to. She will name her crimes in rooms where naming them is tactically unwise (the Trial of Magneto sequence; her conversations with Magneto in the Hellfire Gala era). This is not poor tradecraft; it is doctrine. The Harkness solution — bury the wound, function — nearly ended the species. She will not run that experiment a second time on herself.

**On violence.** Wanda is *not* a pacifist and the file should not mistake her for one. She has killed (Disassembled; numerous combat actions before and since), and she will kill again under sufficient threat to a charge. But she has a marked aversion to violence as a *first* instrument. The deeper pattern: she will use violence against an *individual* she has assessed; she will not use it against an *abstraction* or *class.* This is the moral residue of "no more mutants" — she enacted a class-action erasure once in a state of dissociated grief, and she has organized her post-recovery ethics around never again confusing a category for an enemy.

**On risk-tolerance.** Calibrated low for collateral, calibrated near-zero for self. She does not gamble with other people's outcomes; she gambles freely with her own. This is exploitable in both directions: an actor who threatens her wards can extract almost any concession; an actor who threatens *her* personally will find her unmoved, sometimes inappropriately so.

**On planning.** She does not plan well. Her cognitive style is intuitive-associative, image-and-feeling driven; she is not Strange, not Stark, not Richards. Where she *appears* to plan brilliantly — the Decimation-reversal arcs, the architecture of her solo practice — closer reading shows the work was emotional pattern-recognition expressed *as* plan, not analytic forecasting. Her strategic interface is dream-logic. This is why her interventions look like *parables* in retrospect (the door, the witches' road, the children-as-restoration) rather than like operations.

**On accountability.** Unusually high, by the standards of her tier. She does not flee, does not litigate, does not narrate herself out of her acts. She accepted the consequences of House of M in a way that almost no peer-power figure has accepted comparable acts (compare Stark post-Civil War, Richards post-Illuminati, Cyclops post-Phoenix). This is partly conscience and partly something colder: she does not, at base, believe she is *entitled* to acquittal. The penitent posture is metabolically necessary. Take it away and the self-concept collapses.

---

## 5.4 Her Place in the World — Self-Location

She locates herself, with painful precision, as *a corrective.* Not a hero in the affirmative sense — she does not believe she is owed the title and is visibly uncomfortable when it is offered. Not a villain, though she would accept the word more readily than the previous one. The category she actually inhabits, by her own behavior, is older: *the one who pays.* She is the figure who shows up where the damage is, recognizes some of it as her own, the rest as kindred, and offers herself as the instrument of partial repair, knowing repair will be incomplete.

This is not martyr-cognition in the grandiose register. She does not stage her suffering and does not perform her atonement for an audience. The Orlando-era door is small; the clientele is humble; the work is unglamorous magical first aid. She is doing the work the way someone does AA service — quietly, daily, because the alternative is the version of herself she cannot survive being again.

She believes — and this is the deepest single proposition in her code — that **the world that contains her Billy and her Tommy is the world worth defending.** Everything else is negotiable. The X-Men's project, the Avengers' charter, the magical community's hierarchies, her own life — all are downstream of the prior condition that those two boys continue to exist in a reality stable enough to hold them. This is the load-bearing belief; it is what the operational code is *for.*

It is also, by the file's honest read, the failure mode. Should that condition be violated, the operational code described above ceases to obtain, and the subject reverts to the House of M baseline at minimum and likely beyond it. The handler should not regard the reparative phase as a personality change; it is a *equilibrium,* held in place by the survival of two specific human beings.

---

## 5.5 Philosophical Residues

A short index of the propositions she would, if asked, affirm — derived from the consistency of her conduct across six decades of record:

- **On fate:** She does not believe in it. Her early Romani-coded fatalism (the Lee/Kirby Brotherhood years) eroded across the Englehart and Byrne runs and is fully absent post-Disassembled. She believes outcomes are made, by hands including her own, and she believes this with the bleakness of someone who has made the wrong ones.
- **On forgiveness:** She believes it is owed to others and impossible for herself. The asymmetry is total and structural.
- **On family:** Constructed family is as real as biological. Wanda's lineage has been retconned so many times that biology has lost evidentiary status for her; what remains is the people who stayed. Pietro stayed. Vision (in memory and in his returns) stayed. Billy and Tommy found her. That is family. The X-gene is interesting; it is not kin.
- **On magic:** It is not separate from grief, love, or wish. It is the same substance, made operative. She does not distinguish, the way her teachers do, between disciplined working and emotional state — she knows from her own catastrophes that the distinction is a comforting fiction. Magic is what the unconscious does when it has a hand.
- **On institutions:** Necessary; untrustworthy; survivable; never to be confused with the people they are alleged to serve.
- **On her own death:** She does not fear it. She has experienced it (Trial of Magneto) and returned with a hyperactive reparative drive rather than a sense of reprieve. The handler should note: she is not suicidal in any clinical sense, but she is *not protected* by the ordinary self-preservation instinct that operates in most assets at her tier.
- **On the question whether House of M was wrong:** Yes. She has answered this in conduct, not rhetoric, every day since. The certainty is total. It is also the engine of everything she now does — and therefore not a wound to be healed, in her own implicit theory, but a debt to be serviced for the duration.

---

*— End Section 5. Section 6 (Interpersonal Pattern & Relational Map) to follow.*


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# Moral & Ethical Framework — Wanda Maximoff

*The code as enacted across six decades of published behavior, not as she would describe it under oath.*

---

## 1. The Operative Code (Derived, Not Professed)

Wanda has never sat down and written a manifesto. She is not Captain America with a creed, not Doom with a doctrine, not Magneto with an ideology. Her ethics are **affective and casuistic** — decided in the moment, by feel, against the face in front of her. To recover the actual code one has to read the *pattern of acts*: what she has consistently refused, what she has consistently done, what she has done and then atoned for, and what she has done and never apologized for. From that pattern, the following operative rules emerge.

**Rule One — Persons over categories.** The single most consistent thread across sixty years is that Wanda treats the individual standing in front of her as morally prior to any group they belong to. She fought *for* the Brotherhood but recoiled at any specific cruelty asked of her; she abandoned Magneto not on doctrinal grounds but because particular acts violated her sense of the particular victims; she opens a literal storefront door (the Orlando-era practice) to *anyone* who comes asking, without screening for affiliation. She has helped enemies' relatives, sheltered strangers, treated synthezoids as full persons before the culture caught up. This rule is **load-bearing**: nearly every other consistency in her behavior derives from it.

**Rule Two — Loyalty is sacred and asymmetric.** She gives more than she demands. Loyalty, once extended, is not contingent on reciprocation. She remained loyal to Pietro through paranoia, manipulation, the Inhumans rupture, and the House of M conspiracy he engineered. She remained loyal to Vision through dismantlement, the cold reconstruction, and his serial repudiations of her. She remained loyal to the Avengers through expulsions and accusations. The corollary — that her loyalty is exploitable — is the single most reliable lever any handler has ever pulled on her.

**Rule Three — Power is shameful unless it serves.** She does not enjoy her capability. She does not display it for its own sake, never poses, never threatens, rarely escalates first. The chaos magic is treated, behaviorally, the way a recovering addict treats a substance: kept at distance, deployed reluctantly, regretted afterward even in success. Compare to Strange (curatorial pride) or Doom (instrumental pride) or even Pietro (kinetic joy). Wanda's relationship with her own power is **prophylactic**, not celebratory.

**Rule Four — Mourn aloud, never alone, but mourn small.** Her permitted grief is intimate-scale: a candle, a quiet word, a hand on a shoulder. She does *not* grant herself the right to grieve at the scale her losses actually warrant. This is the central fracture in the code (see §4): the rule prohibits the only grief proportionate to her wounds, and so the grief, when it comes, comes as catastrophe.

**Rule Five — Accept the consequence.** She does not flee accountability. After Disassembled she does not run; she becomes findable. After House of M she does not hide behind Doom's culpability when it is offered as exculpation. After resurrection she does not request a clean slate. The acceptance is sometimes self-punitive past the point of usefulness, but it is constant.

**Rule Six — No bystanders, if she can help it.** Civilians are non-negotiable. Across every era, including the decompensations, her use of force avoids non-combatants when reality-testing is intact; when reality-testing fails (Disassembled, M), the violence still skews toward people inside her frame of reference rather than random crowds. She has never, in any era, knowingly targeted a child.

**Rule Seven — Truth-telling to intimates; deception to power.** She lies easily to institutions — SHIELD, governments, the Illuminati, even to teammates when she judges they are acting as institutional rather than as individuals. She does not lie to lovers, children, or close friends in any sustained way. The asymmetry is moral, not strategic.

---

## 2. What She Will Do

- **Defy a legitimate authority on behalf of one person.** She will break a chain of command, walk out of a sanctioned operation, contradict a teammate publicly, if a specific person in front of her is being mishandled. Documented across the Avengers, West Coast, Krakoa, and solo eras.
- **Take a wound meant for someone else.** She steps in front. Repeatedly. Her body and her sanity have both been used as shields.
- **Open a door to a stranger who is suffering.** The Orlando-era practice formalized what had always been informal: petitioners receive an audience.
- **Bargain with reality itself for a loved one.** This is the *signature* moral act — and the most dangerous. She will warp probability, alter causality, breach metaphysical boundaries in the service of someone she loves. She does it small daily (a hex to keep a friend from a falling cornice) and she has done it cosmically (M).
- **Hold an unwelcome truth privately for the sake of another's stability.** She is capable of carrying knowledge alone — about Pietro, about Vision, about her father — when sharing it would harm.
- **Negotiate with monsters.** She will sit across from Doom, from Mephisto, from her father in his worst configurations, if the negotiation might recover something lost or prevent something coming. She does not refuse the table on grounds of purity.
- **Restore what she has destroyed, at any personal cost.** The post-Decimation reparative campaign is multi-decade and ongoing; she has died inside the work and resumed it on resurrection.
- **Forgive.** Wonder Man, Pietro, Magneto in his better postures, the Avengers who exiled her. The forgiveness is real, not strategic. It is also a vulnerability.

---

## 3. What She Will Not Do

- **Harm a child.** Categorical. There is no episode in the record where she knowingly endangers a child, and her decompensations skew, almost defensively, *away* from minors in the blast radius.
- **Sell out an individual to spare herself.** No record of her trading another person's location, identity, or vulnerability to escape consequence. She has accepted custody, exile, and death rather than offer up a name.
- **Use her magic for personal enrichment, status, or pleasure.** No record of any working performed for vanity, wealth, comfort, or sexual advantage. The output is always *for* someone, even when it goes wrong.
- **Mock a supplicant.** She will refuse, she will warn, she will deliver hard verdicts — but she does not humiliate the person who came to her in need. This is one of the cleanest threads in her conduct.
- **Disavow the children.** Wiccan and Speed, even before they were confirmed as the recovered souls of Thomas and William, were treated by her as morally inviolable. She would dismantle the Avengers institutionally before she would let either be harmed.
- **Take a deal that requires the erasure of another's consent.** Note the irony: she has *violated* this rule at decompensation scale (M is a non-consensual remaking of the world), but in deliberate conduct she refuses it. She will not, e.g., magically resolve a partner's ambivalence, will not unmake an enemy's free choice in negotiation. The contrast between her decompensated behavior and her considered behavior on this exact point is one of the most important data in the file.
- **Stand silently while a vulnerable person is humiliated by someone with power over them.** The intervention may be quiet — a redirected question, a hex turning a mocker's word into nonsense — but it happens.
- **Pledge to anything that asks her to renounce love as a category.** She has refused initiations, covens, schools, and political projects that required emotional disinvestment as their price.

---

## 4. Where the Code Fractures

The fractures are not many but they are catastrophic, and they cluster around a single fault line.

**Fracture One — Grief at scale.** Rule Four (mourn small) cannot contain the actual magnitude of her losses. When the dam fails, the entire code fails *with* it, because every other rule presupposes a Wanda whose reality-testing is intact. Disassembled and House of M are not violations of her ethics by a different person; they are her ethics *suspended* by a grief her code never gave her permission to feel. The fracture is not in the values; it is in the **regulatory architecture** that the values depend on.

**Fracture Two — The asymmetry of consent.** She holds individual consent as nearly sacred when conscious. When decompensated, she has overridden the consent of the entire mutant species, of the inhabitants of an entire constructed reality, of intimates whose memories she has rearranged. The fracture: she has never resolved, in any considered statement, *how* the categorical respect for consent in her code coexists with the categorical breach in her record. She accepts the consequence (Rule Five) without ever theorizing the breach. She does not have a doctrine of when reality-warping is permitted; she has only a doctrine of restitution after the fact.

**Fracture Three — Loyalty exploited.** Rule Two (asymmetric loyalty) is repeatedly weaponized against the other rules. Pietro's House of M nudge succeeded precisely because her loyalty to him was not contingent on his honesty. Magneto, in every era, has been able to draw her closer than her better judgment endorses. The code does not contain a self-protective sub-clause and she has not added one in sixty years.

**Fracture Four — Reparation as identity.** Rule Five (accept consequence) has, post-2005, metastasized into something closer to compulsion. The reparative drive is no longer a discrete response to wrongdoing; it is the *medium in which she lives*. This is a fracture because it inverts the original ethic: instead of accepting consequence as the price of agency, she has begun to *seek* the role of debtor, which subtly nullifies the responsibility she claims to honor — a permanent penitent is a person who can no longer be held to account in normal terms.

**Fracture Five — The categorical refusal that wasn't.** "No more mutants" violated Rule One (persons over categories) more profoundly than any single act in superhero history. It is the precise inverse of her professed ethic: she punished a *category* for what individuals (Magneto, Pietro, the Illuminati) had done. The fact that this act sits in the record alongside a lifetime of category-skeptical behavior is the central interpretive problem of her moral biography. The reading the evidence supports: the act was not a chosen ethical position but a *grief-driven misfire* in which the symbol "mutants" stood in, in her wish-cognition, for "the apparatus that took my children and my husband and my mind." The act expressed her grief, not her ethics. But she committed it, and her code has not produced a satisfactory account of how.

---

## 5. Shifts Over Time

**Phase I — Inherited Ethics (Brotherhood era).** The early code is *borrowed*. She acts within Magneto's frame because she has no other frame; her dissent is somatic and reluctant rather than articulated. Already visible: the refusal to enjoy cruelty, the bias toward the individual victim, the discomfort with her own power.

**Phase II — Institutional Ethics (early Avengers).** She adopts the Avengers' code as a scaffolding. This is the period in which she behaves most like a "standard hero" — sanctioned, deferential to team consensus, identified with the badge. The code in this phase is most coherent and least her own.

**Phase III — Domestic Ethics (Vision marriage, the children).** A new center of gravity. Loyalty narrows and deepens; the ethical universe contracts to husband, children, near family. Heroism becomes background. This is the only era in which her ethics rest on a foundation that is *hers* — chosen partner, made children, constructed home.

**Phase IV — Suppressed Ethics (post-Harkness intervention, late 80s through early 2000s).** The code persists but it is **untethered from the wound that should be informing it**. She behaves morally but mechanically; the affective core has been excised. This is the period of greatest exploitability — without access to the grief, she has no warning system for her own decompensation.

**Phase V — Catastrophic Ethics (Disassembled / House of M).** The code does not so much shift as *fail*. Wish-cognition replaces deliberation. What looks like a new ethics is in fact the absence of ethics — a wound speaking through the architecture.

**Phase VI — Reparative Ethics (post-M to present).** The most considered ethical period of her life. She now operates with explicit knowledge of what she is capable of, what she has done, and what her code failed to prevent. The Orlando-era door-always-open practice is a *deliberate ethical institution* — the first one she has ever built for herself. The Krakoa reckoning, the work to restore mutants, the careful management of her relationship with Wiccan and Speed: all reflect an ethics that has finally integrated the catastrophe rather than denying or atoning blindly for it. **This is the most morally serious version of Wanda the record contains** — and also the most fragile, because it is held in place by conditions (the twins alive, no fresh catastrophic loss) that are not under her control.

---

## 6. Justifications — How She Explains Herself to Herself

Wanda's internal justifications, recovered from her dialogue and conduct, run in a narrow channel:

- *"They needed me."* The most frequent. Used to justify intervention, overextension, breaking ranks, staying too long with bad attachments.
- *"I couldn't let them be alone in it."* The grief-companion justification — used to explain why she sat with enemies, why she stayed with Vision through the cold reconstruction, why she opens the door.
- *"It was mine to fix."* The reparative formula. Used to explain why she does not delegate consequences of her own actions, sometimes to a fault.
- *"I didn't mean — "* The decompensation formula. Notable for being **unfinished** in nearly every utterance; she does not complete the sentence because she does not believe intention exculpates her, and the literature of grief-driven harm she has not read confirms her instinct.
- *"I am not him."* The negative self-definition, against Magneto. The most fragile of her justifications, because it defines her by what she refuses rather than what she affirms, and refusal is not a foundation.

What is **conspicuously absent** from her self-justification: appeals to destiny, to mutant supremacy, to magical prerogative, to the privilege of power, to the unique pain that entitles unique action. She has every grandiose justification available to a person of her capability and uses *none* of them. This absence is itself a moral datum.

---

## 7. Net Read

Wanda's ethics, taken as a whole, describe a woman whose code is **personalist, anti-institutional, loyalty-driven, anti-grandiose, restitutionary, and consent-respecting** — with a single, devastating fault line where unmetabolized grief breaches every other rule. The code is genuinely her own in the reparative phase, genuinely borrowed in the early phases, and genuinely *absent* in the decompensated episodes. She does not have a philosophy; she has a practice, and the practice is more coherent than she gives herself credit for.

The handler-relevant fact: she is the rare subject whose stated values and enacted values *match*, with the catastrophic exception that she cannot be trusted to remain herself across a sufficiently large fresh loss. Her ethics are real. Her ethics are also conditional on a regulatory capacity that has failed before and could fail again. Any assessment that treats her code as either purely admirable or purely suspect has not read the file.

— End section.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE — WANDA MAXIMOFF

*Compiled from sixty years of published verbal record (Lee/Kirby 1964 → Orlando 2023+). Granular pattern-mapping; longitudinal; tells flagged in bold for handler reference.*

---

## 1. Substrate: The Sokovian Layer

The subject is not a native English speaker. Her L1 is the Romani-inflected Eastern European register of her childhood (rendered variously as Transian, Sokovian, or generic Balkan across editorial eras). This substrate produces a residue audible across her entire career, even at peak fluency:

- **Article elision and slightly inverted syntax under stress.** "*Is not what I meant*" / "*You will tell me the truth now*" / "*The boy, he is mine.*" The pattern thins to near-invisibility in social/Avengers settings and re-emerges sharply under affect — particularly grief, anger, or supplication. **This is a reliable tell:** when Wanda's syntax drifts toward the substrate, her conscious control is degrading.
- **Formal/archaic register where colloquial would be expected.** "*I do not wish it*" rather than "I don't want to"; "*You are kind to say so*" rather than "thanks." Reads to American interlocutors as either old-world courtesy or witchy gravitas; in fact is the cautious overcorrection of a non-native who was taught the language in books and by Pietro.
- **Romani lexical retention** — *brother, sister, mother* are sometimes given in the substrate tongue in moments of private address to Pietro, in incantation, and in prayer. The endearments she uses for the twins (*my Billy, my Tommy, little ones, sweet boy*) are English but cadenced with the lullaby-rhythm of the Romani diminutive.
- **Inherited oaths.** Her ejaculative exclamations skew to *"By the All-Mother" / "Goddess" / "By the Wundagore"* — never American profanity, almost never even mild Anglo-Saxon expletive. She has been on panel for six decades and has substantively never sworn in English. **Marked absence.**

## 2. Register Map by Context

**With the Avengers (institutional baseline).** Cooperative, deferential, slightly under-asserted. Sentences are short, declarative, mission-relevant. She volunteers tactical observation but rarely opinion. Says *"Yes, Captain"* / *"I will try"* — note the *try* construction, almost compulsive; she rarely promises outcome, only effort. Avoids the first-person possessive in team contexts ("the team," "we," "the Avengers") long past the point where she has earned the *I*.

**With Pietro.** Intimate, fast, overlapping. Code-switches into the substrate language for endearment and for fights. Pattern of *placating diminution* — she shrinks her own concerns to soothe his anxiety, often closing arguments with "*it is nothing, brother, let it be.*" Across decades she is the *de-escalator;* he is the *pressuriser.* When she finally pushes back (Children's Crusade, Trial of Magneto) the syntax is foreign-formal: "*You do not get to decide this for me.*"

**With Vision.** Slow, gentle, explicitly tender, with a teacher's patience for his literalism. Uses metaphor and then unpacks it. *"It was a figure of speech, my love"* recurs across the Englehart/Byrne run. Her affect-vocabulary is most developed here — she taught herself to name feelings *for him,* which means she learned to name them at all in the second person before the first. This has consequences (see §6).

**With Magneto.** Two registers, sequentially. *Daughter-register* (post-revelation): tight, controlled, monosyllabic when possible, formal address ("*Father*" only sparingly and usually loaded; more often the name). *Subject-register* (pre-revelation, Brotherhood era): near-silent compliance, eyes-down, "*Yes*" and "*As you say.*" The shift between the two is itself a tell: when she returns to subject-register around him she is dissociating into the child.

**With the twins (Wiccan, Speed).** Maternal, halting, apologetic, *over-careful.* Long pauses before address; rehearsal-quality phrasing. She speaks to them as if every sentence might be the last she is permitted. Frequent self-interruption: "*I — I am sorry, I did not mean to —*". Touch-words ("*my sweet boy,* *my heart*") deployed at higher density than with anyone else in her life.

**With the public / civilian clients (Orlando run, the open-door shop).** Warm, professional, plainspoken, slightly maternal. Drops the witch-formal register almost entirely; speaks the way a small-town doctor speaks. *"Tell me what happened. From the beginning. Take your time."* The very ordinariness of this register is performed; she has worked to sound un-frightening.

**In combat.** Verbally sparse to silent. Issues short directives ("*get down,*" "*move,*" "*no*") and emits incantation, but rarely banters and never gloats. Among the highest-output combatants on Earth she is also the *least talkative* combatant. The gap between her destructive capacity and her in-combat verbiage is itself diagnostic: she does not want to be experienced as the agent of what she is doing.

**In incantation.** Cadenced, often invented-Latinate or fragments of Romani, sometimes pure syllabic chant. Pre-Bendis era: rhyming couplets, fairy-tale meter ("*hexes, like a child's spell, do their work*"). Post-Bendis: less ornamented, more ad hoc, sometimes only a verb ("*undo,*" "*let it be,*" "*no more*"). **Critical pattern:** her most consequential utterances in the record are *three words or fewer.* "*No more mutants.*" "*No.*" "*Bring them back.*" The shorter the spell, the larger the wound driving it.

## 3. Diction & Lexicon

- **Preferred verbs:** *wish, want, try, mean, undo, let, bring, give, take.* Note the wish-cluster (*wish/want/mean*) — her cognitive primaries are intentional and affective rather than analytical. She does not say *plan, calculate, intend;* she says *want* and *mean.*
- **Avoided verbs:** *promise* (uses *try*); *deserve* (uses *should* with negative polarity — "*I should not*"); *forgive* (asks for it, almost never extends it explicitly, though she enacts it).
- **High-frequency nouns:** *family, mother, brother, children, home, world, reality, magic.* The semantic field is *kin and the container that holds kin.*
- **Low-frequency nouns:** *power, control, victory, enemy.* She talks around her own capability rather than naming it; the word *power* is almost always in someone else's mouth about her.
- **Self-reference vocabulary.** *Witch, mother, sister, daughter, woman.* Almost never *hero, Avenger* in self-description, even at peak Avengers tenure. The institutional identity never took root in her own mouth.
- **Negation.** Disproportionately high rate of negated constructions — "*I did not want,*" "*it was not meant,*" "*no more.*" Her grammar is shaped by what she is trying to undo.

## 4. Rhetoric & Argument Style

She does not argue analytically. She argues by **appeal to feeling and to the listener's better self.** Structurally her persuasive utterances run: (1) acknowledgement of the other's pain, (2) statement of her own grief or guilt, (3) a *please* or *let us.* Rarely a logical refutation; almost never sarcasm; **never** a rhetorical question used to humiliate. When she wins an argument she wins by becoming undeniable, not by being right.

In moral confrontation — Magneto, Doom, the X-Council post-M — her rhetoric shifts to **flat declarative absolutes.** "*I will not.*" "*That is not true.*" "*You will not touch them.*" The argument is closed by refusal rather than rebuttal. **Tell:** when she stops explaining and begins declaring, the conversational window has closed and the magical window is opening.

## 5. Deflection & Evasion Language

Wanda is not a skilled liar. Her deflection register is narrow and identifiable:

- **The pivot-to-service.** Asked how she is, she answers about what needs doing. "*I am — there is much to do today.*" Across decades.
- **The geographical pivot.** Asked about feeling, she answers about place. "*I have been in Calabria. The air is good there.*" The Orlando run is full of this.
- **The third-person retreat.** Discussing herself in difficult moments she slides into *"a woman who…" / "someone like me…"* — the substrate-language preference for impersonal construction is a ready-made dissociative tool.
- **The Pietro-deflection.** When pressed personally she changes subject to her brother. He is her conversational decoy.
- **The historical apology.** Asked about anything difficult in the present she offers an apology about the past. "*I know what I did. I am sorry for it.*" This functions to redirect interlocutors into reassuring her, and ends the inquiry. **Tell:** unprompted reference to House of M / the Decimation in conversation is almost always a deflection from a more recent and live wound.
- **The notable absence: she does not gaslight.** She will withhold, redirect, apologize-deflect, and dissociate — she will not insist that another's perception is wrong. Even at her most magically world-altering she preserves a strange interpersonal honesty.

## 6. How She Communicates Love

Slowly, indirectly, somatically, and through *making things*. Verbal "I love you" is rare and weighty; she rations it. More common: the small culinary or domestic act (she cooks for guests; the Orlando solo run has her brewing tea as introduction-ritual); the offered hand; the careful study of the beloved's face before speaking. With Vision she developed a private vocabulary of metaphor-and-gloss. With the twins she has reverted, post-loss, to *naming them* repeatedly — saying *Billy. Tommy.* as if to fix them in the world. The verbal love-tic with the twins is the **diminutive-plus-possessive:** *my Billy, my sweet boy, my Tommy.* When she addresses them without the possessive, she is performing restraint — usually because she fears she will scare them by claiming too much.

## 7. How She Communicates Threat

Almost never explicitly. The threat register is **the collapse of register itself** — she gets quieter, the substrate syntax tightens, the eye contact lengthens, the hands begin to move at the periphery. When language does emerge it is brief, absolute, and uninflected: "*You will not.*" / *"Stop."* / *"Enough."* Whole confrontations may pass with fewer than ten words from her. **The handler-relevant pattern:** Wanda escalating into violence does *not* sound like Wanda escalating. The vocal volume does not rise; the sentence length drops; the substrate emerges; and then the air changes. By the time she has spoken three words in this register, intervention is already late.

A subordinate verbal threat-tell: **the unfinished conditional.** "*If you do this thing —*" trailing into silence. The completed sentence is the magical act.

## 8. How She Communicates Grief

This is the most studied register in her record because the entire post-1989 arc is its inflection. Grief surfaces verbally as:

- **Present-tense reference to the dead or undone.** "*They are mine. They are my sons.*" Not *were.* The tense itself is the symptom — she has not relocated the lost objects into the past.
- **Sentence fragments and trailing-off.** "*I just — I —*" Aborted self-reference is her grief-signature. The fluent woman becomes inarticulate around the wound.
- **The recursive apology.** *"I'm sorry. I'm sorry. I'm sorry."* Repetition without escalation — flat, near-liturgical. Bendis writes this; Robinson writes this; Orlando writes this. **Reliable indicator of acute grief-state rather than ordinary remorse.**
- **The denial-formula.** *"No. No. No no no."* The triple-or-greater negation is the *House of M* utterance in miniature. When it appears in conversation, the speaker is at the lip of reality-rejection. Three *no*s is the verbal precursor of a hex.
- **Disbelief language as cognition.** Per the grief literature (Pop-Jordanova 2021), disbelief/denial is a core complicated-grief feature; in Wanda's record it surfaces as the literal sentence *"This is not real"* or *"It cannot be"* — uttered to the world rather than to a listener. **Critical tell:** when she begins addressing reality itself in the second person ("*you cannot do this to me*"), the reality-warping faculty is engaging.

## 9. Voice Quality & Paralinguistics (inferred from canon stage direction)

- Low-pitched, deliberate cadence; tendency to soften further in distress (most grief-stricken people raise; she drops). The voice goes *down and quiet* before the largest events.
- Long pauses are her native punctuation. She listens at length before answering; the silence is not strategic but cognitive — she is composing in a second language and across a partially dissociated interior.
- **Laugh:** rare, late, and small. Almost always at a child or at Pietro's expense.
- **Cry:** late and quiet. She weeps mid-sentence without acknowledging it; does not break to compose herself; this is one of the more identifiable canonical images of her.

## 10. Written / Mediated Communication

She is not a texter, not an emailer, not a poster. Her written voice (letters in the Robinson and Orlando runs, journal entries in *Children's Crusade*) is **elevated, slightly archaic, carefully punctuated** — the prose of someone who learned to write English from older books. Signs letters with full name; does not use her code name in correspondence. Handwriting is described as small, even, slightly back-slanted. Her communications discipline is high in a single direction (she does not over-share) and low in another (she is bad at strategic silence — when asked directly she tends to answer truthfully even at cost).

## 11. The Diagnostic Tells, Consolidated

For handler reference, the following verbal markers — in approximate order of escalation — indicate departure from baseline:

1. **Substrate syntax surfacing** in English speech → arousal climbing past baseline regulation.
2. **Shift to formal/declarative absolutes** ("I will not") → argument-window has closed.
3. **Third-person self-reference** ("a woman like me") → dissociative thinning beginning.
4. **Recursive apology** ("I'm sorry, I'm sorry, I'm sorry") → acute grief activation.
5. **Present-tense reference to the lost** ("they *are* my sons") → grief unmetabolized and live.
6. **Triple negation** ("no, no, no") → denial-state, reality-rejection imminent.
7. **Second-person address to reality itself** ("this cannot be") → reality-warping engaging.
8. **Volume drop, sentence-length collapse, substrate tightening, hands at periphery** → intervention already late.
9. **The unfinished conditional** ("If you —") → the sentence is being completed in magic.
10. **Three words or fewer, uttered quietly** → the load-bearing utterances of her life have all fit this profile. "*No more mutants.*" Treat any such utterance from her, in any context of grief or threat, as a potential reality-class event.

— End linguistic profile.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Behavioral forecasting for the unobserved hours. Each prediction is a conditional inference from the longitudinal record, calibrated to the subject's documented attachment template, defense architecture, and reparative-phase operating state. Format: GIVEN → EXPECT, with substantiation. Confidence flagged where warranted.*

---

## 1. Domestic Routine — The Unwatched Hours
